The CLI's per-Lambda materialization pass then routes ARN entries through the new helper `materializeLayerFromArn` in [src/local/layer-arn-materializer.ts](src/local/layer-arn-materializer.ts) BEFORE the existing `cpSync`-merge into `/opt`: optional `sts:AssumeRole` (via the new `--layer-role-arn` flag — independent of `--assume-role`, scoped only to the layer-fetch step) → `lambda:GetLayerVersion` against the **layer ARN's region** (NOT the dev profile region — load-bearing because the SDK client must point at the bucket region the presigned URL was signed for; tested explicitly) → `fetch()` the `Content.Location` presigned S3 URL (no AWS credentials needed on the GET — the presign carries them) → unzip into a per-ARN tmpdir using a self-contained ZIP decoder (Node's `zlib.inflateRaw` + the documented PKZIP layout). The decoder rejects entries that escape the destination directory (Zip Slip CVE class) AND rejects symlink entries (Unix mode `S_IFLNK`) so a malicious layer can never redirect to arbitrary host paths. **Tmpdir cleanup on unzip failure** (review-fix): the unzip step is wrapped in a try/catch that `rmSync`s the just-created tmpdir before re-throwing, so a malformed-ZIP / Zip-Slip / symlink rejection never leaks the directory. Per-ARN tmpdirs are tracked alongside the existing multi-layer merge tmpdir on both code paths (`ImagePlan.layerArnTmpDirs[]` in [src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts](src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts); `layerTmpDirs: Set<string>` in [src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts](src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts)) so the existing SIGINT / outer-finally cleanup walks every directory regardless of layer kind — long-running `start-api` invocations never leak. **Last-wins file-collision semantic is preserved** end-to-end because every ARN entry materializes to its own dir BEFORE the same `cpSync({recursive:true, force:true})` merge runs in template order. **Failure modes surface actionable hints**: `GetLayerVersion` `AccessDeniedException` (or any "not authorized" wire-error) wraps as `LayerMaterializationError` with the message "GetLayerVersion access denied; check the credentials / role can read the layer (grant lambda:GetLayerVersion on the layer ARN, or pass `--layer-role-arn` to assume a role in the layer account)"; STS AssumeRole failures surface a separate hint pointing at the role trust policy. **Container Lambdas (`Code.ImageUri`)** still ignore `Layers` (matches AWS's at-deploy-time rejection of layers on container images). **Out of scope (still rejected with a clear error)**: literal strings that aren't valid layer-version ARNs (e.g. an S3 ARN typo), `Fn::GetAtt 'foo.bar'` YAML-only string form (CFn JSON never emits it). Two real-AWS integ tests deferred per the issue's "Test strategy" — the public AWS Powertools layer requires AWS credentials and threading those through the integ runner is a separate concern. New unit tests: 9 in [tests/unit/local/layer-arn-materializer.test.ts](tests/unit/local/layer-arn-materializer.test.ts) (hand-rolled DEFLATE ZIP fixture exercises the full pipeline: region-correct client construction / STS hop credential forwarding / AccessDenied actionable error / STS failure-mode hint / Zip Slip rejection / HTTP-failure error / missing Content.Location guard / unzip-and-merge correctness / tmpdir-rmSync-on-unzip-failure); 12 in [tests/unit/local/lambda-resolver.test.ts](tests/unit/local/lambda-resolver.test.ts) covering `parseLayerVersionArn` (canonical / hyphenated name / GovCloud `us-gov-west-1` / China `cn-north-1` / non-Lambda ARN reject / function ARN reject / unversioned reject / 13-digit account-id reject / non-numeric version reject) + 1 updated test asserting literal-ARN entries now resolve successfully + 1 new test asserting malformed strings still reject with a clear "Expected a same-stack Ref... OR a literal layer-version ARN" message + 3 new tests covering multiple-ARN order preservation / mixed `[asset, arn]` order preservation in both directions; 2 new caller-integration tests in [tests/unit/cli/local-invoke-layers.test.ts](tests/unit/cli/local-invoke-layers.test.ts) verifying `ImagePlan.layerArnTmpDirs` is populated for `cdkd local invoke` and `layerTmpDirs` is populated for `cdkd local start-api` (so the SIGINT / outer-finally / graceful-shutdown cleanup loop actually finds the dirs).

- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke --from-state` and `cdkd local run-task --from-state` resolve `Fn::ImportValue` / `Fn::GetStackOutput` env vars + ECS `Secrets[].ValueFrom` against cdkd state (closes [#454](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/454)). Pre-PR the env-var substituter only handled `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` / `Fn::Sub` / `Fn::Join` against the consumer stack's state; a Lambda env var like `OTHER_STACK_BUCKET: {Fn::ImportValue: 'ProducerStack-BucketName'}` reached the substituter, fell through to the "unsupported intrinsic" branch, and was warn-and-dropped — multi-stack CDK apps couldn't run locally with substituted values. Post-fix the substituter has an async sibling `substituteAgainstStateAsync` (and `substituteEnvVarsFromStateAsync`) that consults a new `CrossStackResolver` on the `SubstitutionContext` for both intrinsics; the legacy sync helpers stay unchanged (they continue to surface the new intrinsics as `unresolved` so callers that don't supply the resolver get the existing warn-and-drop UX without source-incompatible churn). The shared resolver factory `buildCrossStackResolver(consumerRegion, opts)` in [src/cli/commands/local-state-loader.ts](src/cli/commands/local-state-loader.ts) (mirrors `loadStateForStack`'s region-resolution chain) wires a fresh `S3StateBackend` + the persistent `ExportIndexStore` (`s3://{bucket}/cdkd/_index/{region}/exports.json`, already populated by `cdkd deploy` since PR #348). `resolveImport` consults the index first (O(1)) and falls back to a per-stack `state.json` scan on miss; `resolveGetStackOutput` reads the producer stack's state directly. Per-key best-effort: missing index entries, deleted producer stacks, S3 access denied → drop with a `--from-state: could not substitute env var X` warning, never abort the invoke. **Pseudo-parameter integration**: an inner intrinsic in the import-value argument (e.g. `{Fn::ImportValue: {Fn::Sub: 'MyStack-${AWS::Region}-Bucket'}}`) resolves against the existing `pseudoParameters` bag first, then the resulting string is looked up. **Cross-stack v1 scope**: same-account + same-region only (the resolver fast-path consults the consumer's region index; per-stack fallback also filters to the consumer region). Cross-region `Fn::ImportValue` is rejected (CFn structural — `Fn::ImportValue` itself is same-region by AWS contract); cross-account `Fn::GetStackOutput.RoleArn` is deferred (#449) — surface a clear "tracked under issue X" error rather than silently downgrading. **CLI wiring**: `local-invoke.ts` gains a `envHasCrossStackIntrinsic(templateEnv)` predicate that gates the resolver construction so literal + same-stack-intrinsic env maps don't pay the extra S3-client / index-load cost; same gating in `local-run-task.ts` via a new `EcsImageResolutionNeeds.needsCrossStackResolver` field surfaced by `detectEcsImageResolutionNeeds`. ECS run-task additionally needs an **async post-pass** because `parseContainerDefinition` is synchronous: the new exported helper `applyCrossStackResolverToTask(task, context)` in [src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts](src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts) walks each container's raw template (preserved on `task.resource`), re-resolves Environment / Secret entries with the async helper, patches the resolved values into `container.environment` / `container.secrets` in place, and filters the matching `"... dropped: ..."` warnings off the container's `warnings` array. Implementation: [src/local/state-resolver.ts](src/local/state-resolver.ts) (new `CrossStackResolver` interface + `consumerRegion` field + async helpers), [src/cli/commands/local-state-loader.ts](src/cli/commands/local-state-loader.ts) (new `buildCrossStackResolver` factory), [src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts](src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts) (cross-stack gating + async substitution call site), [src/cli/commands/local-run-task.ts](src/cli/commands/local-run-task.ts) (post-pass after `resolveEcsTaskTarget`), [src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts](src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts) (`needsCrossStackResolver` flag + `applyCrossStackResolverToTask` post-pass). 21 new unit tests in [tests/unit/local/state-resolver.test.ts](tests/unit/local/state-resolver.test.ts) covering the legacy-intrinsic delegation path, resolver-hit / resolver-miss / resolver-throws on both intrinsics, inner-`Fn::Sub`-argument resolution for `Fn::ImportValue`, `Fn::GetStackOutput.Region` fall-back to `consumerRegion` / `pseudoParameters.region`, cross-account `RoleArn` rejection, missing-resolver pass-through, env-var-level resolved-or-dropped audit, and the warn-and-drop UX preservation when the resolver is absent.

- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local start-api` REST v1 IAM authorizer support (`AuthorizationType: 'AWS_IAM'`, closes [#447](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/447)). Pre-fix, REST v1 routes declaring `AuthorizationType: 'AWS_IAM'` hard-errored at discovery (`src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts` ~line 658) — CDK apps gated by SigV4-signed IAM credentials could not run locally. Post-fix, those routes boot cleanly and the local server verifies the incoming `Authorization: AWS4-HMAC-SHA256 ...` SigV4 header against the developer's local AWS credentials (resolved via `STSClient`'s default credential chain — same chain every other cdkd command uses; no new dependency). New shared module [src/local/sigv4-verify.ts](src/local/sigv4-verify.ts) (`verifySigV4` + `parseAuthorizationHeader` + `canonicalizePath` + `canonicalizeQueryString` + `validateAmzDateMatchesCredentialDate` + `amzDateOutsideSkew` + `defaultCredentialsLoader`) implements the SigV4 spec end-to-end: parse the header into `(Credential, SignedHeaders, Signature)`, reconstruct the canonical request (canonical URI / sorted query string / header normalization / SHA-256 payload hash supporting the `UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD` marker), derive the signing key (HMAC chain `kDate → kRegion → kService → kSigning`), recompute the signature, and constant-time compare. **Security default — fail-closed**: outcomes are **valid signature with the dev's credentials** → request reaches the handler with `principalId = <accessKeyId>` (no IAM context — see scope note below); **no/malformed Authorization** → 401 `missing-identity`; **signature mismatch with dev's own creds** → 403 `policy-deny`; **expired timestamp (15-min skew)** / **credential-scope-date mismatch** / **unsupported algorithm** → 403 `policy-deny`; **different `Credential` access-key-id than the dev has** → **403 DENY by default**; **dev's credential chain unresolvable** → **403 DENY by default** (no admit-by-default). The pre-review version warn-and-passed on both foreign-identity and unresolved-credentials paths — that admitted unauthenticated requests as if signature-verified, trivially spoofable by setting any access-key-id in the header. Post-fix the new opt-in flag `--allow-unverified-sigv4` (off by default) explicitly opts INTO the warn-and-pass behavior for both paths; in that mode the handler receives a clearly-fake `principalId = 'unverified-foreign-identity'` or `'unverified-no-creds'` so handler code cannot mistake the request for a verified call. Case-insensitive access-key compare at the `Credential` match step closes a related spoofing path where mixed-case AKIDs would fail the strict-equality compare. **Explicitly out of scope**: IAM policy evaluation (resource / action / condition rules) — that requires the deployed IAM data plane, separate architectural project. Signature-verified callers reach the handler under their own identity; downstream authorization is the dev's responsibility. **Implementation**: new `IamAuthorizer` discriminated union member in [src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts](src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts) (synthetic `logicalId: 'AWS_IAM'` — no companion `AWS::ApiGateway::Authorizer` resource exists for IAM); `detectRestV1Authorizer` short-circuits on `AuthorizationType === 'AWS_IAM'` at the Method level (before the `AuthorizerId` Ref check) and returns the new kind. [src/local/http-server.ts](src/local/http-server.ts) `runAuthorizerPass` extended with an `iam` branch — no result cache (every request has a unique signature; AWS-deployed API Gateway doesn't cache AWS_IAM either) — and `buildOverlay` emits the REST v1 lambda-style overlay with the access-key-id as `principalId`. New `StartApiServerOptions` fields `sigV4CredentialsLoader` (lazy-resolved at most once per server lifecycle), `sigV4WarnedForeignIds` (dedup set for the opt-in warn-and-pass mode), and `sigV4AllowUnverified` (the opt-in toggle). [src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts](src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts) new CLI option `--allow-unverified-sigv4` with explicit fail-closed-by-default help text; detects IAM routes at boot, emits a one-line `warnIamRoutes` summary naming every affected route + an explicit "fail-closed; pass --allow-unverified-sigv4 for warn-and-pass dev mode" caveat. Docs updated in [docs/local-emulation.md](docs/local-emulation.md) (new "AWS_IAM authorizer" subsection spelling out the verify-vs-emulate boundary, accepted tooling — `curl --aws-sigv4`, Postman, `awscurl`, AWS SDK signers — and the opt-in unverified-pass behavior) + README.md authorizer list. 38 new unit tests at [tests/unit/local/sigv4-verify.test.ts](tests/unit/local/sigv4-verify.test.ts) covering parser positive + 4 reject paths; canonicalizePath / canonicalizeQueryString cases; `validateAmzDateMatchesCredentialDate` and `amzDateOutsideSkew`; and `verifySigV4` end-to-end for the full fail-closed + opt-in matrix (accept-valid / missing-auth / tampered-sig / tampered-body / expired-timestamp / malformed-header / unsupported-algorithm / foreign-identity DENIES by default / foreign-identity ALLOW-with-flag emits placeholder principalId / credentials-load-failure DENIES by default / credentials-load-failure ALLOW-with-flag emits placeholder / scope-date-mismatch / stable-identity-hash / session-token passthrough / case-insensitive AKID match / AWS reference test vector round-trip). The existing [tests/unit/local/authorizer-resolver.test.ts](tests/unit/local/authorizer-resolver.test.ts) "hard-errors on AWS_IAM REST v1 (deferred)" test was inverted to assert the new `kind: 'iam'` attachment.

- ✅ Feature: `cdkd local start-api` Cognito User Pool multi-pool federation (closes [#456](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/456)). Pre-PR `src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts` only inspected `ProviderARNs[0]` and ignored the rest — CDK apps with federated identity (multiple user pools on one authorizer, e.g. a multi-tenant SaaS with one pool per tenant) could only verify tokens issued by the first pool; every other pool's token rejected with "signature verification failed". Post-PR every entry in `ProviderARNs[]` is parsed at discovery time into a new `pools: ReadonlyArray<CognitoPoolRef>` field on `CognitoUserPoolAuthorizer` (each `{userPoolArn, region, userPoolId}`); the legacy top-level `userPoolArn` / `region` / `userPoolId` fields stay as backward-compat aliases pointing at `pools[0]` so any downstream caller reading them keeps working. **Request-time pool selection**: `verifyCognitoJwt` in [src/local/cognito-jwt.ts](src/local/cognito-jwt.ts) parses the JWT's unverified `iss` claim, walks `pools[]` to find the matching `https://cognito-idp.<region>.amazonaws.com/<userPoolId>` entry, fetches THAT pool's JWKS, and runs full signature / `exp` / `iss` verification against it. A token whose `iss` matches no configured pool rejects with 401 **without touching JWKS** — multi-pool federation must not accept a token whose issuer was never registered. **Security fix (post-review BLOCKER)**: when EVERY pool's JWKS is in pass-through mode (e.g. JWKS fetch failed at boot in offline corporate-proxy environments), the resolver now rejects a malformed / unparseable JWT instead of admitting it. Pre-fix, a multi-pool configuration where pool[0] had passed-through JWKS would accept any token that "looked like" it claimed pool[0]'s issuer — and an unparseable string would skip the issuer check, falling through to the pass-through admit branch. Post-fix, when `pools.length > 1` and the token is unparseable / has a 2-part header.payload structure, the resolver returns 401 / 403 with no JWKS contact (a configuration-only attack surface is closed). A cross-pool signature mismatch (token claims pool A as issuer but is signed with pool B's key) rejects naturally because pool A's JWKS doesn't carry pool B's kid. **Discovery hard-fails on any malformed entry** — a single bad ARN aborts the whole authorizer at boot with the offending `ProviderARNs[<idx>]` index named, rather than failing mid-request for one tenant only. **Per-pool JWKS pass-through**: the CLI's `prewarmJwks` (in [src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts](src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts)) now iterates `auth.pools` and pre-warms a JWKS URL per pool; each URL gets its own `JwksCache` entry with the existing TTL semantics (1hr success / 60s failure short-TTL from PR 8b), so one pool unreachable degrades to pass-through for that pool only — sibling pools still verify normally. **Backward compat**: a single-element `ProviderARNs[]` (the historical single-pool case) behaves identically to pre-PR — `pools[0]` is the only candidate and the `iss` check matches it. **Error-message UX**: pre-PR `pickStringFromArn` hard-coded "ProviderARNs[0]" in every error message; post-PR the resolver threads the actual index into the `<stack>/<authorizer>.ProviderARNs[<idx>]` location so users see exactly which entry is malformed. Implementation across [src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts](src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts) (new `CognitoPoolRef` type, `pools[]` walk in `resolveRestV1Authorizer`'s `COGNITO_USER_POOLS` branch, per-index error locations on `pickStringFromArn`) + [src/local/cognito-jwt.ts](src/local/cognito-jwt.ts) (request-time `iss`-driven pool selection in `verifyCognitoJwt`; multi-pool malformed-token reject; new private `buildCognitoIssuer` helper; defensive fallback to legacy single-pool fields preserves any third-party caller that constructs the authorizer literal without `pools`) + [src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts](src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts) (`prewarmJwks` iterates `auth.pools`). 10 new / updated unit tests: 3 in [tests/unit/local/authorizer-resolver.test.ts](tests/unit/local/authorizer-resolver.test.ts) (multi-pool extraction with 3 ARNs / malformed-entry rejection / index-named error message) + 7 in [tests/unit/local/cognito-jwt.test.ts](tests/unit/local/cognito-jwt.test.ts) (verify token signed by SECOND configured pool against its own JWKS / issuer-mismatch reject without touching JWKS / cross-pool signature mismatch / single-element pools[] backward compat / per-pool JWKS pass-through where one pool is reachable and the other not / multi-pool malformed-token DENY when unparseable / multi-pool malformed-token DENY when 2-part).

- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` / `cdkd local run-task` cross-account / cross-region ECR pull (closes [#455](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/455)). Pre-PR `src/local/ecr-puller.ts:pullEcrImage` hard-errored on every cross-account or cross-region ECR image URI with a "deferred to a follow-up PR" pointer, forcing users with centralized shared-services ECR registries (or multi-region registries) to do a full deploy + AWS-side invoke just to exercise locally — defeating the local-emulation value proposition for the most common enterprise ECR setup. Post-fix, `pullEcrImage` accepts an optional `ecrRoleArn?: string` and auto-detects cross-account from `sts:GetCallerIdentity`: same-account / same-region keeps the pre-PR fast path (no STS hop, default credential chain), explicit `--ecr-role-arn <arn>` issues `sts:AssumeRole` via the default credential chain (1-hour session, session name `cdkd-local-ecr-<ts>`) and threads the resulting temporary credentials into the ECR client, cross-account WITHOUT `--ecr-role-arn` proceeds with the caller's credentials (works when the target ECR repository's resource policy grants the caller directly via cross-account IAM grant; AWS surfaces a clean `AccessDenied` if missing, and the info log points users at `--ecr-role-arn`), and cross-region authenticates against the URI's region directly (the ECR client is built for `parsed.region`, NOT the caller's profile region). The `EcrPullOptions.region` field semantics narrowed from "caller-region guard input" to "STS seed region only" — the ECR client always builds for the URI's region. **`--no-pull` short-circuits BEFORE any STS calls** so a `--no-pull --ecr-role-arn` combo doesn't waste a single STS round-trip on a path that only verifies the local cache. **Module-level STS credential caching** (#485 follow-up): `pullEcrImage` caches both `GetCallerIdentity` (keyed by `callerRegion`) and `AssumeRole` (keyed by `(roleArn, callerRegion)`) at module scope with a 5-minute safety margin against the recorded STS `Expiration`, so an ECS run-task with N containers under one `--ecr-role-arn` issues only 1× GetCallerIdentity + 1× AssumeRole regardless of N. New `--ecr-role-arn <arn>` flag wired into `cdkd local invoke` (consumed by `resolveContainerImagePlan`'s ECR-pull fallback when no matching cdk.out asset is found) and `cdkd local run-task` (threaded through `RunEcsTaskOptions.ecrRoleArn` to `prepareOneImage`'s ECS-task ECR branch in `src/local/ecs-task-runner.ts`). **`cdkd local start-api` flag deferred**: start-api currently rejects container Lambdas at boot (the only ECR-pull entry point), so wiring the flag there would be a UX trap (silently-ignored option) — added in the same PR that lands container Lambda support in start-api. Per-error class `LocalInvokeBuildError` for AssumeRole failures includes the role ARN and the underlying STS error (e.g. `AccessDenied`) plus a trust-policy hint. Pre-fix hard-error messages (`Cross-account ECR pull is not supported in cdkd local invoke v1 — deferred to a follow-up PR.` / `Cross-region ECR pull is not supported in cdkd local invoke v1 — deferred to a follow-up PR.`) removed entirely. Stale "Tier 3 deferred" comment in [src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts](src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts) `parseContainerImage` JSDoc updated to point at the new helper behavior. Implementation: [src/local/ecr-puller.ts](src/local/ecr-puller.ts) (new `ecrRoleArn` field + `assumeRoleForEcr` helper + branched-on-`assumed` ECR client construction + skipPull short-circuit relocated above STS block + module-level caches for GetCallerIdentity + AssumeRole) + [src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts](src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts) (new `LocalInvokeOptions.ecrRoleArn` field + `--ecr-role-arn <arn>` Option + plumbed through `resolveContainerImagePlan`) + [src/cli/commands/local-run-task.ts](src/cli/commands/local-run-task.ts) (new `LocalRunTaskOptions.ecrRoleArn` + `--ecr-role-arn <arn>` Option + plumbed through `runOpts`) + [src/local/ecs-task-runner.ts](src/local/ecs-task-runner.ts) (new `RunEcsTaskOptions.ecrRoleArn` + plumbed to `pullEcrImage`). 19 unit tests in [tests/unit/local/ecr-puller.test.ts](tests/unit/local/ecr-puller.test.ts) (rewritten from 8) covering same-account fast path / cross-region no-longer-hard-errors / cross-account without role pass-through / cross-account with role full STS hop + threaded creds / same-account-with-role explicit opt-in / cross-region + cross-account + role full matrix / AssumeRole failure surfaces actionable error / AssumeRole returns no Credentials clear error / GetCallerIdentity no Account clear error / skipPull short-circuits before STS / explicit-region option seeds STS not ECR / cached GetCallerIdentity / cached AssumeRole / stale-expiration eviction / per-`(roleArn, region)` isolation / no-Expiration defensive fallback. Real-AWS integ deliberately not extended in this PR (cross-account requires a 2nd AWS account's pre-published image — opt-in flag `CDKD_TEST_CROSS_ACCOUNT_ECR=1` deferred to a follow-up since the default integ stays single-account; the new code paths are fully covered at the unit layer).

- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` and `cdkd local start-api` now honor Lambda `Properties.EphemeralStorage.Size` via `--tmpfs /tmp:rw,size=<N>m` (closes (#440)). CDK 2.x's `lambda.Function({ ephemeralStorageSize: cdk.Size.gibibytes(N) })` synthesizes `EphemeralStorage: { Size: N * 1024 }` (MiB; default 512, max 10240). Pre-fix the field was silently dropped at the lambda-resolver layer, so the local container's `/tmp` was a regular overlay-fs path with no size cap: handlers writing > 512 MiB succeeded locally but failed in AWS with `IOError: No space left on device`, and handlers detecting available `/tmp` size via `statvfs` / `df` saw the host's free space instead of the configured cap. Post-fix the resolver surfaces `ephemeralStorageMb?: number` on the shared `ResolvedLambdaBase` (so both ZIP and IMAGE Lambdas inherit it — `--tmpfs` overlays mount-time inside any container regardless of base image), the docker-runner accepts an optional `tmpfs?: { target: string; sizeMb: number }` on `runDetached` and emits `--tmpfs <target>:rw,size=<sizeMb>m`, and both CLI commands plumb the value through (`cdkd local invoke` via `ImagePlan.tmpfs`, `cdkd local start-api` via `ContainerSpec.tmpfs` resolved once at server boot in `buildContainerSpec`). The shared parser `extractEphemeralStorageMb` in [src/local/lambda-resolver.ts](src/local/lambda-resolver.ts) enforces the AWS 10240 MiB ceiling at parse time (templates over the limit hard-error with an actionable message at `cdkd local invoke` boot rather than hanging on a `docker run` that AWS would have refused anyway), floors fractional MiB values (`docker --tmpfs size=...m` accepts integers only), and silently drops intrinsic-valued `Size` entries (the `{Ref: 'SomeParam'}` shape that's uncommon for `EphemeralStorage` but theoretically valid — local invoke can't resolve those without the template's Parameters context the deploy engine has, and the safe fallback is no `--tmpfs` which preserves pre-#440 behavior). The `--tmpfs` flag is emitted AFTER the `-e` env block and BEFORE `--workdir` in the docker-runner argv (between mount-shaped flags and image-config flags); single source of truth `/tmp` target is centralized in `resolveTmpfsForLambda` in [src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts](src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts) and the equivalent inline call site in [src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts](src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts). Container Lambdas (`Code.ImageUri`) get the cap too — `--tmpfs` overlays inside container images just like on the public base images, and `EphemeralStorage` applies to both AWS Lambda packaging types. New unit tests: 7 in [tests/unit/local/lambda-resolver.test.ts](tests/unit/local/lambda-resolver.test.ts) (ZIP / IMAGE surface / omit-when-absent / > 10240 rejection / fractional-floor / intrinsic-drop / non-object-malformed-drop), 3 in [tests/unit/local/docker-runner.test.ts](tests/unit/local/docker-runner.test.ts) (flag emission / omission / argv ordering between -e env and --workdir), 2 in [tests/unit/cli/local-invoke-resolve-plan.test.ts](tests/unit/cli/local-invoke-resolve-plan.test.ts) (IMAGE branch ImagePlan.tmpfs surfacing + omission), and 2 in [tests/unit/local/container-pool.test.ts](tests/unit/local/container-pool.test.ts) (ContainerSpec.tmpfs propagation through startOne + omission).

- ✅ Fix: `cdkd local start-api` accepts `Fn::Sub` shapes on `AWS::ApiGatewayV2::Route.Target` (closes [#444](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/444)). Pre-fix `parseHttpApiTargetIntegration` in [src/local/route-discovery.ts](src/local/route-discovery.ts) accepted only the two CDK 2.x-canonical `Fn::Join` shapes (`['/', ['integrations', { Ref }]]` and `['', ['integrations/', { Ref }]]`) plus the literal `'integrations/<id>'` string; a `CfnRoute` with `target: cdk.Fn.sub('integrations/${IntId}', { IntId: cfnInteg.ref })` (verified via real `cdk synth` 2026-05-22) synthesized a 2-arg `Fn::Sub` that hard-failed route discovery for the whole API at boot with the misleading "Target must be 'integrations/<id>' or Fn::Join..." error. Post-fix, `parseHttpApiTargetIntegration` recognizes both `Fn::Sub` forms — 1-arg `{Fn::Sub: 'integrations/${LogicalId}'}` (AWS-docs canonical form, the placeholder name is a direct Ref to the integration logical ID; dotted refs like `${X.attr}` are rejected since Integration has no GetAtt shape that produces a route-Target id) and 2-arg `{Fn::Sub: ['integrations/${Var}', { Var: { Ref: 'LogicalId' } }]}` (what `cdk.Fn.sub(template, vars)` synthesizes when users build `target` programmatically). Both forms require the load-bearing `integrations/` prefix in the template so a `Fn::Sub` referencing something unrelated still hard-errors with the same shape as any other bad input. Error message updated to mention the new accepted shape. 4 new unit tests in [tests/unit/local/route-discovery.test.ts](tests/unit/local/route-discovery.test.ts) covering Fn::Sub 1-arg / Fn::Sub 2-arg / reject-non-integrations-prefix / reject-non-Ref-binding. **Audit context**: this is the canonical user-visible gap surfaced by the broader intrinsic-coverage audit. The audit also identified two deferred residuals filed as follow-up sub-issues — [#470](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/470) (`pickStringFromArn` rejects `Fn::GetAtt` on REST v1 Cognito Authorizer ProviderARNs — needs `--from-state` plumbing to derive the JWKS URL) and [#471](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/471) (three private `pickRefLogicalId` helpers should consolidate into a shared util). The full audit / coverage matrix is captured at [issue #444](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/444) as a comment thread for future replays. REST v1 ResourceId / ParentId fields accept only `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt RootResourceId` and never `Fn::Sub`, but empirical `cdk synth` shows CDK never emits Fn::Sub there — left as documented theoretical gap rather than a sub-issue.

- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke --assume-role` now accepts an optional value (`[arn]` Commander grammar) and auto-resolves the execution-role ARN from cdkd state when paired with `--from-state` (closes [#442](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/442)). Pre-PR the flag was explicit-ARN-only: users had to look up the deployed function's role ARN themselves on every invocation, so they defaulted to passing through their typically-admin shell credentials — and the local handler accidentally succeeded against AWS APIs the deployed function would be denied (the "local pass / production fail" trap). Post-PR `--assume-role` has three forms: (1) `--assume-role <arn>` — explicit ARN (existing PR 1 behavior, takes precedence when set); (2) `--assume-role` (bare) — auto-resolves the function's `Properties.Role` from cdkd state and assumes that ARN automatically; (3) `--no-assume-role` — explicit opt-out that forces dev creds even with `--from-state`. The new helper `resolveExecutionRoleArnFromState(state, logicalId)` in [src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts](src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts) (exported for unit testing) walks `state.resources[<Fn>].properties.Role` (with `observedProperties.Role` fallback): literal-string ARNs starting with `arn:` pass through; `{Fn::GetAtt: [<RoleId>, 'Arn']}` and `{Ref: <RoleId>}` shapes resolve against the sibling IAM Role resource's `attributes.Arn` (recorded at deploy time by `IAMRoleProvider.create` / drift refresh); `Fn::Sub` / `Fn::Join` and other shapes return `undefined` in v1 — once a real CDK app emits those shapes for `Role` the resolver gets extended per memory rule `feedback_verify_cdk_synth_shape_before_resolver.md`. The pre-existing `suggestAssumeRoleFromState` hint path is preserved for users who do NOT opt into auto-assume — when `--from-state` is set without `--assume-role`, the deployed role ARN is still logged once as a hint so users can discover the scoped-credentials path. **Auto-resolve gate**: bare `--assume-role` without `--from-state` warns + falls back to dev creds (no state to read against). **STS failure mode**: insufficient permissions / trust-policy mismatch surfaces a warn + falls back to dev creds — this is a developer-loop tool, not a security boundary, and a hard-error on STS rejection would block iteration. **Precedence**: explicit `--assume-role <arn>` wins over auto-resolved ARN; `--no-assume-role` wins over both. Commander's auto-negation collapses `--no-assume-role` onto `options.assumeRole = false`, so the runner branches on `typeof options.assumeRole` (`string` → explicit ARN, `true` → auto-resolve, `false` → opt-out, `undefined` → default). 13 new unit tests in [tests/unit/cli/local-invoke-auto-assume-role.test.ts](tests/unit/cli/local-invoke-auto-assume-role.test.ts) covering the resolver's full per-shape matrix: literal-ARN pass-through / Fn::GetAtt array-form + dot-form lookup / Ref-shape lookup / sibling-missing fallback / Arn-attribute-missing fallback / Fn::Sub + Fn::Join out-of-scope rejection / observedProperties fallback when properties.Role is absent / properties precedence over observedProperties / Role-absent + Lambda-absent guards. The real-AWS integ at [tests/integration/local-invoke-from-state/](tests/integration/local-invoke-from-state/) is unchanged in this PR (the new code paths are unit-test-covered; threading STS-assume through the existing integ requires extending the fixture's IAM Role with a trust policy that allows the integ runner's principal — deferred to a follow-up).

- ✅ Drift coverage v3 push (batch 1, [#445](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/445)): per-provider `getDriftUnknownPaths` audit + Lambda `Code.ImageUri` recovery. Walked all 11 providers that declare `getDriftUnknownPaths` and classified every entry into category 1 (architecturally unrecoverable — AWS redacts on read / no read API / not part of read shape), 2 (recoverable via secondary SDK call), or 3 (recoverable from a response cdkd already has). Audit finding: 10 of 11 providers' declarations are already category 1 with sound inline rationale (firehose write-only `Password` / `AccessKey` redacted on `DescribeDeliveryStream`; secretsmanager `SecretString` / `GenerateSecretString` deliberately not surfaced to avoid plaintext leak; lambda-layer `Content` is a pre-signed URL on `GetLayerVersionByArn`; sns-topic `Subscription` managed via separate `AWS::SNS::Subscription` resource; servicediscovery `PrivateDnsNamespace.Vpc` not returned by `GetNamespace`; kms `BypassPolicyLockoutSafetyCheck` / `PendingWindowInDays` are create/delete-only inputs; appsync `GraphQLSchema.DefinitionS3Location` is write-only on `GetIntrospectionSchema`; ec2 6 sub-resource types' `Tags` defense-in-depth — CFn schemas don't model Tags; cloudfront-oai `CallerReference` is cdkd-set to logicalId at create regardless of template; dynamodb-globaltable already empty after PR #391). **`AWS::Lambda::Function.Code` is the category 3 lift in this PR** — pre-PR `getDriftUnknownPaths` returned the whole `['Code']` subtree, which also hid `Code.ImageUri` drift on container Lambdas (`PackageType: 'Image'`). `GetFunction.Code.ImageUri` IS returned by AWS for container Lambdas; only the ZIP-side sub-paths (`Code.S3Bucket` / `Code.S3Key` / `Code.S3ObjectVersion` / `Code.ZipFile` / `Code.SourceKMSKeyArn`) are genuinely unrecoverable (AWS returns a pre-signed `Code.Location` URL, never the original asset key). Post-PR `readCurrentState` surfaces `Code: { ImageUri }` when AWS reports it (container Lambdas only — ZIP-package Lambdas continue to omit the `Code` key entirely so the comparator's state-keys-only walk handles their absence cleanly), and `getDriftUnknownPaths` narrows to the 5 ZIP-side sub-paths so the comparator skips them via the `entry + '.'` prefix-match semantics. Console-side image swaps on `lambda.DockerImageFunction` constructs (or `Code.fromAssetImage`) now surface as drift instead of being silently ignored. `Code.ResolvedImageUri` (post-resolution digest, AWS-managed) is intentionally NOT surfaced — it changes on every ECR push of the same tag and would fire false drift on benign re-pushes. Implementation in [src/provisioning/providers/lambda-function-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/lambda-function-provider.ts) (`readCurrentState` + `getDriftUnknownPaths` + updated docstrings); 3 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/lambda-function-provider-readcurrentstate.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/lambda-function-provider-readcurrentstate.test.ts) (container Lambda surfaces `Code.ImageUri` and drops `ResolvedImageUri` / ZIP Lambda omits the `Code` key / `getDriftUnknownPaths` shape regression guard). The 10 already-category-1 providers' declarations stay unchanged; their rationale was independently re-verified during the audit and the existing inline comments are sufficient.

- ✅ Fix: `docker build` parity with CDK CLI's `cdk-assets-lib` (closes "`# syntax=docker/dockerfile:1` Dockerfile fails in cdkd but works in `cdk deploy`" regression). Pre-fix, cdkd's `src/assets/docker-build.ts` invoked `docker build` via Node's `execFile` with `maxBuffer: 50 * 1024 * 1024`. On hosts where BuildKit's progress output exceeded that ceiling (typical first-time frontend-image pull + multi-stage build with `# syntax=docker/dockerfile:1` + heredocs / `RUN --mount=type=cache`), `execFile` silently killed the child process with `ERR_CHILD_PROCESS_STDIO_MAXBUFFER` and the build looked like a Dockerfile syntax failure. CDK CLI was unaffected because it uses streaming `spawn` with no `maxBuffer`. Post-fix, a new shared helper at [src/utils/docker-cmd.ts](src/utils/docker-cmd.ts) (`getDockerCmd` + `runDockerStreaming` + `spawnStreaming`) routes every docker subprocess call through streaming spawn: stdout/stderr are collected via push-based event handlers (no ceiling), and when `--verbose` is set the chunks are also mirrored to `process.stdout` / `process.stderr` so the user sees live progress. Build env now sets `BUILDX_NO_DEFAULT_ATTESTATIONS=1` (matches `cdk-assets-lib`'s `Docker.build`) so Buildx does not attach the provenance attestation manifest that ECR rejects on single-arch pull. **`CDK_DOCKER` env var**: `getDockerCmd()` reads `process.env.CDK_DOCKER` and falls back to `'docker'`, letting podman / finch / nerdctl users swap the binary without code changes. Wired through every docker call site in cdkd: [src/assets/docker-build.ts](src/assets/docker-build.ts), [src/assets/docker-asset-publisher.ts](src/assets/docker-asset-publisher.ts) (build / login / tag / push), [src/local/ecr-puller.ts](src/local/ecr-puller.ts) (login / pull / image inspect / `--no-pull` verifier), [src/local/docker-runner.ts](src/local/docker-runner.ts) (pull / run / logs / rm / version probe), [src/local/ecs-network.ts](src/local/ecs-network.ts) (network create / sidecar / network rm), [src/local/ecs-task-runner.ts](src/local/ecs-task-runner.ts) (volume rm / run / wait / stop / logs), and [src/local/docker-image-builder.ts](src/local/docker-image-builder.ts) (local-invoke container Lambda build + executable re-tag). **`DockerImageAssetSource` type widened to match the official CDK Cloud Assembly schema**: new fields `executable` (build-script source mode), `dockerBuildContexts` (`--build-context`, BuildKit 1.4+), `dockerBuildSsh` (`--ssh`), `dockerBuildSecrets` (`--secret`), `networkMode` (`--network`), `platform` (`--platform` from manifest), `cacheFrom` (`--cache-from`), `cacheTo` (`--cache-to`), and `cacheDisabled` (`--no-cache`); the new `DockerCacheOption` type carries `{type, params?}` with the standard `type=...,k=v,...` flag formatter. `directory` is now optional (mutually exclusive with `executable`). **`executable` source mode**: when set, cdkd runs the user-supplied command in the asset directory (or `cdkOutDir` if no `directory` is given), captures stdout, treats it as the local image tag. The publisher and local-invoke / ECS run-task paths then re-tag the script's output to their deterministic `cdkd-asset-<hash>` / `cdkd-local-invoke-<hash>` / `cdkd-local-run-task-<hash>` name via `docker tag` so downstream push / `--no-build` cache reuse keep working unchanged. **`buildDockerImage` signature change** (internal-only): from `(asset, cdkOutDir, tag, opts)` to `(asset, cdkOutDir, opts)` with `tag` moved into `opts` and the function returning the actual local tag (the input `tag` in directory mode, the script's stdout in executable mode). Build-arg iteration order via `Object.entries` is preserved (load-bearing for layer-cache stability across the publisher + local-invoke + ECS run-task paths). New unit tests in [tests/unit/utils/docker-cmd.test.ts](tests/unit/utils/docker-cmd.test.ts) (`CDK_DOCKER` resolution) and [tests/unit/assets/docker-build.test.ts](tests/unit/assets/docker-build.test.ts) (BUILDX_NO_DEFAULT_ATTESTATIONS=1 env path + every BuildKit flag forwarding + executable source mode + flag ordering). Existing [tests/unit/assets/docker-asset-publisher.test.ts](tests/unit/assets/docker-asset-publisher.test.ts) / [tests/unit/local/docker-image-builder.test.ts](tests/unit/local/docker-image-builder.test.ts) / [tests/unit/local/ecr-puller.test.ts](tests/unit/local/ecr-puller.test.ts) migrated from low-level `node:child_process` mocking to `src/utils/docker-cmd.js` mocking so they exercise the post-fix code path. Real-Docker integ at [tests/integration/local-invoke-buildkit/](tests/integration/local-invoke-buildkit/) builds a Dockerfile that declares `# syntax=docker/dockerfile:1` AND uses BuildKit-only heredocs + `RUN --mount=type=cache` and invokes the resulting container Lambda end-to-end; deploys nothing.

- ✅ Fix: `cdkd local start-api` no longer hard-errors at boot when an authorizer's `AuthorizerUri` Lambda Arn intrinsic does not resolve to a same-template Lambda (closes [#431](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/431)). Pre-fix the route-level `IntegrationUri` got the deferred-501 treatment in PR #430, but `authorizer-resolver.ts:resolveLambdaArn` (called from `detectRestV1Authorizer` / `detectHttpApiAuthorizer`) still threw `RouteDiscoveryError`, so a CUSTOM / REQUEST authorizer with a cross-stack `AuthorizerUri` aborted boot for the whole API — asymmetric with how the same unresolvable shape on `IntegrationUri` was handled. Fix introduces a private `AuthorizerLambdaUnresolvableError` (subclass of `RouteDiscoveryError` so existing `instanceof RouteDiscoveryError` tests on direct calls to `resolveHttpApiAuthorizer` / `resolveRestV1Authorizer` still pass); `attachAuthorizers` catches it before the generic catch and flips the route to `{...route, unsupported: {reason: ...}}` with the resolver's detail prefixed by `authorizer Lambda Arn unresolvable —`. The route appears in the route table as `[501 Not Implemented]`, boot continues, HTTP 501 + reason JSON body at request time — symmetric with route-level unresolvable `IntegrationUri`. Cognito / JWT authorizers unaffected (no Lambda Arn resolution at boot); structural authorizer errors (AWS_IAM, missing `JwtConfiguration`, malformed identity source, unknown `Type`) stay hard-errors because they're template-structural problems not Lambda-Arn cross-stack issues. The class-1 vs class-2 distinction matters because attaching no authorizer + leaving the route normal would silently expose a user-protected route to unauthenticated requests just because the authorizer Lambda is in another stack — the deferred-501 is the safe failure mode. Implementation in [src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts](src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts) (new private subclass + `resolveLambdaArn` throws the typed error + `attachAuthorizers` per-route catch). The TS `erasableSyntaxOnly` mode rejects `constructor(public readonly reason: string)` parameter properties, so the field is declared separately and assigned in the constructor body. The `RouteDiscoveryError` parent's `Object.setPrototypeOf(this, RouteDiscoveryError.prototype)` (the well-known `extends Error` transpile-target workaround) overrides the subclass prototype, so the constructor re-applies `Object.setPrototypeOf(this, AuthorizerLambdaUnresolvableError.prototype)` after `super()` — without this `instanceof AuthorizerLambdaUnresolvableError` in `attachAuthorizers` returns false and the deferred-501 path doesn't trigger. 4 new unit tests in [tests/unit/local/authorizer-resolver.test.ts](tests/unit/local/authorizer-resolver.test.ts) (REST v1 TOKEN cross-stack / REST v1 REQUEST cross-stack / HTTP API v2 REQUEST cross-stack / structural-error stays hard-error). Integ fixture at [tests/integration/local-start-api/lib/local-start-api-stack.ts](tests/integration/local-start-api/lib/local-start-api-stack.ts) extended with a `/v1/cross-stack-auth` route whose `AuthorizerUri` is overridden via `addPropertyOverride` to a cross-stack-shape `Fn::Sub: '${ImportedAuthFn.Arn}'`; verify.sh asserts the route returns 501 + reason body without invoking any Lambda. The CFn override pattern (`feedback_inject_intrinsic_via_override.md`) lets the fixture exercise the cross-stack path without spinning up a separate stack.
- ✅ `cdkd local start-api`: deferred-error unsupported routes + REST v1 MOCK CORS preflight subset. Pre-PR the discovery layer threw `RouteDiscoveryError` on the FIRST per-route integration it could not emulate (most commonly the OPTIONS Method backed by a MOCK integration that CDK's `RestApi({ defaultCorsPreflightOptions: ... })` auto-emits), so a single unsupported route blocked boot for the whole API. Post-PR every discoverable route classifies into one of four buckets: (1) **normal** (AWS_PROXY + resolvable Lambda Arn — dispatched as before); (2) **synthetic CORS preflight** (`mockCors` on `DiscoveredRoute` — REST v1 `HttpMethod: OPTIONS` + `Integration.Type: MOCK` + `IntegrationResponses[].ResponseParameters` carrying literal `method.response.header.Access-Control-Allow-*` pairs in AWS's `"'value'"` literal-with-quotes shape; the http-server returns the captured status + headers directly on OPTIONS without invoking any Lambda); (3) **deferred-error unsupported** (`unsupported.reason` on `DiscoveredRoute` — non-AWS_PROXY REST v1 integrations other than the MOCK CORS preflight subset, HTTP API v2 service integrations with `IntegrationSubtype`, WebSocket APIs (`ProtocolType: WEBSOCKET`), Function URLs with `AuthType !== 'NONE'` or `InvokeMode: RESPONSE_STREAM`, and routes whose Lambda Arn intrinsic doesn't resolve against the same template — boot proceeds, http-server returns HTTP 501 + `{"message": "Not Implemented", "reason": <discovery reason>}` at request time); (4) **hard error** (template-structural failures: missing `Integration` on a Method, non-Ref `RestApiId` / `ApiId`, ParentId-chain cycle / missing parent / wrong parent type / missing PathPart, malformed Route `Target`, unresolvable `TargetFunctionArn` on a Function URL — boot still aborts via `RouteDiscoveryError` because there is not enough info to surface a meaningful 501). Boot prints a per-route `[warn]` summary of class (3) routes BEFORE the listening banner so users see the deferred 501s at startup, and the route table tags them `[501 Not Implemented]` / `[MOCK CORS preflight]` so the http-server's behavior on each path is obvious at a glance. `uniqueLambdaIds` (in [src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts](src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts)) skips class (2) / (3) routes when building the container pool, so unsupported routes do not waste boot time on containers that will never be called. The authorizer-attacher ([src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts](src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts)) also skips class (2) / (3) routes — defense-in-depth so a Function URL flagged unsupported for `AuthType: AWS_IAM` (used to be a hard error) doesn't surface here instead of as the cleaner 501. CORS preflight detection of class (2) is deliberately conservative — intrinsic-valued `ResponseParameters` are dropped silently (cdkd cannot evaluate VTL locally), and if the drop leaves zero header literals the route falls back to class (3) instead of returning a broken preflight. Implementation across [src/local/route-discovery.ts](src/local/route-discovery.ts) (new `DiscoveredRoute.unsupported` / `mockCors` fields + per-source classifier rewrites + `extractRestV1MockCorsConfig` helper), [src/local/http-server.ts](src/local/http-server.ts) (post-`matchRoute` short-circuit for mockCors → `writeMockCorsPreflight` and for unsupported → `writeNotImplemented`), [src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts](src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts) (skip-on-unsupported guard in `attachAuthorizers`), [src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts](src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts) (`uniqueLambdaIds` filter + `warnUnsupportedRoutes` summary + route-table label change in `printRouteTable`). 11 new / updated unit tests in [tests/unit/local/route-discovery.test.ts](tests/unit/local/route-discovery.test.ts) (CDK-shape MOCK CORS extraction + 204 default + non-OPTIONS MOCK fall-through + no-IntegrationResponses fall-through + intrinsic-`ResponseParameters` fall-through + per-integration unsupportedness on REST v1 / HTTP API v2 / Function URL + multi-error aggregation rewrite) + 3 new tests in [tests/unit/local/http-server.test.ts](tests/unit/local/http-server.test.ts) (501 body shape + no Lambda invoke on unsupported + 204 preflight no Lambda invoke). The CDK CLI emits `Integration.Type: MOCK` on every OPTIONS Method created by `defaultCorsPreflightOptions`, so the most common reason `cdkd local start-api` rejected a real-world CDK app at boot is now resolved end-to-end (preflight headers served locally) instead of either / both of the previous hard-error / opt-out paths.
- ✅ Fix: `DiffCalculator.valuesEqual` no longer silently treats "one-side intrinsic, other-side concrete" as equal. Pre-fix, `src/analyzer/diff-calculator.ts:351` returned `true` whenever either side was a CFn intrinsic node — the rationale was "state has resolved value like 'arn:...', template has `Fn::GetAtt` so we can't compare". This was load-bearing for the common case where the resolver successfully resolved the template intrinsic to the same string state already held; in that case `valuesEqual` saw two equal strings, not an intrinsic. But when the resolver **failed** (e.g. `Fn::GetAtt: [NewBucket, Arn]` referencing a resource not yet in state because the next deploy will CREATE it), the unresolvable intrinsic reached `valuesEqual` and the short-circuit silently masked the diff. Surfaced 2026-05-16 against a CDK app where a refactor moved `new s3.Bucket(this, 'SiteBucket', ...)` into a `Construct` wrapper (logical ID flipped from `SiteBucket397A1860` to `StaticSiteSiteBucket1A888BC8`); the BucketDeployment Lambda's inline IAM `DefaultPolicy` (same logical ID across both deploys — it's a sibling of the unchanged singleton Lambda's `ServiceRole`) carried `Resource: Fn::GetAtt: [<bucket-logical-id>, Arn]`. Pre-fix the diff calculator reported `0 to update` for the policy, the `PutRolePolicy` UPDATE was skipped, and the next deploy attempted to invoke the BucketDeployment CR against the newly-created bucket while the Lambda's role still allowed only the deleted old bucket — `aws s3 sync` rejected with `AccessDenied (s3:ListBucket) on resource "arn:aws:s3:::mystack-staticsitesitebucket1a888bc8"`. Post-fix, `valuesEqual` distinguishes three cases: (1) both sides intrinsic → structural compare via `JSON.stringify` (handles state-written-with-unresolved-intrinsic + identical-shape no-op); (2) one side intrinsic, other concrete → NOT equal (fail-safe to UPDATE; the resolver already tried best-effort, a remaining raw intrinsic typically means the intrinsic references a NEW resource not yet in state, which IS a real change); (3) both concrete → existing deep-equal path. Spurious UPDATEs on resource types whose update path is idempotent are acceptable; under-detecting was the real bug. Implementation in [src/analyzer/diff-calculator.ts](src/analyzer/diff-calculator.ts); 5 new / updated unit tests in [tests/unit/analyzer/diff-calculator.test.ts](tests/unit/analyzer/diff-calculator.test.ts) covering the canonical IAM-policy-rebound-to-new-bucket regression, both-sides-identical-intrinsic NO_CHANGE, both-sides-different-intrinsic UPDATE, and the unresolvable-on-template-side fail-safe path. Real-AWS integ at [tests/integration/diff-intrinsic-target-change/](tests/integration/diff-intrinsic-target-change/) deploys a top-level S3 Bucket + IAM Role with `bucket.grantReadWrite(role)` (CDK auto-emits an inline `DefaultPolicy` with `Resource: Fn::GetAtt: [<bucket>, Arn]`), then re-deploys with the bucket moved into a `Construct` wrapper (bucket logical ID flips, role's `DefaultPolicy` logical ID stays); verify.sh fetches the role's inline policy after each deploy via `iam:GetRolePolicy` and asserts the post-refactor policy references the v2 bucket's ARN and NOT the v1 bucket's. The post-refactor deploy plans `1 to create, 1 to update, 1 to delete` (pre-fix it was `1 to create, 0 to update, 1 to delete`).
- ✅ Scenario coverage matrix orphan closeout (follow-up to [#423](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/423) / PR #425). Closes both day-1 orphans surfaced by `vp run scenario-coverage`. **`deletion-policy-retain`** gets a new real-AWS integ at [tests/integration/deletion-policy-retain/](tests/integration/deletion-policy-retain/) — two `ssm.StringParameter` resources, one `RemovalPolicy.RETAIN` and one `RemovalPolicy.DESTROY`; `verify.sh` deploys, runs `cdkd destroy --force`, asserts the Retain param SURVIVED in SSM (`get-parameter` succeeds) while the Destroy param is gone (`ParameterNotFound`), then manually deletes the intentionally-retained param so AWS leaves clean. Cleanup trap covers leftover-state cases on early-exit. Verifies cdkd's `shouldRetainResource(deletionPolicy)` path in [src/types/state.ts](src/types/state.ts) end-to-end. **`partial-create-cleanup`** is REMOVED from `KNOWN_SCENARIOS` with an inline rationale comment in [scripts/build-scenario-coverage-matrix.ts](scripts/build-scenario-coverage-matrix.ts) — the behavior (PRs #374 / #377 / #378 / #379 / #380, ~12 providers) is exercised at the unit-test level (`tests/unit/provisioning/*-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts`), and mid-create-wiring failure injection on real AWS is impractical (no deterministic way to reject `applyTags` / `PutIntegrationResponse` / `RegisterScalableTarget` mid-flight after the parent `Create*Command` already succeeded). Keeping the tag in the canonical taxonomy as a permanent orphan would dilute the orphan-as-signal value of the matrix; the unit-test coverage IS the structural guarantee here. New tally: **89 / 89 fixtures annotated, 28 / 28 scenarios covered, 0 orphan** (was 88 / 88 / 27 / 29 / 2-orphan day-1).
- ✅ Phase 2B of #392 — scenario coverage **visibility report** (closes [#423](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/423)). [docs/scenario-coverage.md](docs/scenario-coverage.md) + `docs/_generated/scenario-coverage.json`, generated by [scripts/build-scenario-coverage-matrix.ts](scripts/build-scenario-coverage-matrix.ts), run via `vp run scenario-coverage`. Mirrors Phase 2A's shape on a DIFFERENT axis: Phase 1 (provider-coverage) tracks "is every registered AWS resource type exercised by at least one integ?" — structural answer, CI-gated. Phase 2A (CLI-flag coverage) tracks "does every declared CLI flag appear in some integ verify.sh?" — visibility-only. Phase 2B (this) tracks "does every cdkd-canonical real-AWS regression pattern have an integ backstop?" — visibility-only. Each `tests/integration/<fixture>/.scenarios.json` sidecar declares which canonical patterns the fixture exercises (`{"scenarios": ["vpc-lambda-eni-release", "nat-gateway-cleanup"]}`). Empty `[]` = "intentionally no canonical scenario applies" (per-service smoke tests). Absent file = "not yet annotated" (surfaced in the un-annotated section). Canonical taxonomy lives in [scripts/build-scenario-coverage-matrix.ts](scripts/build-scenario-coverage-matrix.ts) as `KNOWN_SCENARIOS` (29 entries spanning real-AWS DAG/eventual-consistency patterns, cross-stack references, custom-resource patterns, migration patterns, drift/state patterns, broad-regression sets, type-family-specific tricky patterns, local-execution patterns); a sidecar tag outside the taxonomy is hard-rejected at parse time so typos surface immediately. Day-1 backfill: 88 / 88 fixtures annotated, 27 / 29 scenarios covered, 2 legitimately orphan (`deletion-policy-retain` — no integ exercises it; `partial-create-cleanup` — unit-test-covered class of behavior, mid-deploy failure injection on real-AWS is impractical). The orphan-as-signal IS the value of the matrix. 28 unit tests at [tests/unit/scripts/build-scenario-coverage-matrix.test.ts](tests/unit/scripts/build-scenario-coverage-matrix.test.ts) cover sidecar parsing (malformed JSON / non-object root / missing key / non-string entries / whitespace-only), per-fixture reading, fixture listing, `buildReport` (un-annotated / opt-out / coverage mapping / orphan surfacing / unknown-tag capture / malformed throw / stable sort), `KNOWN_SCENARIOS` taxonomy invariants (lowercase-hyphenated names, non-empty single-line descriptions), and markdown rendering. CI auto-regen check wired in [.github/workflows/ci.yml](.github/workflows/ci.yml) following the same pattern as [#399](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/399): `vp run scenario-coverage` + `git diff --quiet -- docs/scenario-coverage.md docs/_generated/scenario-coverage.json` so a forgotten regeneration is a CI hard-fail rather than a soft skill-step warning. Adding a new scenario: 3 steps — add an entry to `KNOWN_SCENARIOS` with a one-line description, tag existing fixtures that exercise it (or write a new one), run `vp run scenario-coverage`. Removing a scenario: drop from `KNOWN_SCENARIOS` and the next regen surfaces every cleanup site as an invalid-tag error.

- ✅ Phase 2A of #392 — CLI flag coverage **visibility report** ([docs/cli-flag-coverage.md](docs/cli-flag-coverage.md) + `docs/_generated/cli-flag-coverage.json`, generated by `scripts/build-cli-flag-coverage-matrix.ts`, run via `vp run cli-flag-coverage`). Parses every `new Option('<spec>')` declared in [src/cli/options.ts](src/cli/options.ts) (single-line AND multi-line constructor calls) for long-form flag names + scans every `tests/integration/<name>/verify.sh` for `--<flag>` mentions, then surfaces "declared but not exercised in any integ verify.sh" as a per-flag review question. **Deliberately NOT a CI gate** (contrast with the provider-coverage matrix from PR #404 / #419) — many cdkd flags (`--dry-run`, `--verbose`, `--profile`, etc.) are tested adequately at the unit-test level; surfacing those as "uncovered" would produce >50% false-positive noise and defeat any gate's signal-to-noise. The right consumer is the contributor reviewing "does THIS flag warrant a real-AWS test?" — a question only the contributor can answer per-flag. 20 unit tests at [tests/unit/scripts/build-cli-flag-coverage-matrix.test.ts](tests/unit/scripts/build-cli-flag-coverage-matrix.test.ts) cover the parser helpers (flag-spec parser handles `<arg>` / `[arg]` / variadic / short+long forms; option-spec extraction handles single-line and multi-line `new Option(...)`; shell scan deduplicates and ignores short-form flags to keep the axis symmetric with declared-flags). Initial run: 10 / 27 declared flags exercised in integ verify.sh, 17 not — the gap mostly reflects unit-test coverage as designed. Phase 2B (scenario tag coverage matrix) tracked separately as [#423](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/423) because it needs design work (taxonomy + sidecar format + 88-fixture backfill) beyond the mechanical mirror this PR ships — shipped in the bullet above.

- ✅ Integration test coverage matrix + orphan-provider gate (closes [#392](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/392)). New script [scripts/build-integ-coverage-matrix.ts](scripts/build-integ-coverage-matrix.ts) parses `src/provisioning/register-providers.ts` for the registered SDK Provider type set and scans every `tests/integration/<name>/{lib,bin}/*.ts` for three coverage signals: literal `AWS::Service::Type` references (covers `CfnResource` / `addPropertyOverride` patterns AND `// covers: AWS::...` documentation comments), L1 `new <ns>.Cfn<TypeName>(` calls resolved via the import-line alias map, and L2 `new <ns>.<Construct>(` calls against a curated `CDK_L2_TO_L1` lookup table. Outputs [docs/integ-coverage.md](docs/integ-coverage.md) (human-readable per-type fixture list + orphan / allow-list summary) + `docs/_generated/integ-coverage.json` (machine-readable). Run via `vp run integ-coverage`. **New PreToolUse hook** at [.claude/hooks/provider-integ-gate.sh](.claude/hooks/provider-integ-gate.sh) blocks `git commit` when a new `registry.register('AWS::Foo::Bar', ...)` line is staged without matching integ coverage; mirrors `provider-docs-gate.sh`'s shape (cd / `git -C` resolution, refactor pass-through). Carve-out is the sidecar [.claude/integ-coverage-allowlist.json](.claude/integ-coverage-allowlist.json) (key = `AWS::Service::Type`, value = non-empty rationale string) — sidecar lives OUTSIDE `src/provisioning/register-providers.ts` so allow-list edits do not trigger the [integ-broad-gate](.claude/hooks/integ-broad-gate.sh)'s real-AWS broad integ requirement. Detection inside the hook is the rigorous-but-cheap subset (literal type id + `Cfn<Type>(` L1 class + sidecar entry) — pure-L2 fixtures rely on a `// covers:` documentation comment OR a refresh of the matrix. 17-case smoke test at `.claude/hooks/provider-integ-gate.test.sh` + 28 unit tests at `tests/unit/scripts/build-integ-coverage-matrix.test.ts`. Wired into [.claude/settings.json](.claude/settings.json) alongside the existing `provider-docs-gate.sh` and the new step in [.claude/skills/verify-pr/SKILL.md](.claude/skills/verify-pr/SKILL.md) regenerates the matrix and warns on dirty diff. **Day-1 backfill**: 8 existing fixtures gained `// covers: <type>` comments documenting transitively-covered orphans (`apigateway` / `api-cognito` for Method/Resource/Stage/Deployment; `alb` for Listener/TargetGroup/SecurityGroupIngress; `ec2-vpc` for NetworkAclEntry/SubnetNetworkAclAssociation; `remove-protection` for InstanceProfile via L2 ASG; `infra-security` for UserToGroupAddition+KMS::Alias; `dynamodb-streams` for EventSourceMapping; `bedrock-agentcore` for the alpha L2 `agentcore.Runtime`); 13 sidecar entries cover genuinely-uncovered types (Glue Workflow / SecurityConfiguration / Job / Crawler / Connection / Trigger / Kinesis StreamConsumer / S3Tables Namespace + Table / RDS DBProxy + DBProxyTargetGroup + DBProxyEndpoint / ServiceDiscovery::Service / ApiGateway::Account). Sibling PR [#401](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/390) (`audit-provider-coverage`) tackles a different axis (provider-internal capability coverage); the two artifacts are complementary. Final tally: 98 / 111 covered, 13 allow-listed, 0 silent orphans (matches the issue's "no silent gaps after day 1" acceptance criterion). Follow-up [#399](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/399) shipped the CI auto-regen check — the `check-build-test` job in [.github/workflows/ci.yml](.github/workflows/ci.yml) runs `vp run integ-coverage` and `git diff --quiet`-fails when the regenerated output drifts from the committed `docs/integ-coverage.md` / `docs/_generated/integ-coverage.json`, so a forgotten regeneration is a CI hard-fail rather than a soft `/verify-pr` skill-step warning.

- ✅ RDS DBProxy family: drift `--revert` round-trip audit + new `RDSDBProxyTargetGroupProvider.readCurrentState`. Closes the deferred drift audit from PRs #394 / #400 / #406. **New readCurrentState** on `RDSDBProxyTargetGroupProvider` ([src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-targetgroup-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-targetgroup-provider.ts)) reverse-maps `DescribeDBProxyTargetGroups` (for `ConnectionPoolConfigurationInfo`) + `DescribeDBProxyTargetsCommand` (for `DBClusterIdentifiers` / `DBInstanceIdentifiers`, reverse-mapped from the AWS-side target list via the `Type` discriminator) to CFn property shape. Pre-PR the provider had no `readCurrentState` → drift comparator fell back to CC API → CC API is broken on this type (Issue #385 the SDK provider was added to fix in the first place). `DBProxyNotFoundFault` / `DBProxyTargetGroupNotFoundFault` return `undefined` (resource gone — drift comparator skips). **Round-trip audit**: 13 new unit tests across `tests/unit/provisioning/rds-dbproxy-{,endpoint-,targetgroup-}provider*.test.ts` verifying that `update()` correctly round-trips the readCurrentState shape during `cdkd drift --revert`. Each provider has three scenarios: (1) identical observed-shape on both sides → no SDK call (the comparator's "non-drifted top-level keys carry AWS-current values" invariant); (2) drifted scalar field (RoleArn / VpcSecurityGroupIds / ConnectionPoolConfig) round-trips through the appropriate Modify\* SDK call with the desired value; (3) drifted Tags round-trip through `AddTagsToResource` with the desired tag set. Plus 4 new `readCurrentState` tests for DBProxyTargetGroup (full reverse-map / corrupted-state guard / parent-gone idempotent / pool-config-omitted fallback). **No shape mismatches found in the audit** — the existing readCurrentState reverse-mappings on DBProxy / DBProxyEndpoint already match what `update()` accepts as `previousProperties`, so drift `--revert` works for the full family without code changes beyond the new TargetGroup readCurrentState.

- ✅ Follow-up to PR #397 (`AWS::DynamoDB::GlobalTable`): closes all 8 remaining deferred items from PRs #384 / #388 / #393 / #397 (Issue #402). **Item A (functional)**: new `applyAutoScalingDiff(tableName, dimension, oldSettings, newSettings, client?)` helper in [src/provisioning/providers/dynamodb-globaltable-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/dynamodb-globaltable-provider.ts) issues `RegisterScalableTarget` + `PutScalingPolicy` (PolicyType `TargetTrackingScaling`, AWS-canonical policy names `DynamoDB{Write,Read}CapacityUtilization:table/<table-name>`) on autoscaling add / modify, and `DeleteScalingPolicy` + `DeregisterScalableTarget` on remove. Idempotent-upsert semantics — `RegisterScalableTarget` accepts no-op Min/Max changes silently; `PutScalingPolicy` is upsert on the same policy name. Best-effort: AWS errors log at WARN with the exact `aws application-autoscaling ...` recovery command and the deploy continues (matches the cross-region Tags propagation contract from PR #393). Wired into 4 sites in `update()`: (1) table-level write dimension AFTER the BillingMode flip (so a PAY_PER_REQUEST → PROVISIONED + new autoscaling templates don't try to Register against a not-yet-PROVISIONED table), (2) per-replica modify path's read dimension via the regional autoscaling client, (3) per-replica added path's read dimension, (4) per-replica removed path's read dimension (explicit teardown before `ReplicaUpdates: Delete` so a future re-add of the same region doesn't collide on a stranded scaling target). **Force-teardown on PROVISIONED → PAY_PER_REQUEST flip** is load-bearing: AWS rejects autoscaling targets on on-demand tables, so any prior target must come down regardless of whether the (now-invalid) template still carries the settings. `SeedCapacity` is intentionally NOT forwarded — it is a CFn create-only field with no `RegisterScalableTarget` surface (and `readAutoScalingSettings` already skips it). **Items E / F / G / H (unit tests)**: Kinesis `ENABLING`-status filter (`readReplicaSubSpecs` accepts ACTIVE OR ENABLING), multi-destination ACTIVE disambiguation (picks the first ACTIVE destination per the CFn per-replica `{StreamArn}` shape), `replicaArnForRegion` defensive `undefined` return on malformed ARN (< 6 colon-segments), and `delete()` `--remove-protection` flip-off-success → DeleteTable-RNF → region-mismatch refuses idempotency. 14 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/dynamodb-globaltable-provider-roundtrip.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/dynamodb-globaltable-provider-roundtrip.test.ts) (97 total, was 83). **Items B / C / D (real-AWS integ)**: [tests/integration/dynamodb-globaltable/](tests/integration/dynamodb-globaltable/) fixture extended with `CDKD_TEST_UPDATE=autoscaling` (read AND write `Capacity.autoscaled` via the canonical CDK 2.x shape verified via real `cdk synth` probe — `WriteProvisionedThroughputSettings.WriteCapacityAutoScalingSettings: {MinCapacity, MaxCapacity, TargetTrackingScalingPolicyConfiguration: {TargetValue}}` and per-replica `ReadProvisionedThroughputSettings.ReadCapacityAutoScalingSettings`) and `CDKD_TEST_UPDATE=cross-region` (adds eu-west-1 replica). `verify.sh` exercises a full round-trip: baseline → ttl/tags → deletion-protection → billing-provisioned → autoscaling (asserts `aws application-autoscaling describe-scaling-policies` reports a `TargetTrackingScaling` policy with `TargetValue=70`) → cleared baseline (asserts policy is GONE) → destroy. **Item D (cross-region) gated behind `CDKD_INTEG_MULTI_REGION=1`** so the default `bash verify.sh` invocation stays under 8 min (cross-region adds ~15-25 min + ~$0.10-0.20 in cross-region replication). When opted in, asserts replica add → `DescribeTable` against eu-west-1 succeeds → replica remove → eu-west-1 RNF.

- ✅ New SDK Provider: `AWS::RDS::DBProxyEndpoint` — completes the RDS DBProxy family (DBProxy + DBProxyEndpoint + DBProxyTargetGroup all on the dedicated-SDK-provider path now). Pre-PR DBProxyEndpoint went through CC API; consolidating to a dedicated provider matches the sibling DBProxy / DBProxyTargetGroup providers added in PR #387 / #394 and lets future changes (drift handling, partial-create cleanup) evolve across the whole family in one place. New file [src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-endpoint-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-endpoint-provider.ts) implements the full lifecycle: **create** validates required `DBProxyName` + `VpcSubnetIds`, issues `CreateDBProxyEndpointCommand`, then polls `DescribeDBProxyEndpoints` every 5s until `Status === 'available'` (15 min cap; terminal `incompatible-network` / `insufficient-resource-limits` fail fast). Returns `physicalId = DBProxyEndpointName` plus `Endpoint` / `DBProxyEndpointArn` / `IsDefault` / `VpcId` in `attributes`. **update** issues `ModifyDBProxyEndpointCommand` for `VpcSecurityGroupIds` diff (the only structurally-mutable field on AWS — DBProxyName / VpcSubnetIds / TargetRole are immutable, replacement-detection handles); Tags diff via separate `AddTagsToResource` / `RemoveTagsFromResource` calls with a load-bearing tag-map equality short-circuit BEFORE the ARN-lookup Describe call (closes the wasted-Describe minor that PR #394 review surfaced — applied here in the new code from day 1 rather than retrofitted). **delete** calls `DeleteDBProxyEndpointCommand` + polls until `DBProxyEndpointNotFoundFault`. Both `DBProxyEndpointNotFoundFault` AND `DBProxyNotFoundFault` (parent gone via CASCADE) are treated as idempotent success (region-match gated). **getAttribute** resolves the 4 attributes via `DescribeDBProxyEndpoints`, cached per `(physicalId, attribute)`. **import** is explicit `--resource <id>=<DBProxyEndpointName>` first; falls back to paginated auto-lookup via `DescribeDBProxyEndpoints` + `ListTagsForResource` matched against `aws:cdk:path`. **readCurrentState** reverse-maps DescribeDBProxyEndpoints + ListTagsForResource to CFn property shape so drift detection works on the SDK-provider path (was CC-API fallback pre-PR); emits `TargetRole = 'READ_WRITE'` AWS default when the field is omitted. 23 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/rds-dbproxy-endpoint-provider.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/rds-dbproxy-endpoint-provider.test.ts). Registered in [src/provisioning/register-providers.ts](src/provisioning/register-providers.ts) alongside the other RDS provider entries.

- ✅ Docs fix: CLAUDE.md "Provider Pattern" `interface ResourceProvider` example block. Pre-fix the prose example documented `update(physicalId, logicalId, ...)` / `delete(physicalId, logicalId, ...)` / `getAttribute(physicalId, logicalId, ...)`, which contradicted the actual `src/types/resource.ts` interface declaration (`update(logicalId, physicalId, ...)`, `delete(logicalId, physicalId, ...)`, `getAttribute(physicalId, resourceType, ...)`). PR #387 round 1 review caught the signature mismatch as a blocker in the new DBProxyTargetGroup provider — the prose was the silent source of the trap. Fixed prose to mirror the source-of-truth.

- ✅ Follow-up to PR #384 (`AWS::DynamoDB::GlobalTable`): complete provider coverage — closes the MVP scope caveats from the previous bullet. **In-place `update()`** now covers every mutable surface (replaces the previous `ResourceUpdateNotSupportedError` stub) — Tags, DeletionProtection, TableClass, SSE, StreamSpec, OnDemand throughput, BillingMode flip, Replica add / remove / modify, GSI add / remove / modify, TimeToLive toggle, with immutable-field guards on TableName / KeySchema / AttributeDefinitions removals / LocalSecondaryIndexes. **AWS state-machine constraint** is load-bearing: `UpdateTableCommand` accepts only ONE of `{BillingMode, ReplicaUpdates, GlobalSecondaryIndexUpdates}` per call, so the update flow SERIALIZES each category into its own SDK round-trip with a `waitForTableActiveAfterUpdate` between every step. Order: (1) wait for current ACTIVE (defensive), (2) Tags diff via `TagResource` / `UntagResource` (no UpdateTable, no wait), (3) non-conflicting flat fields (DeletionProtectionEnabled / TableClass / SSE / Stream / OnDemand) in one combined `UpdateTableCommand`, (4) BillingMode flip in its own UpdateTable (PROVISIONED ↔ PAY_PER_REQUEST with derived ProvisionedThroughput via the new shared `derivePerCallProvisionedThroughput()` helper — defaults match `create()` so PAY_PER_REQUEST templates with no explicit BillingMode no longer false-fire a flip), (5) Replica diff via serial Delete-then-Add-then-Update with wait-for-ACTIVE / wait-for-gone (Tags-only cross-region modifies skip the empty UpdateReplica that AWS would reject), (6) GSI diff via serial Delete-then-Add-then-Update (Add merges AttributeDefinitions in the same UpdateTable call), (7) TimeToLive toggle via `UpdateTimeToLiveCommand` (Enabled=false uses the previous AttributeName on disable). New pure-functional helpers `diffReplicas(old, new)` + `diffGlobalSecondaryIndexes(old, new)` + `derivePerCallProvisionedThroughput(props, region)` exported for testing. **Per-replica drift surfacing** for the LOCAL replica only: `readCurrentState` now reverse-maps `ContributorInsightsSpecification` (via `DescribeContributorInsightsCommand` → `{Enabled: bool}`), `PointInTimeRecoverySpecification` (via `DescribeContinuousBackupsCommand` → `{PointInTimeRecoveryEnabled: bool}`), and `KinesisStreamSpecification` (via `DescribeKinesisStreamingDestinationCommand` — first ACTIVE / ENABLING destination's `StreamArn` + optional `ApproximateCreationDateTimePrecision`). Cross-region replicas get `undefined` for these in v1 (would need per-region SDK clients — deferred follow-up); each sub-spec call is best-effort, omitting the offending key on error rather than failing the whole drift read. **Tags shape correction** (load-bearing): the CFn `AWS::DynamoDB::GlobalTable` schema has NO top-level `Tags` — Tags live inside each `Replicas[].Tags` entry (CDK's `cdk.Tags.of(tableV2).add(...)` synthesizes there). `create()` / `update()` / `readCurrentState()` / `handledProperties` all corrected to the per-replica shape (real-AWS integ caught a Tags-update silently failing because of the top-level vs per-replica mismatch). **TimeToLiveSpecification round-trip**: removed from `getDriftUnknownPaths`; `readCurrentState` now calls `DescribeTimeToLiveCommand` and reverse-maps to `{AttributeName, Enabled: true}` when AWS reports `ENABLED`; transient `UPDATING` / `DISABLING` statuses omit the key (race-tolerant). Only `WriteProvisionedThroughputSettings` + `WriteOnDemandThroughputSettings` remain in the deny-list (auto-scaling reverse-mapping non-trivial). **PR #384 review nits addressed**: `waitFor*` helpers now throw `ProvisioningError` with `resourceType` + `logicalId` parity (not bare `Error`); misleading "Replica may already be gone" comment in `delete()` rewritten to "Table itself already gone — outer DeleteTable will handle idempotency"; `attributeCache` field gets an explicit invalidation-contract docstring; tag-fetch silent swallow now logs at WARN; stale "MVP" docstring rewritten; `readCurrentState` docstring no longer claims billing-mode-gating for ProvisionedThroughput. **PR #388 review fixes** (3-axis review caught a real bug class): (1) **partial-create cleanup leak** — pre-fix, cleanup issued a bare `DeleteTable` which AWS rejects on a multi-replica table (orphaning the just-added replica). Cleanup now mirrors `delete()`: `DescribeTable` + per-region Delete ReplicaUpdates + waitForReplicaGone + `DeleteTable`. (2) **BillingMode default skew** — `update()` defaulted missing BillingMode to PROVISIONED while `create()` defaulted to PAY_PER_REQUEST, false-firing a flip diff on every redeploy of a PAY_PER_REQUEST template; both sides now default to PAY_PER_REQUEST. (3) Cross-region replica with Tags-only diff used to issue an empty `UpdateReplica` (AWS rejects with ValidationException); detected and skipped now. (4) Hardcoded `ReadCapacityUnits: 5` on BillingMode flip replaced with the shared helper. (5) Double `config.region()` resolution and `replicas` variable shadowing removed. **34 new unit tests** in [tests/unit/provisioning/dynamodb-globaltable-provider-roundtrip.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/dynamodb-globaltable-provider-roundtrip.test.ts) (now 64 total) + 1 new in [partial-create-cleanup test](tests/unit/provisioning/dynamodb-globaltable-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts) (now 6 total): update-path tests (Tags / flat fields / BillingMode flip / Replica add+remove+modify / TTL toggle + disable / GSI Create+Delete+Modify / Tags-only-cross-region-skip / immutable-field rejections / strict no-op assertion / BillingMode-default-no-flip regression) + diff-helper unit tests + PROVISIONED-create derivation + readCurrentState drift coverage gaps (SSE-enabled / DeletionProtectionEnabled / Replica-Tags placeholder) + TTL round-trip tests + per-replica sub-spec tests + delete-path edge tests (`waitForReplicaGone` poll loop / non-RNF DescribeTable → ProvisioningError) + create-per-replica-Tags wire-up regression + partial-create-cleanup-drops-replicas-first regression. **Integ extension** at [tests/integration/dynamodb-globaltable/](tests/integration/dynamodb-globaltable/): new `CDKD_TEST_UPDATE` env var on the fixture stack mutates `TableV2` props (`ttl` / `tags` / `deletion-protection` / `billing-provisioned`); `verify.sh` now exercises a second `cdkd deploy` with `CDKD_TEST_UPDATE=ttl,tags` between baseline deploy and destroy, asserting `describe-time-to-live` reports ENABLED and `list-tags-of-resource` carries the `UpdateTest=true` user tag (real-AWS validated 2026-05-16).

- ✅ Fix: `RDSProvider` wait budgets bumped from 10 min to 30 min — surfaced during the rds-aurora integ destroy on 2026-05-16 where `waitForInstanceDeleted` timed out at 10 min on an Aurora writer instance whose AWS-side delete genuinely took ~12 min (Aurora writer delete latency varies by region + account quota state; the AWS-side delete is correctly executing, it's only cdkd's poll budget that was too short). cdkd state was preserved + the user saw `PartialFailureError` exit 2 even though AWS was clean within a few more minutes.
