Affected 4 wait helpers in [src/provisioning/providers/rds-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/rds-provider.ts): `waitForClusterAvailable` / `waitForClusterDeleted` / `waitForInstanceAvailable` / `waitForInstanceDeleted` — all bumped from `maxWaitMs = 600_000` (10 min) to `1_800_000` (30 min). Matches the existing 30 min budget already in [docdb-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/docdb-provider.ts) and [neptune-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/neptune-provider.ts) — the inconsistency had been an oversight from when those sibling providers were added later under a more conservative timeout. No new tests needed (the wait helpers are private and exercised end-to-end by the integ).

- ✅ New SDK Provider: `AWS::RDS::DBProxy` + in-place update support for `AWS::RDS::DBProxyTargetGroup` — completes the RDS DBProxy family started in PR #387 ([Issue #385](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/385)). **DBProxy provider** in [src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-provider.ts) mirrors the structural pattern of the existing `RDSProvider` but covers a single CFn type: **create** validates required CFn properties (`EngineFamily` / `Auth` non-empty / `RoleArn` / `VpcSubnetIds`), issues `CreateDBProxyCommand`, then polls `DescribeDBProxies` every 5s until `Status === 'available'` (bounded by 15 min — Aurora DBProxy provisioning typically takes 1-3 min in practice; terminal statuses `incompatible-network` / `insufficient-resource-limits` fail fast); on success returns `physicalId = DBProxyName` plus `Endpoint` / `DBProxyArn` / `VpcId` in `attributes`. **update** issues `ModifyDBProxyCommand` only when one or more mutable fields diff (`Auth` / `RequireTLS` / `IdleClientTimeout` / `DebugLogging` / `RoleArn` / `VpcSecurityGroupIds`) — the CFn property `VpcSecurityGroupIds` is translated to the SDK input field `SecurityGroups` at the wire layer. **Tags diff** is applied via separate `AddTagsToResourceCommand` / `RemoveTagsFromResourceCommand` calls (the proxy ARN is recovered + cached for these). EngineFamily and VpcSubnetIds are immutable on AWS; the deploy engine's replacement-detection layer should catch diffs upstream. **delete** calls `DeleteDBProxyCommand`, then polls `DescribeDBProxies` until `DBProxyNotFoundFault` (AWS keeps the proxy in `deleting` state for ~30-60s after the API returns; bounded by 15 min). `DBProxyNotFoundFault` at any point treated as idempotent success (region-match gated via the shared `assertRegionMatch` helper). **getAttribute** resolves `Endpoint` / `DBProxyArn` / `VpcId` via `DescribeDBProxies`, cached per `(physicalId, attribute)`. **import** is explicit `--resource <id>=<DBProxyName>` first; falls back to paginated auto-lookup via `DescribeDBProxies` + per-proxy `ListTagsForResource` matched against `aws:cdk:path`. **readCurrentState** reverse-maps `DescribeDBProxies` + `ListTagsForResource` to the CFn property shape so drift detection works on the SDK-provider path (was CC-API fallback pre-PR). 24 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/rds-dbproxy-provider.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/rds-dbproxy-provider.test.ts). **DBProxyTargetGroup in-place update** in [src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-targetgroup-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-targetgroup-provider.ts) replaces the `ResourceUpdateNotSupportedError` MVP-stub from PR #387: target add/remove via `RegisterDBProxyTargets` / `DeregisterDBProxyTargets` (cluster + instance identifiers independently; `DBProxyTargetNotFoundFault` on deregister is idempotent, same shape as delete()) and connection-pool config rewrite via `ModifyDBProxyTargetGroupCommand`. Same `DBProxyName` / `TargetGroupName` immutability semantics as create — those fields are part of identity, a diff surfaces as replacement upstream. 5 new unit tests on the update path (DBProxyName-required rejection / no-op when unchanged / Modify on pool-config diff / register added + deregister removed clusters / DBProxyTargetNotFoundFault idempotent). `register-providers.ts` wires both providers under their respective resource types. Real-AWS validated via `/run-integ rds-aurora` (deploy + destroy clean, including the IndirectPort SG ingress that originally surfaced [#381](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/381) and the AuroraProxyProxyTargetGroup destroy that originally surfaced #385). Follow-up scope: `AWS::RDS::DBProxyEndpoint` SDK provider (currently goes through CC API, separate concern from the DBProxy + TargetGroup family); per-property mutability matrix audit for drift `--revert` round-trip.

- ✅ New SDK Provider: `AWS::RDS::DBProxyTargetGroup` — closes [Issue #385](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/385). Pre-PR this type went through Cloud Control API, but CC API's resource handler for `AWS::RDS::DBProxyTargetGroup` fails the delete path with `Value null at 'dBProxyName' failed to satisfy constraint: Member must not be null (Service: Rds, Status Code: 400)` — the handler cannot derive `DBProxyName` from the TargetGroup ARN (the primary identifier per CFn schema) so the underlying `DeregisterDBProxyTargets` API call goes out with `DBProxyName: null` and AWS rejects it. Surfaced during the Issue #381 rds-aurora integ destroy run (the parent DBProxy deleted successfully, but its TargetGroup wiring resource failed and cdkd reported `PartialFailureError` exit 2 even though the AWS-side CASCADE delete cleaned up the target group anyway). Per memory rule `feedback_dedicated_provider_over_special_case.md` the fix is a dedicated SDK Provider (not a `cloud-control-provider.ts` special-case). New file [src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-targetgroup-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/rds-dbproxy-targetgroup-provider.ts) implements the type: **create** optionally `ModifyDBProxyTargetGroupCommand` (when `ConnectionPoolConfigurationInfo` is set) → `RegisterDBProxyTargetsCommand` (with `DBClusterIdentifiers` / `DBInstanceIdentifiers`) → `DescribeDBProxyTargetGroupsCommand` to recover the TargetGroupArn for state; **update** throws `ResourceUpdateNotSupportedError` in MVP (the per-property surface — add/remove targets, pool config rewrites — is a follow-up); **delete** reads `DBProxyName` + targets from `state.properties` and issues `DeregisterDBProxyTargetsCommand`, treating `DBProxyNotFoundFault` / `DBProxyTargetGroupNotFoundFault` / `DBProxyTargetNotFoundFault` as idempotent success (region-match-gated via the shared `assertRegionMatch` helper) — the parent DBProxy may already be gone by AWS CASCADE or by a sibling cdkd delete. **What this resource actually does on AWS**: every DBProxy gets a default TargetGroup (`TargetGroupName: 'default'`) auto-created by AWS; the CFn resource only manages target REGISTRATIONS and the connection-pool config — the TargetGroup object itself is not deleted on resource delete, it lives and dies with the parent DBProxy. **getAttribute** returns the TargetGroupArn for `'TargetGroupArn'` and `'default'` for `'TargetGroupName'`. **import** is explicit-override-only (the TargetGroup has no tags — the parent DBProxy carries the cdkd `aws:cdk:path` tag, not the wiring child). Registered in [src/provisioning/register-providers.ts](src/provisioning/register-providers.ts) alongside the existing RDS provider entries. 20 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/rds-dbproxy-targetgroup-provider.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/rds-dbproxy-targetgroup-provider.test.ts) covering: handledProperties shape / create with cluster targets + Describe recovery / create with ConnectionPoolConfig ordering / DBProxyName-required rejection / Describe-returned-empty rejection / no-targets create skips Register / update-rejection / delete with cluster IDs / DBProxyNotFoundFault idempotent / DBProxyTargetGroupNotFoundFault idempotent / DBProxyTargetNotFoundFault idempotent / no-targets delete is no-op / DBProxyName-missing-from-state rejection / region-mismatch surfaces ProvisioningError / non-NotFound errors propagate / getAttribute TargetGroupArn / getAttribute TargetGroupName / getAttribute unknown returns undefined / import with knownPhysicalId / import without knownPhysicalId returns null. Real-AWS destroy validation deferred to a follow-up PR (`/run-integ rds-aurora` end-to-end with this fix). Follow-up scope: dedicated `AWS::RDS::DBProxy` provider too (currently working via CC API but at family-consistency risk); in-place update support for DBProxyTargetGroup (add/remove targets, pool config rewrites).

- ✅ New SDK Provider: `AWS::DynamoDB::GlobalTable` (CDK v2 `dynamodb.TableV2`) — closes [Issue #383](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/383). Pre-PR a `new dynamodb.TableV2(this, 'X', { partitionKey })` (no explicit `tableName`) synthesized as `AWS::DynamoDB::GlobalTable` and fell through to Cloud Control API, which did NOT receive a `TableName` field — so AWS auto-generated random names like `yq2phLewTEUtzr4sy2gYFRU4I-1OGJ0UFLOKOOV` instead of cdkd's canonical `${stackName}-X<hash>` shape. Per memory rule `feedback_dedicated_provider_over_special_case.md` the correct fix is a dedicated SDK Provider (not adding the type to `FALLBACK_NAME_RULES`). New file [src/provisioning/providers/dynamodb-globaltable-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/dynamodb-globaltable-provider.ts) mirrors the structural shape of `DynamoDBTableProvider` but uses the **2019.11.21 DynamoDB API generation** (regular `CreateTableCommand` + `UpdateTableCommand` with `ReplicaUpdates`, NOT the legacy 2017.11.29 `CreateGlobalTableCommand` endpoints which are incompatible with the CFn type). Coverage: **create** generates the table name via `generateResourceName(logicalId, { maxLength: 255 })`, calls `CreateTableCommand`, polls until `ACTIVE`, then issues one `UpdateTableCommand(ReplicaUpdates: [{Create: {...}}])` SERIALLY per non-local replica region (AWS rejects multiple replica updates per call), waits for each replica's `ReplicaStatus=ACTIVE`, applies `TimeToLiveSpecification` via `UpdateTimeToLiveCommand`, and surfaces `Arn` / `StreamArn` / `TableId` in `attributes`. Auto-enables `StreamSpecification: { StreamViewType: 'NEW_AND_OLD_IMAGES' }` (with an info log) when the template has cross-region replicas but didn't opt into streams explicitly — AWS rejects cross-region replication otherwise. **Partial-create cleanup** (PR #374-class): every post-`CreateTableCommand` wiring call is wrapped in an inner try/catch that issues a best-effort `DeleteTableCommand` before re-throwing, so a wait-for-active failure or a replica-add failure does not leave a billing AWS-side orphan with no cdkd state record. Cleanup-step failures escalate to WARN with the `aws dynamodb delete-table --table-name <id>` recovery command. **delete** runs the inverse: optional `--remove-protection` flip-off (`UpdateTableCommand(DeletionProtectionEnabled: false)` with wait-for-active), `DescribeTable` to find non-local replicas, one `UpdateTableCommand(ReplicaUpdates: [{Delete: {RegionName}}])` per replica with wait-for-gone, then `DeleteTableCommand` on the local region only. DELETE idempotency is region-match-gated via the shared `assertRegionMatch` helper. **update** throws `ResourceUpdateNotSupportedError` in MVP (the per-property update surface — replica add/remove, GSI add/remove, BillingMode flip, throughput rewrites — is a follow-up). **getAttribute** resolves `Arn` / `StreamArn` / `TableId` from `DescribeTable` with a `(physicalId, attribute)` cache per provider instance. **readCurrentState** reverse-maps `DescribeTable` + `ListTagsOfResource` to CFn property shape with type-discriminator-gated placeholders per memory rule `feedback_always_emit_check_type_discriminator.md` — Class 1 guards keep CFn-invalid placeholders (`StreamSpecification` without `StreamViewType`, `SSESpecification` with `SSEEnabled: false`) off the wire; Class 2 guards keep empty-`[]` GSI / LSI placeholders off (which would round-trip as "remove all GSIs"). `Replicas` and `Tags` are always-emitted (`[]` placeholder) per PR #145 pattern so console-side replica adds / tag adds show as drift on the v3 observedProperties baseline. **getDriftUnknownPaths** declares `TimeToLiveSpecification` + `WriteProvisionedThroughputSettings` + `WriteOnDemandThroughputSettings` as drift-unknown in v1 (the create path applies them but the reverse-mapping is non-trivial and would fire false drift). **import** uses `resolveExplicitPhysicalId(input, 'TableName')` + DescribeTable verify on override, falls back to paginated `ListTablesCommand` + per-table `DescribeTable` + `ListTagsOfResourceCommand` matched against `aws:cdk:path`. Wired into [src/provisioning/register-providers.ts](src/provisioning/register-providers.ts) and added to `PROTECTION_PROPERTY_BY_TYPE` in [src/cli/commands/destroy-runner.ts](src/cli/commands/destroy-runner.ts) so `--remove-protection` counts protected GlobalTable resources. The pre-existing `IntrinsicFunctionResolver.constructAttribute()` Arn handler already covered `AWS::DynamoDB::GlobalTable` (returns the same `arn:${partition}:dynamodb:${region}:${accountId}:table/${physicalId}` shape as `Table`); the `StreamArn` branch returns `undefined` in the resolver so downstream `Fn::GetAtt` resolution falls through to the provider's `getAttribute`, which now does the real `DescribeTable.LatestStreamArn` lookup. 29 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/dynamodb-globaltable-provider-roundtrip.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/dynamodb-globaltable-provider-roundtrip.test.ts) covering handledProperties shape / create with single-region + auto-stream-enable on cross-region + explicit TableName + replica adds + TTL application + missing-KeySchema/AttributeDefinitions rejection / update-rejection / delete with replica teardown + region-match guard + --remove-protection flow / getAttribute Arn+StreamArn+TableId+cache+unknown / readCurrentState reverse-mapping with always-emit Replicas+Tags + Class 1 guards + RNF-returns-undefined / getDriftUnknownPaths declaration / import explicit-override + auto-mode tag matching. 5 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/dynamodb-globaltable-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/dynamodb-globaltable-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts) covering cleanup-fires-on-waitForActive-failure / no-cleanup-when-CreateTable-itself-fails / cleanup-itself-fails-propagates-original-error-with-WARN+recovery-command / cleanup-also-fires-on-replica-add-failure / CreateTableCommand-first-call-sanity. Real-AWS integ scaffold at [tests/integration/dynamodb-globaltable/](tests/integration/dynamodb-globaltable/) deploys a `dynamodb.TableV2` with pk+sk + PAY_PER_REQUEST + single replica (deploy region) + `RemovalPolicy.DESTROY`, then asserts the deployed AWS table name starts with `${StackName}-` (closes the reported user bug) before destroy. MVP scope: in-place update is deferred; per-replica drift (`ContributorInsightsSpecification` / `PointInTimeRecoverySpecification` / `KinesisStreamSpecification`) is deferred; the read-side `WriteProvisionedThroughputSettings` reverse-mapping is deferred via `getDriftUnknownPaths`.

- ✅ Fix: `IntrinsicFunctionResolver.resolveGetAtt` now falls back to a nested attribute-path walk when the flat dot-key lookup misses (closes [Issue #381](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/381)). Pre-fix, `Fn::GetAtt: [<RDSCluster>, 'Endpoint.Port']` would silently fall through to `constructAttribute`'s default `return physicalId` and produce errors like `Invalid integer value rdsaurorastack-auroracluster23d869c0` downstream — the canonical user-visible trigger is CDK's `Connections.allowDefaultPortFrom(...)` pattern emitting `AWS::EC2::SecurityGroupIngress` "IndirectPort" rules that read the cluster's port via `Fn::GetAtt`. The root cause was a shape mismatch between SDK providers (which store nested attrs as **flat dot-keys**, e.g. `attributes['Endpoint.Port'] = '3306'`) and the **CC API fallback** (which stores nested attrs as actual nested objects, e.g. `attributes.Endpoint.Port = 3306`). The resolver only looked up flat dot-keys. When a resource flips to the CC API fallback path (e.g. RDSProvider falls back when the template has `CopyTagsToSnapshot` / `DBClusterParameterGroupName` — properties not in `handledProperties`), the resulting state has nested-object attributes and the flat-key lookup misses → physicalId default fallback → AWS gets the wrong value. Fix in [src/deployment/intrinsic-function-resolver.ts](src/deployment/intrinsic-function-resolver.ts) `resolveGetAtt`: after the existing flat-key lookup misses AND the attribute name contains `.`, walk the dot-separated path against the `attributes` object before falling through to `constructAttribute`. Flat-key still wins (SDK providers unaffected); nested-path walk is purely additive for CC API stored attributes. Handles 2-level nesting (`Endpoint.Port`) and deeper paths (`A.B.C`), gracefully fails on intermediate non-objects (string-typed intermediate falls through cleanly without TypeError). 5 new unit tests in [tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-functions.test.ts](tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-functions.test.ts) covering: flat-key wins / nested-walk fallback (Endpoint.Port + Endpoint.Address) / fall through to constructAttribute when neither matches / 3+ level nesting / intermediate non-object safety. Real-AWS regression validated via `/run-integ rds-aurora` (2026-05-16): deploy succeeded end-to-end with the canonical IndirectPort SG ingress rule (the user-visible trigger from #381) created cleanly — no "Invalid integer value" error. Destroy hit a pre-existing unrelated DBProxyTargetGroup bug (`DBProxyName must not be null`), filed as separate follow-up [#385](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/385).

- ✅ Fix: Apply the PR #374 partial-create-cleanup pattern to `RDSProvider.createDBCluster` (Batch Database of Issue #376's 14-provider sweep — the final 1 of 14). Same canonical shape as PRs #377 / #378 / #379 / #380: once `CreateDBClusterCommand` returns, AWS has committed the cluster and BILLING HAS STARTED (Aurora minimum ~$0.07/hour idle). If `waitForClusterAvailable` (the **poll-failure case** specifically called out in Issue #376) times out — or AWS reports `CREATE_FAILED` via the waiter — the cluster keeps running until manual cleanup. The fix wraps the post-create wiring (`waitForClusterAvailable` + `describeDBCluster`) in an inner try/catch that issues best-effort `ModifyDBClusterCommand(DeletionProtection: false, ApplyImmediately: true)` (only when the template requested protection — AWS rejects `DeleteDBCluster` on protected clusters) + `DeleteDBClusterCommand(SkipFinalSnapshot: true)` before re-throwing the original error. Same UX choice as EC2 `createInstance` (PR #379): **do NOT wait for the cluster to fully delete** — the deploy is already failing, making the user wait another 5-30 min on RDS's eventual termination is bad UX. When cleanup itself fails, the WARN escalates to `THE CLUSTER IS STILL RUNNING AND BILLING` with the exact `aws rds modify-db-cluster --no-deletion-protection` + `aws rds delete-db-cluster --skip-final-snapshot` recovery commands. The "AWS returned success but no DBCluster" theoretical edge case gets a one-line comment mirroring the EC2 Instance / SNS Topic / ELBv2 LB precedent. 5 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/rds-dbcluster-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/rds-dbcluster-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts) covering: cleanup fires on waiter failure → `Delete` issued without wait; cleanup flips `DeletionProtection` off before delete when template requested protection; no cleanup when `CreateDBCluster` itself fails; cleanup itself fails → original error propagates with `THE CLUSTER IS STILL RUNNING AND BILLING` WARN; the WARN includes the `modify-db-cluster --no-deletion-protection` recovery command when protection was templated. Test stubs `RDSProvider.waitForClusterAvailable` via a method-replacement on the instance because it's a private polling helper not bound to `mockSend`. **Issue #376 closed**: all 5 batches (Storage / IAM / EC2 / Messaging / Database) shipped — 14 of 14 provider create methods now self-heal on partial-create failure.

- ✅ Fix: Apply the PR #374 partial-create-cleanup pattern to `EventBridgeRuleProvider.create`, `SNSTopicProvider.create`, and `ELBv2Provider.createLoadBalancer` (Batch Messaging of Issue #376's 14-provider sweep — 3 of the remaining 4 providers). Same canonical shape as PRs #377 / #378 / #379: once the first `CreateTopicCommand` / `PutRuleCommand` / `CreateLoadBalancerCommand` returns, AWS has committed the resource; if a subsequent wiring call (`PutTargets` / `SetTopicAttributes` for ArchivePolicy or DataProtectionPolicy or DeliveryStatusLogging / `ModifyLoadBalancerAttributes`) throws, cdkd state has nothing recorded but AWS does. Each cleanup follows the corresponding `delete()` method's order: **EventBridge** — `ListTargetsByRule` → `RemoveTargets` (if any) → `DeleteRule` (mirrors `delete()`); the cleanup re-lists targets because PutTargets may have partially succeeded before throwing, and AWS rejects `DeleteRule` when targets are still attached. EventBusName is threaded through every cleanup call so non-default-bus rules are handled correctly. **SNS** — single `DeleteTopicCommand`. SNS has an **idempotent-create wrinkle** unlike S3/Logs: `CreateTopicCommand` does NOT throw on pre-existing topics (no `BucketAlreadyOwnedByYou` / `ResourceAlreadyExistsException` equivalent) — it silently returns the existing ARN. So cdkd cannot distinguish "we created this" vs "we adopted a pre-existing topic", which matches the existing `delete()` behavior (always deletes). Known limitation: if a user has a pre-existing topic with the same name AND a wiring step fails on first deploy, cdkd will delete the pre-existing topic. Same semantics as the existing destroy code; the new cleanup doesn't make it worse and is documented inline. **ELBv2 LB** — single `DeleteLoadBalancerCommand`. `CreateLoadBalancer` rejects duplicate Names with `DuplicateLoadBalancerName` so no idempotent flag needed; a freshly-created LB has no listeners or target-group attachments yet so a single Delete suffices. The "AWS returned success but no ARN" theoretical path in `createLoadBalancer` (mirror of EC2 Instance's empty-Instances-array case) gets a one-line comment documenting that no cleanup is possible. 10 new unit tests across [tests/unit/provisioning/{eventbridge-rule,sns-topic,elbv2-loadbalancer}-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/): EventBridge has 4 (the canonical 3 + an extra "ListTargets returns empty → only DeleteRule" case to cover the all-or-nothing PutTargets failure mode); SNS and ELBv2 have 3 each. ELBv2 test mocks `ElasticLoadBalancingV2Client` directly via `vi.mock('@aws-sdk/client-elastic-load-balancing-v2', ...)` because ELBv2Provider builds its own client rather than going through `getAwsClients()` (mirroring the existing `elbv2-provider-roundtrip.test.ts` pattern). Issue #376 progress: Batches Storage / IAM / EC2 / Messaging shipped; **only Batch Database (`RDSProvider.createDBCluster`) remains**.

- ✅ Fix: Apply the PR #374 partial-create-cleanup pattern to `EC2Provider.createVpc`, `EC2Provider.createSubnet`, `EC2Provider.createSecurityGroup`, and `EC2Provider.createInstance` (Batch EC2 of Issue #376's 14-provider sweep — 4 of the remaining 7 providers). Same canonical shape as PR #377 (Storage) and PR #378 (IAM): once the first `Create*Command` / `RunInstancesCommand` returns, AWS has committed the resource; if a subsequent wiring call (DNS attribute / `applyTags` / `ModifySubnetAttribute` / `Authorize*` / `Revoke*` / `waitUntilInstanceRunning` / `DescribeInstances`) throws, cdkd state has nothing recorded but AWS does — and **for EC2 this is a NEW orphan class**: unlike IAM / S3 / Logs where the orphan is later detectable as `EntityAlreadyExists` on next deploy, EC2 resources have system-generated IDs (`vpc-aaa`, `subnet-aaa`, `sg-aaa`, `i-aaa`) so the orphan accumulates SILENTLY on every redeploy. The fix wraps the post-first-create calls in an inner try/catch that issues a best-effort `Delete*Command` / `TerminateInstancesCommand` before re-throwing the original error. **`createInstance` is the cost-leak class**: `RunInstancesCommand` starts billing immediately, and the cleanup path issues `TerminateInstancesCommand` WITHOUT waiting for terminated state (the deploy is already failing — making the user wait another 30-120s for the error to surface is bad UX, and if the waiter itself was the wiring failure, waiting again would be ironic). When the terminate cleanup itself fails, the WARN message escalates to `THE INSTANCE IS STILL RUNNING AND BILLING` with the exact `aws ec2 terminate-instances --instance-ids <id>` recovery command — the operator-visible alarm bell that matches the actual risk. No idempotent-create wrinkle for any of these (CreateVpc / CreateSubnet / CreateSecurityGroup / RunInstances all return fresh IDs rather than taking ownership). A freshly-created VPC / Subnet / SG has no dependencies attached (default rules CASCADE-delete with the SG; subnet has no ENIs yet; VPC has only default SG / NACL which CASCADE), so a single Delete\* SDK call suffices in the cleanup path — no need for the retry / side-channel ENI sweep that the corresponding `delete*` methods need. `applyTags` is internally fail-tolerant (swallows errors at WARN), so it cannot fail the wiring path; this is intentional — tag failures should not abort an otherwise-successful create. 12 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/ec2-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/ec2-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts) covering: cleanup fires on wiring failure for each of the 4 methods → reverse `Delete*` / `TerminateInstances` sequence; no cleanup when the first `Create*` / `RunInstances` itself fails (nothing to delete); cleanup itself fails → original error still propagates with a recovery-hint WARN (the createInstance variant asserts the `THE INSTANCE IS STILL RUNNING AND BILLING` alarm prefix specifically). Tests use `vi.mock('@aws-sdk/client-ec2', ...)` to stub the SDK waiter (`waitUntilInstanceRunning`) so the timeout case is simulated without real polling. Issue #376 progress: Batch Storage (PR #377) + Batch IAM (PR #378) + Batch EC2 (this PR) shipped, 2 batches remain (Messaging, Database).

- ✅ Fix: Apply the PR #374 partial-create-cleanup pattern to `IAMRoleProvider.create`, `IAMUserGroupProvider.createUser`, `IAMUserGroupProvider.createGroup`, and `IAMInstanceProfileProvider.create` (Batch IAM of Issue #376's 14-provider sweep — 4 of the remaining 11 providers). Same shape as the Storage batch (PR #377): once the first `Create*Command` returns, AWS has committed the resource; if a subsequent wiring call (managed-policy attach / inline policy / permissions boundary / login profile / group membership / role attach) throws, cdkd state has nothing recorded but AWS does, so the next `cdkd deploy` rejects with `EntityAlreadyExists: <type> with name <X> already exists`. The fix wraps the post-first-create calls in an inner try/catch that issues a best-effort `Detach*` / `RemoveRoleFromInstanceProfile` / `Delete*Policy` / `DeleteLoginProfile` / `DeleteUserPermissionsBoundary` BEFORE `Delete<Role|User|Group|InstanceProfile>Command`. The detach-before-delete ordering is **load-bearing** for IAM — `DeleteRole` / `DeleteUser` / `DeleteGroup` / `DeleteInstanceProfile` all reject when the entity still has attached managed policies, inline policies, group memberships, or role attachments. Cleanup-step ordering mirrors each provider's existing `delete()` method (which already encodes the correct detach order): `IAMRoleProvider.detachAllManagedPolicies` + `deleteAllInlinePolicies` + `DeleteRoleCommand`; `IAMUserGroupProvider.removeUserFromAllGroups` + `detachAllUserPolicies` + `deleteAllUserInlinePolicies` + `DeleteLoginProfile` (NoSuchEntity-tolerant) + `DeleteUserPermissionsBoundary` (NoSuchEntity-tolerant) + `DeleteUserCommand`; `IAMUserGroupProvider.detachAllGroupPolicies` + `deleteAllGroupInlinePolicies` + `DeleteGroupCommand` (no `removeAllUsersFromGroup` — a freshly-created group has no users); per-attached-role `RemoveRoleFromInstanceProfileCommand` + `DeleteInstanceProfileCommand`. **No idempotent-create wrinkle** for any of these — `CreateRole` / `CreateUser` / `CreateGroup` / `CreateInstanceProfile` all reject `EntityAlreadyExists` rather than taking ownership, so no `createdNew<X>` flag is needed (simpler than S3 / Logs). The `IAMInstanceProfileProvider` tracks an `attachedRoles[]` array locally to emit the right `RemoveRoleFromInstanceProfile` calls per successful attach — even when the role-attach loop fails mid-iteration (first role attached, second role fails), only the successfully-attached roles are removed. Cleanup failures are logged at WARN with the exact `aws iam <command>` recovery hints for manual cleanup (detach managed policies + delete inline policies + delete the entity). 12 new unit tests across [tests/unit/provisioning/{iam-role,iam-user,iam-group,iam-instance-profile}-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/) covering: cleanup fires on wiring failure → reverse-order detach + delete sequence; no cleanup when the first `Create*` itself fails (nothing to delete); cleanup itself fails → original error still propagates with a recovery-hint WARN. Tests use the real `NoSuchEntityException` from `@aws-sdk/client-iam` (the providers match on `instanceof`, not on `error.name`) and call `mockSend.mockReset()` between tests (`vi.clearAllMocks()` does NOT drain queued `mockResolvedValueOnce`/`mockRejectedValueOnce` entries, so leftover queue entries from one test bleed into the next). Issue #376 progress: Batch Storage (PR #377) + Batch IAM (this PR) shipped, 3 batches remain (EC2, Messaging, Database).

- ✅ Fix: Apply the PR #374 partial-create-cleanup pattern to `S3BucketProvider.create`, `LogsLogGroupProvider.create`, and `SSMParameterProvider.create` (first three of Issue #376's 14-provider sweep). Same shape as #374: once the first `Create*Command` returns, AWS has committed the resource; if a subsequent wiring call (sub-config / tag / policy / etc.) throws, cdkd state has nothing recorded but AWS does, so the next `cdkd deploy` rejects with `BucketAlreadyOwnedByYou` / `ResourceAlreadyExists` / `ParameterAlreadyExists`. The fix wraps the post-first-create calls in an inner try/catch that issues a best-effort cleanup `Delete*Command` before re-throwing the original error. Cleanup failures are logged at WARN with the exact `aws <svc> delete-<x> --... <physicalId>` command for manual recovery. **Idempotent-create gating** is load-bearing for S3 and Logs: both already accept `BucketAlreadyOwnedByYou` / `ResourceAlreadyExistsException` on `CreateBucket` / `CreateLogGroup` as "take ownership of pre-existing resource", and deleting it on a post-create failure would destroy a user resource that lived before this deploy. Each provider tracks a `createdNew<Bucket|LogGroup>` flag that's true only on a real CREATE; cleanup fires only when it's true. SSM has no idempotent-create wrinkle (`PutParameter` runs with `Overwrite: false`, so AWS rejects pre-existing names at create time — no flag needed). The Logs `ResourceAlreadyExistsException` handling was refactored from the outer catch to inline at the `CreateLogGroupCommand` site, so the outer catch sees only genuine failures and the inner cleanup branch can rely on the flag. **Side effect of the refactor**: pre-PR, when `CreateLogGroup` hit `ResourceAlreadyExistsException`, the outer catch did an early return that SKIPPED all post-create wiring (`PutRetentionPolicy` / `PutDataProtectionPolicy` / `PutIndexPolicy` / `PutBearerTokenAuthentication`). Post-PR, the inline handler falls through to the wiring block, so retention / data-protection / index / bearer-token policies ARE applied to the adopted log group on every deploy. This is correct convergence-to-cdkd-state semantics and is what users expect after a partial-failure recovery, but it does mean that a log group adopted via name collision will have its policies overwritten on next deploy — by design. 12 new unit tests across [tests/unit/provisioning/{s3-bucket,logs-loggroup,ssm-parameter}-provider-partial-create-cleanup.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/) covering: cleanup fires on wiring failure → `Delete*Command` issued; cleanup is skipped when the first call hit the idempotent fallback (S3 + Logs) — pre-existing resource preserved; cleanup is skipped when the first call itself fails non-idempotently (nothing to delete); cleanup itself fails → original error still propagates with a `aws <svc> delete-...` recovery hint at WARN. Issue #376 tracks the remaining 11 providers.

- ✅ Fix: `ApiGatewayProvider.createMethod` now cleans up the AWS-side Method when any wiring call AFTER `PutMethodCommand` fails (closes the partial-create orphan class — first surfaced as a `Method already exists for this resource` rejection on re-deploy after the PR #373 ordering bug had been hit on the previous attempt). The cause is a classic two-phase-commit gap: once `PutMethodCommand` returns, AWS has committed the Method resource; if a subsequent `PutIntegrationCommand` / `PutMethodResponseCommand` / `PutIntegrationResponseCommand` throws, cdkd aborts before the success-return so the Method is NOT recorded in cdkd state, but it still exists on AWS. The next `cdkd deploy` plans CREATE → AWS rejects with `Method already exists for this resource` → the user has to manually `aws apigateway delete-method` before re-deploy. The fix wraps every post-`PutMethod` call in an inner try/catch that issues a best-effort `DeleteMethodCommand` before re-throwing the original error. Cleanup failures are logged at WARN with the exact `aws apigateway delete-method --rest-api-id <id> --resource-id <id> --http-method <m>` command (so the user can run it by hand if the SDK call itself failed); the original error always propagates so the user sees what actually broke. `PutMethodCommand` failure itself is the only path where cleanup is intentionally skipped — AWS never committed the resource so there's nothing to delete and an unconditional `DeleteMethod` would just produce a misleading `NotFoundException` in the logs. Sibling sub-resources (Integration / MethodResponse / IntegrationResponse) are CASCADE-deleted by AWS when the parent Method is deleted, so a single `DeleteMethodCommand` suffices — no need for a 4-step rollback. The class of bug — partial AWS-side commit on `createMethod` failure — was first triggered by the `PutIntegrationResponse`-before-`PutMethodResponse` ordering bug fixed in PR #373; this cleanup makes any future shape of post-`PutMethod` failure self-healing on the next redeploy. 5 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/apigateway-provider.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/apigateway-provider.test.ts) covering cleanup-on-PutIntegration-failure, cleanup-on-PutMethodResponse-failure, cleanup-on-PutIntegrationResponse-failure (belt and braces post-#373), no-cleanup-on-PutMethod-failure, and the cleanup-itself-fails path (original error still propagates).

- ✅ Fix: `ApiGatewayProvider.createMethod` now issues `PutMethodResponseCommand` BEFORE `PutIntegrationResponseCommand`. Pre-fix the call order was `PutMethod` → `PutIntegration` → per-entry `PutIntegrationResponse` → per-entry `PutMethodResponse`, which AWS rejects with `Invalid mapping expression specified: Validation Result: warnings : [], errors : [No method response exists for method.]`: `PutIntegrationResponse` validates that the `MethodResponse` for the same `statusCode` already exists, because IntegrationResponse's `ResponseParameters` / `ResponseTemplates` map onto headers declared by the MethodResponse. The canonical user-visible trigger is `new RestApi(this, 'ChatApi', { defaultCorsPreflightOptions: { allowOrigins: Cors.ALL_ORIGINS, allowMethods: Cors.ALL_METHODS } })`: CDK auto-generates an `AWS::ApiGateway::Method` per resource with `HttpMethod: OPTIONS`, each carrying both `Integration.IntegrationResponses` and `MethodResponses` arrays for the CORS-headers wiring — pre-fix every CORS preflight OPTIONS method failed to create. The fix is a pure reorder: `PutMethod` → `PutIntegration` (if `Integration` is set) → per-entry `PutMethodResponse` → per-entry `PutIntegrationResponse`. `MethodResponses` is also emitted even when `Integration` is absent (the previous code only walked `MethodResponses` after the integration branch — moving it outside the `if (integration)` block also fixes the silent drop for methods without an Integration property, though CDK's CORS-emitted methods always set Integration so this is defense-in-depth). Class of bug: same shape as #370's missing-field drop, but on call ORDERING rather than field forwarding. 2 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/apigateway-provider.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/apigateway-provider.test.ts) (full CORS preflight call-order assertion via `mockSend.mock.calls.map(c => c[0].constructor.name).toEqual([...])`; `MethodResponses` emitted when `Integration` is absent).

- ✅ Fix: `ApiGatewayProvider.createMethod` now forwards every mutable field supported by `PutMethodRequest` and `PutIntegrationRequest`, plus per-status-code `PutIntegrationResponseCommand` calls for `Integration.IntegrationResponses[]`. Pre-fix `createMethod` only sent `restApiId` / `resourceId` / `httpMethod` / `authorizationType` / `authorizerId` on `PutMethodCommand` and `type` / `integrationHttpMethod` / `uri` on `PutIntegrationCommand`, silently dropping every other field. The canonical user-reported failure: `new LambdaIntegration(chatFn, { responseTransferMode: ResponseTransferMode.STREAM })` emits `Integration.Uri: ".../response-streaming-invocations"` (streaming URI) + `Integration.ResponseTransferMode: "STREAM"`; pre-fix cdkd dropped the latter and AWS rejected the integration with `Invalid ResponseTransferMode. Cannot use ResponseTransferMode BUFFERED for Lambda functions invoked by InvokeWithResponseStream for AWS_PROXY integrations.` New Method-level fields forwarded: `ApiKeyRequired`, `OperationName`, `RequestParameters` (Record<string,boolean>), `RequestModels` (Record<string,string>), `RequestValidatorId`, `AuthorizationScopes`. New Integration-level fields forwarded: `ConnectionType`, `ConnectionId`, `Credentials`, `RequestParameters`, `RequestTemplates`, `PassthroughBehavior`, `ContentHandling`, `TimeoutInMillis`, `CacheNamespace`, `CacheKeyParameters`, `TlsConfig`, `ResponseTransferMode`. `IntegrationResponses[]` (CFn shape `[{StatusCode, SelectionPattern?, ResponseParameters?, ResponseTemplates?, ContentHandling?}, ...]`) is applied via per-entry `PutIntegrationResponseCommand` calls (newly imported from `@aws-sdk/client-api-gateway`). The update path was also extended: `updateMethod` now emits a comma-joined `replace /authorizationScopes` patch op (same pattern as `Authorizer.ProviderARNs`) when the array diffs, so `cdkd drift --revert` can round-trip a console-side scope change. `Integration` / `MethodResponses` are still NOT touched by `updateMethod` — they remain separate API Gateway sub-resources (`UpdateIntegration` / `UpdateMethodResponse`) and the `!== undefined` gate plus the existing inline-comment block keep their empty-`{}` placeholders from reaching AWS. `handledProperties['AWS::ApiGateway::Method']` extended with the six new Method fields so the deploy engine does not redirect them to CC API. `TlsConfig` requires a PascalCase → camelCase conversion (CFn emits `{InsecureSkipVerification}`, the SDK input shape is `{insecureSkipVerification}`) — passing the CFn object verbatim would silently drop the field, same class of bug as the original `ResponseTransferMode` regression. `readCurrentState` is **not** extended in this PR — the pre-existing `result['Integration'] = resp.methodIntegration ?? {}` returns SDK-camelCase keys while cdkd state stores CFn-PascalCase, which would fire false-positive drift on every clean run; the right fix is either reverse-mapping the SDK shape back to PascalCase or adding `AWS::ApiGateway::Method` to `drift-cc-api-deny-list.ts`, deferred as a separate concern from this deploy-time fix. 6 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/apigateway-provider.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/apigateway-provider.test.ts) (full Method-field forwarding / `ResponseTransferMode=STREAM` regression / full Integration-field forwarding / per-`IntegrationResponses[]` `PutIntegrationResponseCommand` issuance / absent-IntegrationResponses pass-through) + 1 update-path test in [tests/unit/provisioning/apigateway-provider-roundtrip.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/apigateway-provider-roundtrip.test.ts) (`AuthorizationScopes` comma-joined patch op).

- ✅ `Fn::ImportValue` strong reference + persistent exports index (closes [#343](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/343)). State schema bumped to v4: each consumer's `state.imports[]` records every `Fn::ImportValue` resolved during its last deploy (`{sourceStack, sourceRegion, exportName}`). `cdkd destroy <producer>` and `cdkd state destroy <producer>` now scan every other stack's state.imports[] BEFORE deleting and refuse with `StackHasActiveImportsError` (exit code 2) when any consumer still references the producer — matching CloudFormation's strong-reference semantics. The error message names every offending consumer (`<stack> (<region>): imports export '<name>'`) and points at the two valid resolution paths (destroy the consumer first, or remove the `Fn::ImportValue` from the consumer's template and redeploy). NO `--force` escape hatch (deliberately, matching CFn) — use `Fn::GetStackOutput` at template-authoring time if you want a weak reference instead. Strong-ref check ALWAYS scans state.json directly, never trusting the persistent exports index — a stale index could miss a freshly-recorded consumer and we don't let perf-only data gate destruction safety. Persistent **per-region exports index** at `s3://{state-bucket}/cdkd/_index/{region}/exports.json` (CFn's `ListExports` analog, [src/state/export-index-store.ts](src/state/export-index-store.ts)) makes `Fn::ImportValue` resolution O(1) per lookup at scale: ~100-300ms cold-start GET vs the pre-fix O(N) per-resolve scan (200-stack environments resolved in minutes). Index is a **derived view** rebuilt from state.json on demand — state.json remains the canonical source of truth. Lifecycle: rebuilt automatically on first miss (index 404 / corrupt JSON), updated incrementally after each successful deploy / destroy via If-Match optimistic lock with 5-retry exponential backoff, patched single-entry on resolve miss + state.json fallback hit (drift recovery). Failures are best-effort: the in-memory write continues even after retry exhaustion (logged at warn) and the index self-heals on subsequent operations. **NO periodic rebuild / defrag / vacuum** — only the absence or corruption of the index file triggers a full rebuild. **Migration v3 → v4 is fully transparent**: v4 readers treat v3 state's missing `imports` field as undefined (= empty), v4 writers always emit v4. The strong-reference enforcement activates GRADUALLY as consumers are re-deployed under v4: a v3-era consumer with no `imports[]` field cannot block a producer destroy (matches pre-fix behavior, no regression) until its next redeploy populates the field. Breaking change in release notes: producer destruction that previously succeeded silently while a consumer existed now refuses with a clear error. Resolver context extended with `exportIndex` (optional ExportIndexStore) + `recordedImports` (the bag the resolver pushes entries into for the DeployEngine to persist). `IntrinsicFunctionResolver.resolveImportValue` hot path: index lookup (1 GET cached) → on hit, record + return; on miss, fallback to per-stack listStacks + getState scan, patch the index entry, record + return. `Fn::GetStackOutput` does NOT push into recordedImports by design — it is a weak reference. Implementation: `src/types/state.ts` (schema v4 + `StateImportEntry`), `src/state/export-index-store.ts` (NEW, ~340 LOC), `src/deployment/intrinsic-function-resolver.ts` (cache integration), `src/deployment/deploy-engine.ts` (cache build + per-stack imports collection + state save + post-save index update), `src/cli/commands/destroy-runner.ts` (scanActiveConsumers helper + StackHasActiveImportsError throw + post-destroy indexStore.removeStack), `src/utils/error-handler.ts` (StackHasActiveImportsError class, exit code 2). Tests: 5 new unit test files (41 tests) across `tests/unit/state/export-index-store.test.ts` / `tests/unit/state/schema-v4-migration.test.ts` / `tests/unit/cli/destroy-runner-strong-ref.test.ts` / `tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-import-value-index.test.ts` / `tests/unit/utils/stack-has-active-imports-error.test.ts`. Real-AWS integ at `tests/integration/import-value-strong-ref/` (2-stack producer/consumer fixture) exercises deploy → assert state.imports[] populated → assert index file written → assert producer destroy refused with clear error → simulate v3 → v4 migration by rewriting consumer state as v3 (drops imports[]) → assert producer destroy now proceeds (gradual activation) → assert index purged of producer entries → clean teardown. Full design at [docs/cross-stack-references.md](docs/cross-stack-references.md).

- ✅ Fix: `CustomResourceProvider.{create,update,delete}` now type-guard `properties.ServiceToken` before calling `.startsWith()` (closes [#330](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/330)). Pre-fix any object-shaped ServiceToken value (e.g. an unresolved `{Fn::GetAtt: ['MyHandlerFn', 'Arn']}` intrinsic leaked into `state.properties` by an earlier `cdkd import` that did not resolve intrinsics) crashed with `TypeError: serviceToken.startsWith is not a function` — an unactionable error that was additionally swallowed by `cdkd destroy`'s outer try/catch as `Failed to delete custom resource X, but continuing: ...` so the user could not tell whether the resource was actually deleted or just dropped from state. Fix adds a `typeof serviceToken !== 'string'` guard at the entry of each method that throws `ProvisioningError` with a clear message naming the logical id, the offending `typeof` (e.g. `object`), and pointing the user at `cdkd import` / `cdkd state orphan` as recovery paths. Defensive: the upstream root cause is the companion PR adding intrinsic resolution to `cdkd import`; this PR is the provider-boundary safety net so corrupted state, partial migration, or any future code path that emits raw-intrinsic ServiceTokens fails with an actionable error instead of `.startsWith is not a function`. 4 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/custom-resource-provider.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/custom-resource-provider.test.ts) (per-method type-guard rejection + recovery-path message assertion).

- ✅ Fix: `cdkd import` now resolves CFn intrinsics (`Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` / `Fn::Sub` / ...) in each resource's `Properties` before writing them to `state.properties`, closes [#328](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/328). Pre-fix, `buildStackState` wrote the synth template's Properties literal verbatim — intrinsics and all — which broke `cdkd destroy` for sub-resource types whose `delete()` reads properties at delete time (canonical case: `AWS::Lambda::Permission` whose `FunctionName: {Fn::GetAtt: [<Fn>, 'Arn']}` got passed to RemovePermission as the raw intrinsic object and AWS rejected with `1 validation error detected: ... failed to satisfy constraint`). `cdkd deploy` did NOT have this problem because the deploy engine runs `IntrinsicFunctionResolver` against each resource's Properties before calling `provider.create()` and stores the resolved shape in state. New `resolveImportedProperties(stackState, template, region, stateBackend, logger)` helper in [src/cli/commands/import.ts](src/cli/commands/import.ts) runs AFTER `buildStackState` (so every imported logical ID has a `physicalId` in `stackState.resources` for `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` to bind against) and BEFORE `captureObservedForImportedResources` and `saveState`. Parameters / Conditions are pulled from the template the same way the deploy engine builds its intrinsic context. Per-resource try/catch: intrinsics referencing a resource not in the importable set (custom resources, out-of-scope siblings in selective mode, or a typo) log a warn and leave the raw intrinsic in place — the eventual destroy failure on the un-resolved props is narrower than blowing up the whole adoption flow; the user can re-import once the missing sibling is in state, or `cdkd state orphan` to scrub it. This brings `cdkd import` in line with the v3 schema's "resolved template intent" semantics across both write paths. Existing imported stacks (deployed before this fix) still have raw intrinsics in state — re-import (or `cdkd state orphan` + redeploy) is the migration path; a separate `cdkd state migrate-intrinsics` is out of scope. 4 new unit tests in [tests/unit/cli/import.test.ts](tests/unit/cli/import.test.ts) covering the canonical Lambda Permission `Fn::GetAtt` ARN case, sibling `Ref` resolution, literal-only no-op pass, and the warn-and-keep-raw fallback for unresolvable intrinsics.

- ✅ Sweep: `IntrinsicFunctionResolver.constructAttribute()` adds per-type `Arn` handlers for 18 additional resource types whose physicalId is a name / id (not the full ARN) and where downstream IAM Policy `Resource:` references would otherwise hit the silent `physicalId` fallback. Same class of bug as #329 (ECR Repository) / #365 (DynamoDB GlobalTable) — proactive audit of all SDK-Provider-registered types against the existing switch table to prevent future user reports. Coverage: `AWS::IAM::User`, `AWS::IAM::Group`, `AWS::IAM::InstanceProfile`, `AWS::KMS::Key`, `AWS::Cognito::UserPool`, `AWS::Kinesis::Stream`, `AWS::Events::Rule` (with custom `EventBusName` ARN-segment-aware), `AWS::Events::EventBus`, `AWS::EFS::FileSystem`, `AWS::KinesisFirehose::DeliveryStream`, `AWS::CodeBuild::Project`, `AWS::CloudTrail::Trail`, `AWS::AppSync::GraphQLApi`, `AWS::ServiceDiscovery::PrivateDnsNamespace`, `AWS::ServiceDiscovery::Service`, `AWS::CloudWatch::Alarm` (note `alarm:` separator), `AWS::RDS::DBInstance` + `AWS::DocDB::DBInstance` + `AWS::Neptune::DBInstance` (shared `rds:db:` ARN namespace), `AWS::RDS::DBCluster` + `AWS::DocDB::DBCluster` + `AWS::Neptune::DBCluster` (shared `rds:cluster:` namespace), `AWS::S3Express::DirectoryBucket`. Bonus: removed a dead-code duplicate `AWS::EC2::VPC` handler (the second `if` block at line 726 was unreachable after the comprehensive one at line 568). 27 new unit tests via a parameterized describe block in [tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-functions.test.ts](tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-functions.test.ts) covering each ARN shape + the `Events::Rule` default-bus / custom-bus-name / bus-ARN-extraction branches + unknown-attribute fallback.

- ✅ Fix: `cdkd diff` / `cdkd deploy` no longer emit `Unknown attribute Arn for resource type AWS::DynamoDB::GlobalTable, returning physical ID` when an IAM policy references a CDK `TableV2` ARN (typical CDK shape: `table.grantReadData(fn)` / `table.grantWriteData(fn)`). Pre-fix `IntrinsicFunctionResolver` had a per-type `Arn` handler for `AWS::DynamoDB::Table` (CDK v1 `Table` construct) but not `AWS::DynamoDB::GlobalTable` (CDK v2 `TableV2` construct), so `Fn::GetAtt: [<TableV2>, 'Arn']` fell through to the bare physicalId and the IAM `CreatePolicy` call failed with `Resource <physicalId> must be in ARN format or "*"`. Fix widens the existing branch to match both resource types — the ARN format `arn:${partition}:dynamodb:${region}:${accountId}:table/${physicalId}` is identical for both. 2 unit tests in [tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-functions.test.ts](tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-functions.test.ts) (Arn / unknown-attribute fallback).

- ✅ Fix: `cdkd diff` / `cdkd deploy` no longer emit `Unknown attribute Arn for resource type AWS::ECR::Repository, returning physical ID` (followed by `Fn::Select: index 4 out of bounds (array length: 1)` and `index 3`) when a stack references an ECR Repository via `Fn::GetAtt: [<EcrRepo>, 'Arn']` (typical CDK shape: `containerImage.fromEcrRepository(repo)` execution-role grant), closes [#329](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/329). Pre-fix `IntrinsicFunctionResolver` ([src/deployment/intrinsic-function-resolver.ts](src/deployment/intrinsic-function-resolver.ts)) had per-type handlers for `Arn` on `AWS::Lambda::Function` / `AWS::SNS::Topic` / `AWS::Logs::LogGroup` / `AWS::ECS::Cluster` etc. but `AWS::ECR::Repository` was missing — the default branch returned the bare physicalId (the repo name like `cdksamplestack-myconstructmyecrrepo218ce823`), so downstream `Fn::Split(':', repoName) = [repoName]` (1 element) made `Fn::Select(4, ...)` (which extracts the region segment from `arn:aws:ecr:REGION:ACCT:repository/NAME`) out-of-bounds. Fix adds an `AWS::ECR::Repository` switch handler returning `arn:${partition}:ecr:${region}:${accountId}:repository/${physicalId}` for `Arn` and `${accountId}.dkr.ecr.${region}.amazonaws.com/${physicalId}` for `RepositoryUri`. 3 unit tests in [tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-functions.test.ts](tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-functions.test.ts) (Arn / RepositoryUri / unknown-attribute fallback).

- ✅ Fix: `cdkd drift` no longer fires false positives on `AWS::IAM::Role` / `AWS::IAM::User` / `AWS::IAM::Group` when policies are attached via a **separate** `AWS::IAM::Policy` resource (e.g. CDK's auto-emitted `*DefaultPolicy36563E38` for `role.addToPolicy(...)` / `bucket.grantRead(role)` / `ContainerImage.fromEcrRepository(repo)`'s execution-role grant), closes [#323](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/323). The pre-#323 regression (introduced by PR #175 lifting `Policies` out of `getDriftUnknownPaths` to read via `ListRolePolicies + GetRolePolicy`) didn't filter out policies managed by sibling resources — every Role with such a policy fired `~ Role (...) - Policies: [] + Policies: [{...DefaultPolicy*}]` drift. Fix: new optional `ReadCurrentStateContext` parameter on `ResourceProvider.readCurrentState` carries same-stack siblings; `IAMRoleProvider` / `IAMUserGroupProvider` exclude inline policies whose `PolicyName` matches an `AWS::IAM::Policy` sibling whose `Roles` / `Users` / `Groups` list includes this role/user/group. Helper `collectInlinePolicyNamesManagedBySiblings(targetPhysicalId, context, attachmentField)` exported from [src/provisioning/providers/iam-role-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/iam-role-provider.ts) and consumed by `iam-user-group-provider.ts`'s `collectInlinePolicies`. Context-building helper `buildReadCurrentStateContext(state, excludedLogicalId)` in [src/cli/commands/drift.ts](src/cli/commands/drift.ts) is exported and reused by [state.ts](src/cli/commands/state.ts) `refreshObservedForStack` and [import.ts](src/cli/commands/import.ts) `populateObservedProperties`. Deploy-engine's `kickOffObservedCapture` deliberately does NOT pass context — at deploy time the sibling Policy resource may not be created yet, and the no-context branch is a safe no-op (observed.Policies captures the empty-at-that-moment state, which matches the post-filter AWS state at drift time). 4 new unit tests in [tests/unit/provisioning/iam-role-provider-readcurrentstate.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/iam-role-provider-readcurrentstate.test.ts) cover the filter (matches / doesn't match / console-add still surfaces / no-context backward compat).

- ✅ Fix: `cdkd drift` silently skips `Custom::*` resource types instead of reporting them as "drift unknown" (= actionable-noise category). Pre-fix the output included `? AutoDelete (Custom::S3AutoDeleteObjects)` on every drift run for stacks using `aws-cdk-lib`'s `autoDeleteObjects: true` helper or any user-defined Custom Resource. Drift on a Custom Resource is not actionable from `cdkd drift` (would require re-invoking the handler Lambda), so the noise was pure UX cost. New `DriftOutcome` variant `{ kind: 'skipped' }` is counted in `total` but does not appear in the human report; JSON output adds a `skipped: [...]` array for tooling. Implementation in [src/cli/commands/drift.ts](src/cli/commands/drift.ts) — `Custom::*` is short-circuited to `skipped` BEFORE the provider lookup so the CC-API fallback path (which would reject the type pattern with `ValidationException`) is never reached. Unit test in [tests/unit/cli/drift.test.ts](tests/unit/cli/drift.test.ts) updated to assert the silent-skip behavior.

- ✅ CLI: `cdkd deploy` prints a CDK-CLI-style `Outputs:` section at the end of the per-stack run when the synth template declared `Outputs`. Each line is formatted as `<StackName>.<OutputKey> = <value>` (with a two-space indent), matching upstream `cdk deploy`. The values are sourced from the existing per-stack `state.outputs` (already resolved by `resolveOutputs` against every CFn intrinsic) and filtered by `template.Outputs` keys so Export.Name-duplicated entries don't surface twice. Emitted on both the real-deploy success path and the no-change path (the resolved values are unchanged but still useful as a reference); suppressed under `--dry-run` since nothing was actually deployed. Implementation: new optional `outputs?: Record<string, unknown>` field on `DeployResult` populated via a new `buildDisplayOutputs(template, resolvedOutputs)` helper in [src/deployment/deploy-engine.ts](src/deployment/deploy-engine.ts), printed by [src/cli/commands/deploy.ts](src/cli/commands/deploy.ts) after the `Deployment Summary` block. 3 new unit tests in [tests/unit/deployment/deploy-result-outputs.test.ts](tests/unit/deployment/deploy-result-outputs.test.ts) covering the no-change path with Export.Name filtering, no-Outputs template, and dry-run suppression.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd deploy` default-flip — `--no-prefix-user-supplied-names` is now the DEFAULT (closes [#299](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/299)). Breaking change in v0.94.0 (the repo's `.releaserc.json` maps `breaking: true` → `release: "minor"` since cdkd is in 0.x, so this bumps to v0.94.0 NOT 1.0.0). Before this PR cdkd prepended the stack name to user-declared physical names on Pattern B providers (IAM Role / User / Group / InstanceProfile / ELBv2 LoadBalancer / TargetGroup) by default; pass `--no-prefix-user-supplied-names` to opt OUT. After this PR cdkd skips the prefix by default — every `roleName: 'my-role'` produces an AWS resource named `my-role` consistent with Pattern A providers (Lambda / S3 / SNS / etc.) out of the box. New escape hatch `--prefix-user-supplied-names` (env `CDKD_PREFIX_USER_SUPPLIED_NAMES=true`, cdk.json `context.cdkd.prefixUserSuppliedNames: true`) restores legacy prefixing on Pattern B types — useful when upgrading an existing stack without taking a one-time REPLACEMENT on every Pattern B resource (the deploy-time migration pre-flight from [#300](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/300) detects those stacks and prompts before any provider call). Auto-generated names (where the user did NOT declare a physical name) keep the prefix regardless — those rely on it for cross-stack uniqueness. **Migration path**: see [docs/cli-reference.md](docs/cli-reference.md) under `--prefix-user-supplied-names` → "Migration from pre-v0.94.0" — accept the one-time REPLACEMENT, pin `--prefix-user-supplied-names`, or drop the explicit `roleName` in CDK code. State-side rename helper (`cdkd state rename-strip-prefix <stack>`) is tracked in [#300](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/300). **Deprecated aliases** (still accepted, emit a warning, no-op against the new default): `--no-prefix-user-supplied-names` CLI flag, `CDKD_NO_PREFIX_USER_SUPPLIED_NAMES=true` env var, `cdk.json context.cdkd.noPrefixUserSuppliedNames: true`. Resolution chain (highest wins): `--prefix-user-supplied-names` CLI flag → `CDKD_PREFIX_USER_SUPPLIED_NAMES=true` env → `cdk.json context.cdkd.prefixUserSuppliedNames: true` → default `true` (skip prefix). `resolveSkipPrefix(...)` signature was widened from `(cliValue: boolean)` to `(opts: { prefixUserSuppliedNames?: boolean })` to carry the new opt-in flag. The deprecated CLI flag `--no-prefix-user-supplied-names` is detected via a pre-parse argv walk in `warnDeprecatedNoPrefixCliFlag(argv)` (Commander's auto-negation collapses `--no-X` onto the `--X` key, so there is no separate Commander key for the deprecated flag — declaring both Options together would make `noPrefixUserSuppliedNames` permanently `undefined`). `cdkd destroy` / `state destroy` / `drift` remain unaffected — they operate on the state-recorded `physicalId`. Implementation: [src/cli/config-loader.ts](src/cli/config-loader.ts) (flipped default + new env / cdk.json keys + deprecation warnings on the legacy aliases) + [src/cli/options.ts](src/cli/options.ts) (new `--prefix-user-supplied-names` Option) + [src/cli/commands/deploy.ts](src/cli/commands/deploy.ts) (calls `warnDeprecatedNoPrefixCliFlag()` once at command start + passes `{ prefixUserSuppliedNames }` to `resolveSkipPrefix`). Tests: [tests/unit/cli/config-loader.test.ts](tests/unit/cli/config-loader.test.ts) updated to reflect the new default + new `--prefix-user-supplied-names` resolution chain + deprecated-alias warning paths.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd deploy` migration pre-flight (closes [#300](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/300)) — when `--no-prefix-user-supplied-names` is active AND the existing stack state contains one or more Pattern B resources (IAM Role / User / Group / InstanceProfile / ELBv2 LoadBalancer / TargetGroup) whose `physicalId` still starts with `${stackName}-`, cdkd now lists each affected resource (`<logicalId> (<resourceType>): <oldPhysicalId> -> <newPhysicalId>`) and prompts `Continue? (y/N)` before any provider call runs — the default flips to **no** because the diff-driven REPLACEMENT side effect is destructive, mirroring the `cdkd destroy --remove-protection` default-no precedent; `-y` / `--yes` (the global CDK CLI parity flag) skips the prompt for CI / non-interactive runs and declining exits cleanly with `no resources modified`. Implementation: new shared `PATTERN_B_RESOURCE_TYPES` constant exported from [src/provisioning/resource-name.ts](src/provisioning/resource-name.ts) (single source of truth — keep in sync with the Pattern B provider call sites that consume `generateResourceNameWithFallback`); new pure-functional `findPendingPrefixRenames(stackName, state)` + interactive `promptMigrationConfirm(renames, {yes})` helpers in [src/cli/commands/prefix-migration-check.ts](src/cli/commands/prefix-migration-check.ts); deploy CLI wires the check inside `runStackInner`'s per-stack `try { ... } finally { ... }` block — gated on `skipPrefix === true`, fires AFTER state load AND BEFORE `new DeployEngine(...)` so per-stack AWS-client teardown still runs whether the user confirms or declines; no-op when state is empty (first-time deploy), when no Pattern B resource is still prefixed, or when the flag is off. Non-TTY guard rejects the prompt with an actionable error pointing at `--yes` so CI without the flag does not silently decline. 16 unit tests in [tests/unit/cli/prefix-migration-check.test.ts](tests/unit/cli/prefix-migration-check.test.ts) (no-state / no Pattern B / already-unprefixed / mixed Pattern A+B / every Pattern B type / supplied-stackName-not-state-stackName + prompt yes/no/default/empty/mixed-case/close-on-confirm + non-TTY guard + empty-suffix skip).
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd deploy --no-prefix-user-supplied-names` (closes [#296](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/296)) — opt-in flag that **skips** prepending the stack name to physical names the user explicitly declared in their CDK code (`new iam.Role(this, 'X', { roleName: 'my-role' })` → AWS resource `my-role` instead of `MyStack-my-role`). Auto-generated names (no user-declared physical name) keep the prefix regardless for cross-stack uniqueness. **Off by default for backward compatibility**; a future major-version PR will flip the default after a release cycle (separate issue, not in scope here). Resolution chain (highest wins): CLI flag → `CDKD_NO_PREFIX_USER_SUPPLIED_NAMES=true` env var → `cdk.json` `context.cdkd.noPrefixUserSuppliedNames: true` → default `false`. Only affects **Pattern B providers** whose pre-PR code path ran user-supplied names through `generateResourceName` (which prepended the prefix): `IAMRoleProvider`, `IAMUserGroupProvider` (User + Group), `IAMInstanceProfileProvider`, `ELBv2Provider` (LoadBalancer + TargetGroup). Pattern A providers (Lambda, S3, SNS, SQS, DynamoDB, Logs LogGroup, Events Rule, etc.) historically short-circuited user-supplied names **out** of `generateResourceName` entirely — those types never got the prefix and the flag is a no-op for them by construction. Implementation: new `skipPrefixStore` (`AsyncLocalStorage<boolean>`) + `withSkipPrefix(skip, fn)` helper + `userSupplied?: boolean` option on `ResourceNameOptions` in [src/provisioning/resource-name.ts](src/provisioning/resource-name.ts); shared `generateResourceNameWithFallback(userSupplied, logicalId, options)` helper that splits the call into `userSupplied: true` vs `userSupplied: false` branches so each Pattern B provider's `(properties['X'] || logicalId)` shape collapses to one typed call; new `resolveSkipPrefix(cliValue)` in [src/cli/config-loader.ts](src/cli/config-loader.ts) mirrors `resolveCaptureObservedState`'s pattern; deploy CLI wraps `runStack` in `withSkipPrefix(skipPrefix, ...)` so the resolved flag rides into every provider call via `AsyncLocalStorage` (no provider signature changes required). `cdkd destroy` / `state destroy` / `drift` are unaffected — they operate on state-recorded `physicalId`, not on `generateResourceName`. Caveats documented in [docs/cli-reference.md](docs/cli-reference.md) and README: (1) flipping the flag on an existing stack proposes REPLACEMENT on every Pattern B resource because the AWS-deployed name is prefixed and the new template intent is unprefixed; either flip on new stacks or accept the one-time replacement, (2) `cdkd export`'s IMPORT identifier overlay (PR #285) is kept as-is in this PR — pre-existing stacks deployed without the flag still need the overlay; a future PR may drop the overlay after the default flips. Tests: 14 new in [tests/unit/provisioning/resource-name.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/resource-name.test.ts) (every `withSkipPrefix` + `userSupplied` combination + concurrency isolation + the new `generateResourceNameWithFallback` helper), 7 new in [tests/unit/cli/config-loader.test.ts](tests/unit/cli/config-loader.test.ts) (full resolution-chain matrix), 13 new in [tests/unit/provisioning/no-prefix-user-supplied-names.test.ts](tests/unit/provisioning/no-prefix-user-supplied-names.test.ts) (per-provider verification: flag-on → unprefixed Create input; flag-off → prefixed Create input; logical-id fallback → prefixed regardless of flag).
- ✅ CLI: `--app` and `--state-bucket` optional (fallback to env vars / cdk.json)
- ✅ CLI: Positional stack names, `--all` flag, wildcard support, single stack auto-detection
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd destroy` accepts `--app` option; confirmation accepts y/yes
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd list` / `cdkd ls` (CDK CLI parity) — default per-line display path; `--long`, `--show-dependencies`, `--json` for structured output; reuses shared stack-matcher for pattern filtering
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd publish-assets` synth + build + publish (no deploy) — synthesizes the CDK app, selects target stacks via the standard chain (positional > `--stack` > `--all` > auto-detect with `matchStacks` from `src/cli/stack-matcher.ts`), and runs the same `AssetPublisher.addAssetsToGraph(...) → WorkGraph.execute(...)` pipeline that `deploy` uses — but with `stack: 0` concurrency so only `asset-build` / `asset-publish` nodes fire. No state writes, no provisioning, no lock acquisition. Per-stack accounting: a single stack's asset publish failure surfaces as `PartialFailureError` (exit 2) with the rest of the run completing, matching `cdkd destroy`'s exit-code policy. `-a/--app` accepts both a shell command and a path to a pre-synthesized cloud assembly directory (same dual semantics as `cdkd deploy`'s `-a`); pointing it at `cdk.out` skips synthesis. The legacy `--path <manifest>` flag is gone — pre-synthesized assemblies are re-used via `-a <dir>` instead, which keeps the publish-assets surface symmetric with deploy / diff / destroy. `--role-arn` plumbing is gated behind `src/utils/role-arn.ts` (TODO: PR A) — until then the SDK's standard credential chain applies. Implementation in `src/cli/commands/publish-assets.ts`.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke <target>` — run a Lambda function from a CDK app on the developer's machine, inside a Docker container that bundles the AWS Lambda Runtime Interface Emulator (RIE). Modeled on `sam local invoke` but reusing cdkd's synthesis / asset / construct-path plumbing — no `template.yaml` round-trip. **Target syntax**: CDK display path (`MyStack/MyApi/Handler`) or stack-qualified logical ID (`MyStack:MyApiHandler1234ABCD`); single-stack apps may omit the stack prefix (D4, mirrors deploy/destroy auto-detect). Path matching reuses the same prefix rule as `cdkd orphan` so an L2 path resolves to the synthesized L1 child. **Image source** (D1): full Lambda base image `public.ecr.aws/lambda/nodejs:<v>` (~600MB, same artifact AWS runs for container Lambdas), not SAM's `public.ecr.aws/sam/emulation-*` (~150MB) — bigger one-time pull, smaller "works locally / breaks in AWS" surface. **Asset resolution** (D2): reads `Metadata['aws:asset:path']` on each Lambda's CFn resource (the CDK-blessed hint, same source SAM uses) and bind-mounts the unzipped directory at `/var/task` read-only. Inline `Code.ZipFile` Lambdas materialize to a tmpdir using the Handler-implied filename (`index.handler` → `tmpdir/index.js`). **Env vars**: literal values pass through; intrinsic-valued entries (`Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` / `Fn::Sub`) emit a warn and are dropped (rather than substituting garbage); `--env-vars <file>` accepts SAM-shape `{"LogicalId":{"KEY":"VALUE"}}` plus an optional top-level `Parameters` block (D5). **Default synth behavior** (Q2 recommendation C): synth every time; pass `-a cdk.out` to skip synthesis when iterating. **Q1 recommendation B**: `--assume-role <arn>` opt-in flag (off by default — SAM-compatible pass-through of the developer's shell credentials when not set) calls `sts:AssumeRole` and forwards STS-issued temp credentials to the container so the handler runs under the deployed function's narrow execution role. PR 1 takes an explicit ARN; auto-resolution from the template's `Role` property is deferred to PR 2's `--from-state`. **Container lifecycle**: detached `docker run -d --rm` with the RIE port published on `127.0.0.1:<ephemeral>:8080`, `docker logs -f` streamed to user stdout/stderr, `docker rm -f` from a `try`/`finally` (and a SIGINT handler) so ^C cleans up the container in one shot. **Exit codes**: 0 when RIE answered (success or handler-thrown error — Lambda-style; mirrors AWS API behavior), 1 for cdkd-side errors (Docker missing, image pull failed, target not found, RIE unreachable). **v1 scope**: Node.js runtimes only (`nodejs18.x` / `nodejs20.x` / `nodejs22.x`); Python / container Lambdas / Layers / `--from-state` / `cdkd local start-api` deferred to follow-up PRs. **Custom Resources** (`Custom::*`) are explicitly rejected with a hint at the underlying ServiceToken Lambda. Implementation across `src/local-invoke/{lambda-resolver,env-resolver,runtime-image,docker-runner,rie-client}.ts` + `src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts`; integration test at `tests/integration/local-invoke/` runs fully local (Docker required, no AWS deploy).
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` Python runtime support (PR 4 of #224) — `python3.11` / `python3.12` / `python3.13` now resolve to the matching `public.ecr.aws/lambda/python:<v>` base image, which bundles the same RIE binary the Node.js base image uses, so the docker-runner / env-resolver code paths are unchanged. The previously-Node-only runtime map in `src/local-invoke/runtime-image.ts` was generalized into a `Runtime → { image, fileExtension }` table; `resolveRuntimeImage` keeps its existing single-string return shape and a sibling `resolveRuntimeFileExtension(runtime)` surfaces the source-file extension (`.js` / `.py`) needed by the inline-`Code.ZipFile` materializer in `src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts`. The Python `Handler` shape is `<modulePath>.<funcName>` — the same `.`-delimited grammar as Node — so `materializeInlineCode` keeps its single `handler.lastIndexOf('.')` parse and only the file-extension argument changes per runtime. The "deferred to PR 4" branch's error message no longer lists Python as rejected; only `java*` / `dotnet*` / `ruby*` / `go*` / `provided*` stay deferred. Container Lambda (`Code.ImageUri`) / Lambda Layers / `--from-state` (PR 2) / `cdkd local start-api` (PR 5) remain deferred. **Bonus: rie-client readiness fix**: `waitForRieReady` was upgraded from a TCP-only probe to a real HTTP probe (`POST /` with an empty body, treats every response — including 4xx — as "ready" and `ECONNRESET` / `ECONNREFUSED` / `UND_ERR_SOCKET` / abort as "not ready, retry"). Docker's userland port forwarder accepts TCP connections from the host as soon as `docker run -p` binds the port — BEFORE the container's RIE process has actually started its own HTTP listener — so the pre-fix TCP probe declared "ready" prematurely and the very first `invokeRie` call landed during the gap with `TypeError: fetch failed`. The race was more pronounced on the Python base image (the rapid bootstrap path is longer for Python) but live-testing confirmed it existed for Node 20 too — 5/5 cdkd Node integ runs failed before the fix, 5/5 pass after. Integration test at `tests/integration/local-invoke-python/` deploys nothing and exercises `python3.12` end-to-end against the Lambda Python base image (asset-backed handler + env-var override + inline `Code.fromInline`); structurally mirrors `tests/integration/local-invoke/` so the Node and Python integs are interchangeable templates.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd export <stack>` — hand a cdkd-managed stack over to CloudFormation. Mirror of `cdkd import` (AWS → cdkd) in the reverse direction (cdkd → CFn). State-driven (reads cdkd state for physical IDs) + synth (template + logical IDs). Refuses the run if any template resource is in the never-importable set (`Custom::*` AND `AWS::CloudFormation::CustomResource` — the latter is what `new cdk.CustomResource(...)` emits when no `resourceType` is supplied; both are Lambda-backed and CFn rejects them from IMPORT changesets — `AWS::CloudFormation::Stack`, or has no entry in cdkd state) — all-or-nothing by design; destroy the offenders or remove them from the CDK app first. Resolves each resource type's primary identifier property via `cloudformation:DescribeType` (with a hardcoded fallback table in `src/cli/commands/export.ts` covering ~30 single-key types: S3 / IAM / Lambda / DynamoDB / SQS / SNS / Logs / EC2 / Events / API Gateway / etc.). **Composite primary identifiers** (`primaryIdentifier.length > 1`) are supported for `AWS::ApiGateway::Method`, `AWS::ApiGateway::Resource`, `AWS::EC2::VPCGatewayAttachment`, `AWS::ApiGatewayV2::Integration`, `AWS::ApiGatewayV2::Route`, and `AWS::Lambda::Permission` via per-type splitters in `COMPOSITE_ID_SPLITTERS` that map cdkd's provider-defined `physicalId` format (e.g. `restApiId|resourceId|httpMethod`, `IGW|VpcId`) plus the resource's recorded `properties` (for sub-resource types that store only the secondary id in physicalId and rely on `properties.ApiId` / `properties.FunctionName` for the parent key) to the field map CFn expects in `ResourceIdentifier`. Each splitter returns `{ resourceIdentifier, propertiesOverlay? }`: `resourceIdentifier` is sent to CFn's `ResourcesToImport[]` (always complete — every primaryIdentifier field) and `propertiesOverlay` (optional, defaults to the full identifier) narrows what's written into the synth template's `Properties` so AWS-generated id fields that aren't valid Properties of the type (e.g. `IntegrationId`, `RouteId`, Lambda::Permission's `Id`) don't surface as "Encountered unsupported property" at changeset-create time. Other composite types abort with a clear error pointing at where to register a new splitter. **IMPORT-unsupported types** (CFn schema lacks the handlers needed for IMPORT lookup — either `handlers: []` outright, or no `read` / `list` handler so CFn can't look the resource up by identifier) are auto-handled via a pre-delete + phase-2-CREATE dance (closes [issue #307](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/307)): cdkd skips the resource from phase 1, deletes the AWS-side resource between phases via the appropriate SDK call, and lets CFn re-CREATE in phase 2. Currently registered: `AWS::ApiGatewayV2::Stage` (`handlers: []`; HttpApi auto-emits `$default`; pre-delete via `apigatewayv2:DeleteStage`; brief unavailability ~10s, HttpApi endpoint URL unchanged because it embeds ApiId not StageName) and `AWS::IAM::Policy` (`handlers: ['create', 'delete', 'update']`, no `read` / `list` because inline policy attachments have no first-class AWS resource id; CDK L2 grants auto-emit it — ECS Task Execution Role ECR pull policy, Lambda execution role inline policies, etc.; pre-delete via `iam:DeleteRolePolicy` / `DeleteUserPolicy` / `DeleteGroupPolicy` per attachment target — the inline policy is dropped from each Role / User / Group between phases, so any in-flight AWS API call depending on the granted permission fails with `AccessDenied` until CFn re-CREATEs in phase 2). Pass `--no-recreate-import-unsupported` to block instead. Per-type config in `IMPORT_UNSUPPORTED_RECREATABLE_TYPES` + `PRE_DELETE_HANDLERS` in `src/cli/commands/export.ts`. Acquires the stack lock, confirms with the user, issues `CreateChangeSet --change-set-type IMPORT` → `waitUntilChangeSetCreateComplete` → `ExecuteChangeSet` → `waitUntilStackImportComplete`, then deletes cdkd state for the migrated stack. AWS resources are unchanged; the stack is then managed by `cdk deploy` / `aws cloudformation`. **Phase 1 template preprocessing** (required by AWS CFn IMPORT contract; happens automatically): (a) Outputs are stripped entirely — CFn rejects ANY Outputs in an IMPORT changeset with "you cannot modify or add [Outputs]"; phase 2 UPDATE re-submits the full synth template and restores Outputs along with the non-importable resources. (b) `DeletionPolicy: Delete` is injected on every resource lacking the attribute — CFn IMPORT requires `DeletionPolicy` on every imported resource, and CDK synth only emits it when the user explicitly sets `RemovalPolicy`. cdkd injects `Delete` (not `Retain`) so the post-export CFn template matches the CFn type-default — same as what plain CFn would have applied for a resource without explicit `RemovalPolicy`. The user sees no surprising `Retain` attribute and the post-export `cdk diff` has no DeletionPolicy noise. `UpdateReplacePolicy` is intentionally NOT injected — only `DeletionPolicy` is required for IMPORT. (c) Each resource's `Properties` is overlaid with cdkd's `ResourceIdentifier` map **only when synth already carries a literal-string value for that field AND it differs from `ResourceIdentifier`** (= pre-v0.94.0 prefix-on-user-declared-name legacy case). For auto-generated names (Properties absent) and composite-id intrinsics (`{Ref: ...}` / `{Fn::GetAtt: ...}`) the overlay is skipped — matching upstream `cdk import` behavior, which submits the synth template untouched and identifies AWS resources via `ResourcesToImport[].ResourceIdentifier` alone.
