In multi-stack runs (`--all` / wildcard) the protected stacks count as per-stack failures and contribute to the aggregated `PartialFailureError` exit code 2 — sibling unprotected stacks still destroy in the same run. **`cdkd state destroy` (state-only, no synth) does NOT honor `terminationProtection`** because the flag is a CDK property surfaced via synth and is not stored in cdkd's state.json — `cdkd state destroy` is the explicit "I know what I'm doing, ignore CDK guards" escape hatch when synth is unavailable. `cdkd diff` (read-only) and `cdkd deploy` (forward-only) are unaffected. A future `--remove-protection` flag (separate scope) will provide an explicit one-shot bypass without editing CDK code. Implementation: [src/synthesis/assembly-reader.ts](src/synthesis/assembly-reader.ts) (extract from manifest properties), [src/cli/commands/destroy.ts](src/cli/commands/destroy.ts) (per-stack guard before `runDestroyForStack`), [src/utils/error-handler.ts](src/utils/error-handler.ts) (`StackTerminationProtectionError`); 3 new unit tests in `tests/unit/cli/destroy.test.ts` covering single-protected refusal / unprotected-still-flows / mixed `--all` partial-failure aggregation, plus a `tests/unit/synthesis/assembly-reader.test.ts` propagation test.
- ✅ `cdkd destroy --remove-protection` / `cdkd state destroy --remove-protection` — explicit one-shot bypass for AWS deletion-protection flags so users don't have to edit CDK code + redeploy or reach for the AWS console. Covers stack-level `terminationProtection` (the just-added gate from PR #204 — the bypass logs a WARN line naming the stack and proceeds) AND resource-level protection on **eight** AWS types: `AWS::Logs::LogGroup` (`DeletionProtectionEnabled` via `PutLogGroupDeletionProtection`), `AWS::RDS::DBInstance` + `AWS::RDS::DBCluster` (`DeletionProtection` via `ModifyDBInstance` / `ModifyDBCluster` with `ApplyImmediately: true`), `AWS::DynamoDB::Table` (`DeletionProtectionEnabled` via `UpdateTable` then `DescribeTable` poll until `ACTIVE`), `AWS::EC2::Instance` (`DisableApiTermination` via `ModifyInstanceAttribute`), `AWS::ElasticLoadBalancingV2::LoadBalancer` (attribute `deletion_protection.enabled` via `ModifyLoadBalancerAttributes`), `AWS::Cognito::UserPool` (string-valued `DeletionProtection` enum `'ACTIVE' | 'INACTIVE'` via `UpdateUserPool`), `AWS::AutoScaling::AutoScalingGroup` (string-valued `DeletionProtection` enum `'none' | 'prevent-force-deletion' | 'prevent-all-deletion'` via `UpdateAutoScalingGroup` followed by `DeleteAutoScalingGroup(ForceDelete=true)` so AWS terminates running instances as part of the delete). The flag plumbs through to each provider's `delete()` method via a new `DeleteContext.removeProtection?: boolean` field (in `src/provisioning/region-check.ts`); the destroy-runner sets it on every per-resource delete when the CLI flag is present. Each protection-bearing provider issues the flip-off call **idempotently** when `removeProtection === true` (AWS accepts the no-op already-disabled case without error); flip-off failures are logged at debug and the actual delete still runs. **RDS + Cognito gating change** (BREAKING): prior to this flag, the RDS DBInstance / DBCluster providers always issued `ModifyDB{Instance,Cluster}(DeletionProtection: false)` before destroy, and the Cognito UserPool provider always issued `DescribeUserPool` + (if `ACTIVE`) `UpdateUserPool(DeletionProtection='INACTIVE')` before destroy; both implicit behaviors are now gated on `--remove-protection` to match the other types — destroying an RDS or Cognito UserPool resource whose deletion protection was set externally without the flag will now surface AWS's `InvalidParameterCombination` / `InvalidParameterException` error. ASG is purely additive (no pre-existing bypass); ditto Logs / DynamoDB / EC2 / ELBv2. The interactive confirm prompt is updated when the flag is set: `About to destroy N resources from stack "X", REMOVING DELETION PROTECTION on K of them. Continue? (y/N)` (default flips from `Y/n` to `y/N` so the destructive bypass needs an explicit `y`); `--yes` / `-y` / `-f` skips it. The protection-bearing-resource counter (`countProtectedResources` in `src/cli/commands/destroy-runner.ts`) walks `properties` + `observedProperties` for the per-type protection field; for string-valued enums (Cognito / ASG) the counter consults `PROTECTION_ACTIVE_VALUES_BY_TYPE` to know which enum values count as "currently protected" (`'ACTIVE'` for Cognito; `'prevent-force-deletion'` / `'prevent-all-deletion'` for ASG). Per-PR-level by design — a single `--remove-protection` covers every supported type; there is no per-type variant. Implementation: [src/cli/options.ts](src/cli/options.ts) (CLI flag), [src/cli/commands/destroy.ts](src/cli/commands/destroy.ts) + [src/cli/commands/state.ts](src/cli/commands/state.ts) (terminationProtection bypass + plumb-through), [src/cli/commands/destroy-runner.ts](src/cli/commands/destroy-runner.ts) (`removeProtection` ctx + confirm prompt + counter + string-enum support), [src/provisioning/region-check.ts](src/provisioning/region-check.ts) (`DeleteContext.removeProtection` field), per-provider flip-off in [logs-loggroup-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/logs-loggroup-provider.ts) / [rds-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/rds-provider.ts) / [dynamodb-table-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/dynamodb-table-provider.ts) / [ec2-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/ec2-provider.ts) / [elbv2-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/elbv2-provider.ts) / [cognito-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/cognito-provider.ts) / [asg-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/asg-provider.ts) (newly-introduced SDK provider for `AWS::AutoScaling::AutoScalingGroup` covering create / update / delete / getAttribute / readCurrentState / getDriftUnknownPaths). Tests across `tests/unit/provisioning/remove-protection.test.ts` (24 — 3 per provider type × 8 types) + `tests/unit/provisioning/asg-provider-roundtrip.test.ts` (provider-level coverage) + `tests/unit/provisioning/cognito-provider.test.ts` (3 existing tests rewritten for the new gating semantics) + `tests/unit/cli/destroy.test.ts` (1 termination-protection bypass) + `tests/unit/cli/state-destroy.test.ts` (2 plumb-through) + `tests/unit/cli/destroy-runner-count-protected.test.ts` (12 counter cases — adds Cognito ACTIVE/INACTIVE + ASG `none` / `prevent-force-deletion` / `prevent-all-deletion`).
- ✅ SDK providers for `AWS::DocDB::*` (DBCluster / DBInstance / DBSubnetGroup) + `AWS::Neptune::*` (DBCluster / DBInstance / DBSubnetGroup). Both APIs are RDS-shaped (`Modify*Cluster` / `Modify*Instance` / `Describe*` / `Delete*`); the new providers in [src/provisioning/providers/docdb-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/docdb-provider.ts) and [src/provisioning/providers/neptune-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/neptune-provider.ts) mirror the structural pattern of `RDSProvider` covering create / update / delete / getAttribute / readCurrentState / getDriftUnknownPaths / handledProperties. Pre-PR these types fell through to CC API which provided basic CRUD but couldn't reach `--remove-protection`'s flip-off path; per `feedback_dedicated_provider_over_special_case.md` the consistent fix is dedicated SDK providers (not a CC-API special-case). `--remove-protection` is wired on the cluster types via the same gating pattern as RDS — `DocDBProvider.deleteCluster` / `NeptuneProvider.deleteCluster` / `NeptuneProvider.deleteInstance` issue `Modify*(DeletionProtection: false, ApplyImmediately: true)` ONLY when `context?.removeProtection === true`. **DocDB DBInstance does NOT support `DeletionProtection`** (verified against `@aws-sdk/client-docdb` types — `CreateDBInstanceMessage` / `ModifyDBInstanceMessage` / `DBInstance` shapes have no `DeletionProtection` field), so `--remove-protection` is a documented no-op for that one type and `handledProperties['AWS::DocDB::DBInstance']` does not list the field; Neptune (cluster + instance) supports it on both shapes. `countProtectedResources` in [src/cli/commands/destroy-runner.ts](src/cli/commands/destroy-runner.ts) extends `PROTECTION_PROPERTY_BY_TYPE` with three new entries (`AWS::DocDB::DBCluster` / `AWS::Neptune::DBCluster` / `AWS::Neptune::DBInstance` — all boolean `DeletionProtection`). Deps: `@aws-sdk/client-docdb` + `@aws-sdk/client-neptune` added to [package.json](package.json). Tests: 16 docdb-roundtrip + 15 neptune-roundtrip + 10 cases extending `tests/unit/provisioning/remove-protection.test.ts` (4 DocDB cluster / 1 DocDB instance no-op / 3 Neptune cluster / 3 Neptune instance) + 4 cases extending `tests/unit/cli/destroy-runner-count-protected.test.ts`. Docs: [docs/supported-resources.md](docs/supported-resources.md) (6 new SDK provider rows), [docs/import.md](docs/import.md) (6 new entries), [docs/cli-reference.md](docs/cli-reference.md) (3 bypass-call signatures), [README.md](README.md) (3 new protection-table rows).
- ✅ CLI parser auto-lowers `--resource-warn-after` when `--resource-timeout` is set below the 5m default. Pre-fix: `cdkd destroy --resource-timeout 2m` (without an explicit `--resource-warn-after`) failed every per-resource call at runtime with `InvalidResourceDeadlineError: warnAfterMs (300000ms) must be less than timeoutMs (120000ms)` because the default warn-after (5m) stayed > the user-shortened timeout (2m). Post-fix: [src/cli/options.ts](src/cli/options.ts) `validateAndAutoLowerWarnAfter` walks the resolved global / per-type pairs after both flags parse, and (1) when only the timeout side is user-supplied and the inherited warn would violate `warn < timeout`, auto-lowers warn to `min(5m, 0.5 * timeout)` and emits a `logger.warn(...)` line so the user sees what cdkd did; (2) when the user explicitly set BOTH sides with `warn ≥ timeout` (a hard user error), exits at parse time with a clear message naming the offending TYPE (or "global"). Documented in the `--resource-timeout` option help string and [docs/cli-reference.md](docs/cli-reference.md). The runtime `withResourceDeadline` validator in [src/deployment/resource-deadline.ts](src/deployment/resource-deadline.ts) stays unchanged as the load-bearing guarantee — the new parser-level check is a UX layer above it. Memory entry `feedback_resource_timeout_warn_after_relation.md` documents the trap for future fixture / CLI work.
- ✅ Real-AWS integ + bug fix: `AWS::EC2::LaunchTemplate.LatestVersionNumber` `Fn::GetAtt` resolution. Closes the only end-to-end gap left by PR #205 — before this PR no fixture exercised `--remove-protection` against actually-protected resources on AWS, and the new `AWS::AutoScaling::AutoScalingGroup` SDK provider had never been deployed. New `tests/integration/remove-protection/` deploys 6 protected resources (Logs LG / DDB Table / Cognito UserPool / EC2 Instance / ELBv2 ALB / ASG with `desiredCapacity: 0`) on a 1-VPC + 2-public-subnet layout, then runs the round-trip: deploy → negative `cdkd destroy --force` (expect non-zero — AWS rejects every protected delete) → `cdkd state list` (state preserved) → positive `cdkd destroy --remove-protection --force` (every flip-off + delete succeeds) → `cdkd state list` (state cleared). Step 3 uses `--resource-timeout 6m` to fail-fast at the per-resource cap (otherwise default 30 min would block on the Subnet's wait for ENI release that will never come because the EC2 instance is protected); step 5 is wrapped in a 3-attempt retry with 90s sleep between tries because AWS public IP release after `TerminateInstances` is async (5-10 min lag) and cdkd's per-call retry budget caps at ~1 min, so the first attempt sometimes fails on `Network has some mapped public address(es)` blocking IGW detach. The integ caught a real cdkd bug on the first run: cdkd's `IntrinsicFunctionResolver` was returning the LaunchTemplate physical id (`lt-xxx`) for `Fn::GetAtt LatestVersionNumber`, which `CreateAutoScalingGroup` rejects with "Invalid launch template version: either '$Default', '$Latest', or a numeric version are allowed." Fixed in [src/deployment/intrinsic-function-resolver.ts](src/deployment/intrinsic-function-resolver.ts) — `AWS::EC2::LaunchTemplate.LatestVersionNumber` / `DefaultVersionNumber` now resolve via a real `DescribeLaunchTemplates` SDK call (returns the integer as a string for AWS-SDK consumption), with a `'$Latest'` / `'$Default'` fallback when the SDK call fails (both are AWS-accepted special values, far safer than the resource-id physicalId fallback). [src/provisioning/providers/asg-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/asg-provider.ts) gained a defensive `String(lt.Version)` coercion at the wire layer for the same field — a numeric value would also fail AWS's strict-string validation. 4 new unit tests (3 in `tests/unit/deployment/intrinsic-functions.test.ts` for the new resolver path + 1 in `tests/unit/provisioning/asg-provider-roundtrip.test.ts` for the coercion). Known follow-up: cdkd's `EC2Provider.deleteInternetGateway` / `deleteVpcGatewayAttachment` retry budget should be lifted to ~10 min so `--remove-protection` destroys are self-healing on the public-IP release lag without operator intervention; the integ's step-5 retry loop is the tactical workaround until that lands.
- ✅ Extended `DependencyViolation` retry budget on `EC2Provider.deleteInternetGateway` + `deleteVpcGatewayAttachment` to 10 min total via a new in-provider helper `withDependencyViolationRetry` (5s initial → 60s cap exponential backoff). Self-heals `cdkd destroy --remove-protection` against AWS's asynchronous public-IP-allocation release after `TerminateInstances` (5–10 min lag observed in practice), where the public IP stays mapped to the VPC's IGW and AWS rejects `DeleteInternetGateway` / `DetachInternetGateway` with `DependencyViolation: Network has some mapped public address(es). Please unmap those public address(es) before detaching the gateway.` cdkd's existing `withRetry` (`src/deployment/retry.ts`) caps at ~1 min total budget (1s/2s/4s/8s × 10 attempts capped at 8s), and the destroy-runner's inner 3-attempt loop adds ~35s — neither is enough for AWS's 5–10 min release window. The helper only retries `DependencyViolation` errors (matched by `Code` / `name` / message-substring); every other error class (NotFound, AccessDenied, throttle, etc.) propagates immediately so the existing `isNotFoundError` idempotency path and `ProvisioningError` wrapping are unchanged. Modeled on the Lambda hyperplane ENI cleanup (~30 min budget) and EC2 Subnet/SG side-channel ENI retry patterns. Note on retry layering: `DependencyViolation` is also in `RETRYABLE_ERROR_MESSAGE_PATTERNS` (consumed by `withRetry`) and in the destroy-runner's match list, so after the in-provider 10 min budget exhausts and re-throws, those outer retry loops will see the error and try a few more times — adding at most ~1 min on top, still bounded by the per-resource `--resource-timeout` deadline (default 30 min). Other DependencyViolation-prone EC2 deletes (Subnet / VPC / SecurityGroup) have their own existing retry loops well-tuned for ENI release and are intentionally NOT changed — only IGW + VPCGw wait on the public-IP-allocation lifecycle. The `tests/integration/remove-protection/verify.sh` step-5 3-attempt 90s-sleep retry from PR #206 is now redundant in the common case but **kept** as defense-in-depth (catches edge cases where the AWS lag exceeds 10 min, surfacing as a soft fail rather than hard). Implementation in [src/provisioning/providers/ec2-provider.ts](src/provisioning/providers/ec2-provider.ts); 9 new unit tests in `tests/unit/provisioning/ec2-provider-igw-retry.test.ts` covering retry-until-success / message-variant / non-DependencyViolation propagation / budget exhaustion / not-found idempotency preservation for both target methods.
- ✅ v2 drift coverage push — closes the largest remaining drift / SDK provider gaps in a 7-PR batch landing across v0.61.0 → v0.65.0. (1) **AppSync** ([#210](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/pull/210)): `AWS::AppSync::GraphQLSchema.Definition` round-trips through `graphql-js` `parse(...) → print(...)` so cosmetic SDL diffs (whitespace / comments) no longer fire false drift; `getDriftUnknownPaths` now declares only `'DefinitionS3Location'` (the actual write-only field). (2) **AutoScaling** ([#211](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/pull/211)): `ASGProvider.readCurrentState` + `update()` extended for the 4 complex sub-shapes — `MetricsCollection` (from `EnabledMetrics`), `LifecycleHookSpecificationList` (`DescribeLifecycleHooks`), `TrafficSources` (`DescribeTrafficSources`), `NotificationConfigurations` (`DescribeNotificationConfigurations`). All always-emit `[]` placeholder per PR #145 pattern; `update()` per-sub-shape diff via `EnableMetricsCollection` / `PutLifecycleHook` / `AttachTrafficSources` / `PutNotificationConfiguration` and their Delete counterparts. (3) **Kinesis StreamConsumer + EC2 sub-resource Tags** ([#212](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/pull/212)): new dedicated `KinesisStreamConsumerProvider` (per `feedback_dedicated_provider_over_special_case.md` — replaces CC API fallback; immutable on every property so `update()` rejects with `ResourceUpdateNotSupportedError`); `getDriftUnknownPaths: ['Tags']` since `@aws-sdk/client-kinesis` does not expose a tag API for StreamConsumer. EC2 sub-resources (Route / VPCGatewayAttachment / SubnetRouteTableAssociation / SecurityGroupIngress / NetworkAclEntry / SubnetNetworkAclAssociation) get per-type Tags decision: surfaced when parent `Describe*` response includes them (SubnetRouteTableAssociation / SubnetNetworkAclAssociation), declared via `getDriftUnknownPaths` otherwise. (4) **Glue Workflow + SecurityConfiguration** ([#213](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/pull/213)): 2 dedicated SDK providers extending `glue-provider.ts`. Workflow has full Update path; SecurityConfiguration is immutable (no AWS update API). Both surface readCurrentState with PR #145 always-emit placeholders; SecurityConfiguration's nested `EncryptionConfiguration` (3 sub-configs S3 / CloudWatch / JobBookmarks Encryption) reverse-mapped. (5) **Glue Job / Crawler / Connection / Trigger** ([#214](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/pull/214)): 4 dedicated SDK providers (per the same dedicated-provider-over-CC-API rule). Job / Crawler / Connection are standard CRUD via Create / Update / Delete / Get. **Trigger has a state-machine** — `UpdateTrigger` requires DEACTIVATED, so when state was ACTIVATED the update flow auto-issues `StopTrigger → UpdateTrigger → StartTrigger` to preserve the ACTIVATED state across update. Crawler additionally manages `Schedule` via `StartCrawlerSchedule` / `StopCrawlerSchedule`. (6) **S3 Bucket 12 sub-configs** ([#215](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/pull/215)): closes the largest single drift gap. `LifecycleConfiguration` / `CorsConfiguration` / `WebsiteConfiguration` / `LoggingConfiguration` / `NotificationConfiguration` / `ReplicationConfiguration` / `ObjectLockConfiguration` / `AccelerateConfiguration` (object-shaped) + `MetricsConfigurations[]` / `AnalyticsConfigurations[]` / `IntelligentTieringConfigurations[]` / `InventoryConfigurations[]` (array-shaped, per-id diff via `diffArrayConfigById` helper) all wired through `Get*` (or `List*` paginated for arrays) on read and `Put*` / `Delete*` on update. Always-emit placeholders: `{}` for object-shaped, `[]` for array-shaped, `'Suspended'` for `AccelerateConfiguration.AccelerationStatus`. All 12 added to `handledProperties['AWS::S3::Bucket']` so the deploy engine routes through the SDK provider instead of CC API. (7) **DocDB / Neptune integ test** ([#216](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/pull/216)): real-AWS integ fixture for the providers added in PR #207 (DocDB / Neptune SDK providers). Deploys 1 VPC + 2 private subnets + DocDB cluster + DocDB instance + Neptune cluster + Neptune instance (db.t3.medium, ~$0.07 / run). Per-type 20-min timeouts override the 30-min default since cluster + instance create / delete each take 5-10 min on AWS. Total runtime 25-40 min per round-trip; cleanup trap re-attempts destroy on any failure exit so a botched run does not bill indefinitely.
- ✅ Refactor: `src/local-invoke/` → `src/local/` directory rename (PR 3 of #224). Independent small PR ahead of `cdkd local start-api` (PR 5) — the new directory will host both `cdkd local invoke`'s building blocks AND the upcoming `start-api` server / container-pool modules, so the file-system shape mirrors the `cdkd local *` CLI family. Pure rename: `git mv src/local-invoke src/local` + `git mv tests/unit/local-invoke tests/unit/local` + every `from '../local-invoke/...'` import rewritten to `from '../local/...'`. Integration test directory names (`tests/integration/local-invoke{,-python,-from-state}/`) stay unchanged — those are user-facing test names referenced by `/run-integ` and renaming them would break that surface unrelated to the source-path concern. PR 1 / PR 2 / PR 4's "Recently Implemented" bullets keep their historical `src/local-invoke/...` prose unchanged; only the directory description at the top of "Important Files" and PR 2's clickable file links were updated.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` container Lambda support (PR 5 of #224) — `lambda.DockerImageFunction(...)` / `Code.ImageUri` is now invocable alongside ZIP Lambdas. **Detection** (D5.5): the resolver branches on `Code.ImageUri !== undefined` (extracted from the `Fn::Sub`-shape entry CDK actually synthesizes — critical bug fix C1; the pre-review draft assumed a flat string). When detected, `Runtime` / `Handler` are NOT required (AWS contract: container Lambdas don't have a Handler property — invocation is driven by `ImageConfig.Command` or the image's own CMD). **Local-build path** (D5.1, default): cdkd extracts the asset hash from the `:<hash>` tail of the image URI, looks the matching `manifest.dockerImages[<hash>]` entry up in `cdk.out/<stack>.assets.json`, and runs `docker build` against the recorded build context. When the lookup misses AND the manifest contains exactly one Docker asset, that single asset is used (single-asset fallback — covers digest-pinned URIs that have no extractable hash). The shared build helper lives at `src/assets/docker-build.ts` (extracted from `docker-asset-publisher.ts:buildImage` per D5.4) so both `cdkd publish-assets` / `cdkd deploy` and the local-invoke path go through one code path; invariants preserved: `maxBuffer: 50 * 1024 * 1024`, `Object.entries`-stable build-arg iteration order, parameterized `wrapError` so each consumer wraps with its own typed error class (`AssetError` for the publisher, the new `LocalInvokeBuildError` for local-invoke). **ECR pull fallback** (D5.2): when no asset matches AND the URI is an ECR shape, cdkd verifies same-account / same-region against STS `GetCallerIdentity`, calls `ecrLogin` (mirrors `DockerAssetPublisher.ecrLogin` — same `GetAuthorizationToken` + `docker login --password-stdin` pattern), then `docker pull <uri>`. Cross-account / cross-region URIs hard-error with a clear "deferred to follow-up PR" message naming the offending account / region pair. **`Architectures` honored** (D5.6, critical bug fix C2): `Architectures: [x86_64]` (default) or `[arm64]` is threaded through to `--platform linux/amd64` / `linux/arm64` on BOTH `docker build` AND `docker run`, so an arm64 host running an x86_64 Lambda doesn't hit emulation and an x86_64 host running arm64 doesn't fail with `exec format error`. **`ImageConfig` mapping**: `Command` → docker run CMD args; `EntryPoint` → `--entrypoint <first>` plus the rest as positional args before CMD; `WorkingDirectory` → `--workdir`. When `EntryPoint` is unset (the common case), the image's default entrypoint stays in charge — for AWS Lambda base images that's `/lambda-entrypoint.sh`, which routes to RIE on port 8080. **`--no-pull` semantics differ by code path** (critical bug fix C3): ZIP → skip the public-base `docker pull`; IMAGE local-build → no-op (docker build's default doesn't refresh the FROM cache); IMAGE ECR-pull → skip the pull AND error if the image isn't in the local cache (`docker image inspect` is the verifier). **Discriminated union** (D5.3): `ResolvedLambda` is now `ResolvedZipLambda | ResolvedImageLambda` keyed off `kind: 'zip' | 'image'`; the `Properties.Environment.Variables` resolution / state-resolver / `--from-state` paths are shared on the base interface. **Out of scope** (deferred to follow-up PRs): cross-account / cross-region ECR pull, `EphemeralStorage` mapping (`--tmpfs /tmp:size=Nm`), `--no-build` flag, Lambda Layers (not applicable on container Lambdas — layers are baked at build time). Implementation across `src/assets/docker-build.ts` (NEW, extracted helper) + `src/assets/asset-manifest-loader.ts` (`getDockerImageBySourceHash`) + `src/local/docker-image-builder.ts` (NEW, local-build wrapper with stable cache-friendly tag) + `src/local/ecr-puller.ts` (NEW, same-acct/region only) + `src/local/docker-runner.ts` (extended `runDetached` for `--platform` / `--entrypoint` / `--workdir`) + `src/local/lambda-resolver.ts` (discriminated union, `Fn::Sub`-aware ImageUri extraction, `Architectures` parsing) + `src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts` (`resolveImagePlan` branches on `kind`); 20 new unit tests across `tests/unit/local/{docker-image-builder,ecr-puller,lambda-resolver}.test.ts` + `tests/unit/assets/{docker-build,asset-manifest-loader}.test.ts`; real-Docker (no AWS deploy) integ at `tests/integration/local-invoke-container/` covers the local-build path end-to-end with `lambda.DockerImageFunction` over a minimal Dockerfile.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke --from-state` (PR 2 of #224) — closes the "intrinsic-valued env vars are dropped" gap that PR 1 left explicit. When `--from-state` is set, cdkd reads its S3 state for the target stack and substitutes `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` / `Fn::Sub` placeholders in the function's `Properties.Environment.Variables` with the deployed physical IDs / attributes recorded by `cdkd deploy`. Off by default — PR 1's literal-only / warn-and-drop semantics are preserved when the flag is not set. **Resolution priority** (highest wins): `--env-vars` function-specific entry → `--env-vars` global `Parameters` → `--from-state` substituted intrinsic → template literal. Per-key best-effort: when state is missing for a referenced logical ID, the attribute wasn't captured at deploy time, or the intrinsic isn't one of the three supported (`Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` / `Fn::Sub`), the key is dropped with a warn (matches PR 1 UX) — never aborts the whole invoke. State load failures (no state record, multi-region ambiguity without `--stack-region`, bucket resolution error) also degrade to warn-and-fall-back rather than hard-fail. **Q1 follow-up**: when `--from-state` is set without `--assume-role`, cdkd peeks at the function's `Role` property in state and logs a one-line hint surfacing the deployed execution role's ARN (`Re-run with --assume-role <that-arn> to invoke under the deployed function's narrow permissions`). Auto-assumption is intentionally NOT wired in — that's a future PR's scope; v1 keeps the user's explicit ARN as the only path to scoped credentials. **Out of scope** (deferred): cross-stack `Fn::ImportValue` / `Fn::GetStackOutput`, pseudo parameters (`AWS::Region`, etc.), other intrinsics (`Fn::Join`, `Fn::Select`, `Fn::Split`, etc.). State options follow the standard set: `--state-bucket` / `--state-prefix` / `--stack-region` (the last only used when the same stack name has state in multiple regions). Implementation: new pure-functional substituter at [src/local/state-resolver.ts](src/local/state-resolver.ts) (no AWS SDK calls, fully unit-testable) + state-load helper in [src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts](src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts) mirrors the orphan command's read-only state-loading pattern. 20 unit tests at `tests/unit/local/state-resolver.test.ts`; real-AWS integ at `tests/integration/local-invoke-from-state/` (deploy a Lambda + S3 Bucket, verify PR 1 baseline drops `BUCKET_NAME`, verify PR 2 substitutes the deployed bucket name, then destroy).
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke --no-build` for container Lambdas (closes #233) — skips `docker build` on the IMAGE local-build path (`Code.ImageUri`) and reuses the deterministic `cdkd-local-invoke-<sha-of-source-dir>` tag from a prior `cdkd local invoke` (or manual `docker build`). The local tag is fingerprinted from `directory + dockerFile + dockerBuildTarget + dockerBuildArgs` (already stable since PR 5 of #224), so a subsequent `--no-build` run hits the same tag the first run produced. Verifier shape: `docker image inspect <tag>` — same one-liner the ECR-pull `--no-pull` path uses, factored into a shared `isImageInLocalCache(imageRef): boolean` helper in [src/local/ecr-puller.ts](src/local/ecr-puller.ts) so both verifiers stay in sync. **Per-path semantics** (matches `--no-pull`'s split): IMAGE local-build → skip `docker build`, error with `image '<tag>' not in local registry and --no-build is set; remove --no-build or run docker build manually first.` when the tag is missing; IMAGE ECR-pull → no-op (use `--no-pull` to control that path); ZIP Lambdas → no-op (no `docker build` runs there). Compatible with `--no-pull` (each flag controls a distinct subprocess; setting both is sensible and skips both). Implementation: [src/local/docker-image-builder.ts](src/local/docker-image-builder.ts) (new optional `noBuild: boolean` on `BuildContainerImageOptions`) + [src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts](src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts) (new `--no-build` Commander Option, plumbed through `resolveContainerImagePlan` to the local-build branch). 4 new unit tests in `tests/unit/local/docker-image-builder.test.ts` (happy / cache-miss / tag-stability) + 3 new tests in `tests/unit/cli/local-invoke-resolve-plan.test.ts` (asset-hit threads through / default builds / ECR-pull path no-op); 4th case added to `tests/integration/local-invoke-container/verify.sh` (after the 3 existing cases populate the cache, run with `--no-build` and assert stderr contains "Skipping docker build" and NOT "Building container image").
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local start-api` authorizers + VPC simulation (PR 8b of #224, closes #234) — extends the PR 8a server with full authorizer support and a startup warning for VPC-config Lambdas. **Authorizer kinds**: (1) **Lambda TOKEN** (REST v1, `AWS::ApiGateway::Authorizer.Type === 'TOKEN'`): the header named in `IdentitySource` (default `method.request.header.Authorization`) is forwarded to the authorizer Lambda as `event.authorizationToken`; the Lambda's IAM-policy response is parsed by a literal-or-glob `Resource` matcher (`*`/`?` supported) against the request's methodArn (`arn:aws:execute-api:local:123456789012:local/<stage>/<METHOD>/<path>`); Allow → context flat under `event.requestContext.authorizer`, Deny → HTTP 403, missing header → HTTP 401 without invoking the Lambda. (2) **Lambda REQUEST** (REST v1 + HTTP v2): full request snapshot (headers, query string, path parameters) sent as the authorizer event; HTTP v2 also accepts the simple `{ isAuthorized, context }` response shape; REST v1 missing-identity → HTTP 401 without invoking the Lambda. Allow → context under `event.requestContext.authorizer.lambda` (v2) or `event.requestContext.authorizer` (v1). (3) **Cognito User Pool** (REST v1): Bearer JWT verified locally via `cognito-idp.<region>.amazonaws.com/<pool-id>/.well-known/jwks.json` JWKS; signature (RS256), `exp`, `iss` checked. Allow → claims under `event.requestContext.authorizer.claims`. (4) **JWT** (HTTP v2, `AuthorizerType: 'JWT'`): same JWKS-based verify, with `aud` / `client_id` matched against `JwtConfiguration.Audience` allowlist. Allow → claims under `event.requestContext.authorizer.jwt.claims`. **Authorizer-result cache**: per `(authorizer, identity)` TTL — REST v1 `AuthorizerResultTtlInSeconds` (default 300s, max 3600s); HTTP v2 default 0s (no cache); JWT cached for `min(remaining-exp, 300s)`. Implemented in `src/local/authorizer-cache.ts` (lazy expiry on get). The cache stores the **authorizer's verdict shape** (principalId / policyDocument / context for Lambda; claims for JWT/Cognito) keyed by `(authorizerLogicalId, identityHash)`; on cache hits the IAM `Resource` is re-evaluated against the current request's methodArn so a narrow-Resource policy doesn't leak across routes. **JWKS-fetch failure → pass-through**: when the JWKS endpoint is unreachable at startup, cdkd warns and falls back to a mode where every JWT is accepted as if valid — local-dev fallback for corporate-proxy environments. The behavior is documented in `cdkd local start-api --help`, the README, and `docs/cli-reference.md` so users aren't surprised. **VPC simulation**: VPC-config Lambdas (`Properties.VpcConfig` set) still run locally — cdkd does NOT block them — but the local container is NOT attached to the deployed VPC's subnets. cdkd surfaces a one-line warn at startup naming each affected Lambda; AWS SDK calls still reach public AWS endpoints via the dev's network as usual. **Out of scope (deferred)**: REST v1 IAM authorizers (`AuthorizationType: 'AWS_IAM'`), mTLS authorizers — both hard-errored at discovery with a "deferred follow-up PR" pointer. CORS preflight / hot reload / stage variables / `--from-state` env vars stay deferred to PR 8c. Implementation across `src/local/authorizer-resolver.ts` (NEW — REST v1 + HTTP v2 detection, identity-source parsing, `buildIdentityHash` shared helper), `src/local/authorizer-cache.ts` (NEW — TTL-aware cache), `src/local/lambda-authorizer.ts` (NEW — TOKEN + REQUEST invoke + IAM-policy parser with wildcard `Resource` matching, `extractIdentityValue` / `computeRequestIdentityHash` / `evaluateCachedLambdaPolicy` exposed for the http-server pre-cache pre-compute + Resource re-eval path), `src/local/cognito-jwt.ts` (NEW — JWKS fetch with 1hr success TTL / 60s failure TTL, RS256 verify via Node's `crypto.createPublicKey({format:'jwk'})`, claims extraction, pass-through fallback), `src/local/api-gateway-event.ts` (`applyAuthorizerOverlay` per kind), `src/local/http-server.ts` (per-request authorizer pass before container acquire; rejection writes 401 for missing-identity / 403 for explicit policy-deny on REST v1, 401 across the board on HTTP v2), `src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts` (JWKS prefetch at startup, VPC-config warn loop, authorizer Lambdas added to the container-pool spec map, single `Set<string>` constructed once at server startup so the JWKS pass-through warn fires at most once per JWKS URL per server lifecycle). New unit tests across `tests/unit/local/{authorizer-resolver,authorizer-cache,lambda-authorizer,cognito-jwt,api-gateway-event,http-server}.test.ts` covering REQUEST cache reuse, narrow-Resource per-request re-evaluation, missing-Effect deny, extractBearer edge cases, JWKS HTTP-error / TTL / failure-short-TTL paths, and `writeAuthRejection`'s 401/403 differentiation. Integration test at `tests/integration/local-start-api/` extended with a Lambda REQUEST authorizer-protected `/protected` route — verify.sh asserts both the deny path (no Bearer → 401) and the allow path (`Authorization: Bearer let-me-in` → 200 + protected handler echo of authorizer context).
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` Lambda Layers support (PR 6 of #224, issue #232) — same-stack `AWS::Lambda::LayerVersion` references in `Properties.Layers` are resolved automatically and bind-mounted at `/opt` (read-only) inside the container. The flow: `lambda-resolver.resolveLambdaLayers(...)` walks `Properties.Layers` left-to-right, accepts `{Ref: '<LayerLogicalId>'}` and `{Fn::GetAtt: ['<LayerLogicalId>', 'Ref']}` shapes pointing at a same-stack `AWS::Lambda::LayerVersion`, and reads each layer's `Metadata['aws:asset:path']` to locate the unzipped asset directory under `cdk.out`. The resolved `ResolvedLambdaLayer[]` rides on the shared `ResolvedLambdaBase` so both `cdkd local invoke` and `cdkd local start-api` (via `container-pool.ts`) get layer support. **Order is load-bearing** — AWS layer semantics are "last layer wins on file collision". **Implementation: merge-into-tmpdir, not multiple bind mounts**: integ-testing hit `Error response from daemon: Duplicate mount point: /opt` — Docker rejects two `-v ...:/opt:ro` entries at the same target (bind mounts are NOT layered the way the OCI image stack is). cdkd mirrors AWS's actual runtime behavior (extract every layer ZIP into `/opt` IN ORDER) on the host: single-layer functions bind-mount the layer's asset dir directly (no copy); multi-layer functions get a freshly-merged tmpdir via `cpSync({recursive: true, force: true})` over each layer in template order, then bind-mount the merged tmpdir at `/opt`. The merged tmpdir is recorded in `ImagePlan.layersTmpDir` (`cdkd local invoke`) or `layerTmpDirs: Set<string>` (`cdkd local start-api`'s long-running server) so the cleanup path can `rmSync` it; single-layer mounts are not tmpdirs and are not cleaned up. The `docker-runner.ts` got an `extraMounts: { hostPath; containerPath; readOnly? }[]` field on `runDetached` for composing additional mounts beyond `/var/task` — used both by layer-merge and by future per-Lambda mount needs. **Out of scope** (hard-errors with a clear pointer at the offending entry): cross-stack / cross-account / cross-region literal-ARN entries (`arn:aws:lambda:...`), refs that don't point at an `AWS::Lambda::LayerVersion` (typo'd logical ID), and same-stack refs to a `LayerVersion` whose `Metadata['aws:asset:path']` is missing (no local directory to mount). **Container Lambdas (`Code.ImageUri`) silently ignore `Layers`** — matches AWS's invoke-time behavior (AWS rejects `Layers` on container images at deploy time). Implementation: [src/local/lambda-resolver.ts](src/local/lambda-resolver.ts) (new `ResolvedLambdaLayer` type + `resolveLambdaLayers` exported helper), [src/local/docker-runner.ts](src/local/docker-runner.ts) (`extraMounts` field), [src/local/container-pool.ts](src/local/container-pool.ts) (`ContainerSpec.optDir` field — pre-resolved `/opt` bind-mount source per Lambda, so the warm-pool start path emits one mount per cold-start instead of merging on every request), [src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts](src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts) (`materializeLambdaLayers` helper + `ImagePlan.layersTmpDir` + the entire command body wrapped in a single try/finally with a hoisted `cleanup()` helper called from BOTH the outer `finally` AND the SIGINT handler — pre-review-fix the SIGINT path called `removeContainer` but skipped the tmpdir `rmSync`, leaking the merged-layers tmpdir on every ^C; pre-fix a failure between `mkdtempSync`/`cpSync` in `resolveZipImagePlan` and the docker-run call site also unwound past the per-block finally), [src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts](src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts) (`resolveLambdaByLogicalId` populates `layers`; `materializeLambdaLayers` per-Lambda at server boot; `layerTmpDirs` set drained in the graceful-shutdown path). 23 new unit tests across `tests/unit/local/{lambda-resolver,docker-runner,container-pool}.test.ts` + `tests/unit/cli/local-invoke-layers.test.ts` (covering the merge-on-host last-wins semantics, single-layer bind-mount-direct optimization, cleanup contract, and `ContainerSpec.optDir` propagation through the warm pool) + a real-Docker (no AWS deploy) integ at `tests/integration/local-invoke-layers/` that deploys 1 Lambda + 3 LayerVersions (two of which install the same `nodejs/node_modules/util-greetings/` path) and verifies the handler `require()`s modules from `/opt/nodejs/node_modules/...` AND that the last-declared layer wins on the shared module path.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local start-api` (PR 8a of #224) — long-running local HTTP server that maps API Gateway routes (REST v1 `AWS::ApiGateway::*`, HTTP API `AWS::ApiGatewayV2::*`, Function URL `AWS::Lambda::Url`) to local Lambda invocations against the AWS Lambda Runtime Interface Emulator. Modeled on `sam local start-api` but reusing cdkd's synthesis, asset, and route-discovery plumbing — no `template.yaml` round-trip. **Scope (D8.0)**: AWS_PROXY integrations only; non-AWS_PROXY, ApiGwV2 service integrations (`IntegrationSubtype` set), WebSocket APIs (`ProtocolType: WEBSOCKET`), and Function URLs with `AuthType !== 'NONE'` or `InvokeMode === 'RESPONSE_STREAM'` hard-fail at discovery with the offending route's location named. **Default port (D8.1)**: auto-allocate, printed at startup as `Server listening on http://<host>:<port>` (the load-bearing marker for `verify.sh`); `--port <n>` for SAM parity. **Per-Lambda concurrency (D8.3)**: pool of warm RIE containers per Lambda, default 2 (warm + 1 backup), `--per-lambda-concurrency <n>` raises to max 4. Pool grows lazily under a per-Lambda mutex; idle containers tear down after 60s of inactivity. **`--assume-role` (D8.2)**: extends PR 1's flag to accept both bare `<arn>` (global default) and `<LogicalId>=<arn>` (per-Lambda override) on every invocation; per-Lambda > global > unset (developer creds passed through, SAM-compatible default). **Local intrinsic resolver (C8)**: 30-line resolver in `route-discovery.ts` handles only `Ref`, `Fn::GetAtt: [<X>, 'Arn']`, and the REST v1 invoke-ARN `Fn::Join` wrapper CDK emits; any other intrinsic in `IntegrationUri` / `Target` hard-errors. **Event shape**: HTTP API v2 (used by HTTP API + Function URL) with full `requestContext` (mock `accountId` / `domainPrefix`, explicit `authentication: null` / `authorizer: null`, `cookies` array separated from `headers`, `stageVariables: null`); REST v1 with the legacy multiValueHeaders / identity shape. Header names lowercased + duplicates comma-joined (C14), `cookie` header split into the v2 `cookies` array (C5), `pathParameters` / `queryStringParameters` values `decodeURIComponent`'d while `rawPath` / `rawQueryString` stay raw (C11). **Response translation (C6 / C7)**: shaped (statusCode + body) > Lambda runtime error envelope (`errorMessage` + no statusCode → HTTP 502 with `{"message":"Internal server error"}`) > auto-format any other JSON payload as 200 + `application/json`. v2 `cookies` array → multiple `Set-Cookie:` headers (NOT comma-joined). **Routing precedence (C10)**: 3 tiers per AWS docs (full → greedy `{proxy+}` → `$default`); within "full match" tier, more literal segments wins as a heuristic. **Container lifecycle (D8.5)**: `runDetached` extended to take an optional `--name cdkd-local-<logicalId>-<pid>-<rand>` so the verify.sh trap can sweep orphans (`docker ps --filter name=cdkd-local-`). SIGINT / SIGTERM / uncaughtException / unhandledRejection all run the same dispose path; double-`^C` bypasses dispose and exits 130 immediately. The HTTP server does NOT instantiate `live-renderer` — its `setInterval`-driven repaint loop holds the event loop open and would prevent `process.exit(0)` after graceful shutdown. Implementation across `src/local/{route-discovery,api-gateway-event,api-gateway-response,route-matcher,container-pool,http-server,docker-runner}.ts` + `src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts`. New error classes `RouteDiscoveryError` and `StartApiServerError` in `src/utils/error-handler.ts`. Integration test at `tests/integration/local-start-api/` deploys nothing (HTTP API + REST v1 + Function URL fixture); `verify.sh` boots the server, asserts the route table, curls each route, and shuts down cleanly with a 120s SIGTERM grace + SIGKILL fallback + unconditional `docker ps --filter` orphan sweep. **Out of scope (deferred)**: authorizers (PR 8b), VPC simulation (PR 8b), CORS preflight (PR 8c), hot reload (PR 8c), stage variables (PR 8c — hardcoded `null` in v1), `--from-state`-style env-var substitution (PR 8c), WebSocket APIs (never), per-Lambda concurrency above 4 (raise in 8c if a real workload needs it). **Container-image Lambdas (PR 5 of #224, `Code.ImageUri`) are also rejected by start-api in v1** — `resolveLambdaByLogicalId` short-circuits with a "use cdkd local invoke" hint; threading the per-Lambda image-build / ECR-pull / `--platform` machinery through the warm container pool is non-trivial and deferred to a follow-up PR. **Post-review hardening (review feedback)**: (a) `dispose()` now tracks every in-flight `startOne` in an `inFlightStarts` set and awaits them with a 5s timeout before tearing down, so a SIGINT mid-cold-start doesn't drop the resulting container handle on the floor; pre-fix the dispose-while-startOne race relied solely on the verify.sh `docker rm -f cdkd-local-*` sweep. (b) Inline-`Code.ZipFile` materialization records every `mkdtemp` directory in a server-scoped set; `shutdown` walks that set with `rmSync(..., {recursive:true, force:true})` to prevent compounding tmpdir leaks across long-running server invocations (the original `cdkd local invoke` shape leaked one dir per inline Lambda but was acceptable there because the process exited after one invocation).
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local start-api` hot reload + CORS preflight + stage variables (PR 8c of #224, closes [#235](https://github.com/go-to-k/cdkd/issues/235)) — closes the three big PR 8a deferrals in one PR. **Hot reload (`--watch`)**: opt-in flag installs a [chokidar](https://github.com/paulmillr/chokidar)-backed file watcher over `cdk.out/` plus every routed Lambda's asset directory; a 500ms-debounced change triggers re-synth → re-discover → spec-build → atomic state swap (the `node:http` listener is never re-bound; in-flight requests run against the old container pool while the new pool warms). Synth failures are non-fatal — the previous version keeps serving and a `[warn]` line names the failure. Reload calls serialize via a chained promise so a burst of file events coalesces to one synth. The HTTP server (`src/local/http-server.ts`) was refactored to read state from a closure cell (`currentState: ServerState`) on every request, with `setServerState(next)` swapping atomically and returning the previous state for background disposal. Reload diff: routes added / removed (by `(method, pathPattern, lambdaLogicalId, source, apiVersion)` tuple) + Lambdas whose spec signature (codeDir / env / runtime / handler / debugPort) changed. **CORS preflight**: `buildCorsConfigByApiId` walks the template once at server boot (and on every reload) and produces `apiLogicalId → CorsConfig` for every `AWS::ApiGatewayV2::Api` with a `CorsConfiguration` block; on every OPTIONS request the server reads the `Access-Control-Request-Method` header, finds the route a real request would hit, and (when the matched route is HTTP API v2 + the API has a CORS config + no explicit OPTIONS route is registered) returns `204 No Content` with the canonical `Access-Control-Allow-*` headers via `matchPreflight`. AWS validation rules honored: `*` wildcard for Origin / Methods / Headers; `AllowCredentials: true` echoes the request Origin instead of `*` per the browser fetch spec; `MaxAge` / `ExposeHeaders` surfaced when configured. REST v1 CORS via Mock OPTIONS integration is intentionally NOT intercepted — the discovery layer already rejects Mock integrations at server boot, so REST v1 CORS emulation stays out of scope and uses the deployed API. **Stage variables (`--stage <name>`)**: PR 8a hardcoded `event.stageVariables = null`; PR 8c populates it from the selected Stage's `Variables` (REST v1) / `StageVariables` (HTTP API v2) map. Default selection is the first Stage attached to each API in template order; `--stage <name>` selects a specific Stage by `StageName` (per-API — a `prod` override against a multi-API app picks the matching Stage on each). APIs without a matching Stage get `stageVariables: null` and the CLI surfaces a deduplicated warn line at startup. Function URL routes don't have a Stage. Intrinsic-valued entries in `Variables` (`Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` / `Fn::Sub`) are dropped with a warn (mirrors PR 1's env-var policy — the local server has no deploy state to resolve them against). **Implementation**: 4 new modules — `src/local/file-watcher.ts` (chokidar wrapper with debounce + dynamic `update(paths)`), `src/local/reload-orchestrator.ts` (synth-failure-tolerant reload pipeline with chain-serialized concurrent calls), `src/local/cors-handler.ts` (CFn `CorsConfiguration` parser + canonical preflight matcher), `src/local/stage-resolver.ts` (per-API stage map + `attachStageContext` for routes). `route-discovery.ts` extended with `apiLogicalId?: string` and `stageVariables?: Record<string, string> | null` on `DiscoveredRoute`. `api-gateway-event.ts` reads `route.stageVariables` instead of hardcoding `null`. `http-server.ts` accepts `state: ServerState` and exposes `setServerState` / `getServerState` for the orchestrator. CLI flags: `--watch` (off by default; opt-in) + `--stage <name>` (default first attached); both wired in `src/cli/commands/local-start-api.ts`. Dependency: `chokidar@^5.0.0` added (no native deps; macOS gets fsevents via the `chokidar-fsevents` optional path). Tests: 4 new test files (~50 unit tests) covering stage selection / variable substitution / CORS match-and-reject / orchestrator state-swap / file-watcher debounce; 1 new integ-test extension exercising CORS preflight via curl + REST v1 stage variables in the response body. **Post-review hardening (PR review fix-back)**: (a) `ContainerPool.dispose()` now AWAITS every in-flight `inUse` handle's release (per-entry, 30s drain timeout) before tearing down the underlying container — pre-fix a request mid-`invokeRie` against the old pool when reload fired had its container killed (502 leak) AND the request's `release()` from its `finally` corrupted the post-dispose entries map; the fix adds a per-entry `drainResolvers` list signaled by `release()` plus a pool-level `disposed` flag that makes post-dispose `release()` a safe no-op. (b) CORS preflight's explicit-OPTIONS check is now scoped to the surrogate-matched route's `apiLogicalId` — pre-fix an explicit OPTIONS route on Stack B's REST v1 API at the same path would suppress preflight on Stack A's HTTP API v2; the same-API filter closes the cross-API contamination. (c) Successful preflights always emit `Vary: Origin` so downstream caches don't share responses across origins. (d) `Access-Control-Request-Headers` lists with embedded empty entries (`"Content-Type,,Authorization"`) now reject the preflight rather than silently skipping the empty entry — matches AWS's stricter validation. (e) `file-watcher` close() now sets a `closed` flag checked in both `fire()` and the inner `setTimeout` callback so a chokidar event arriving mid-`close()` doesn't land an `onChange` after teardown. (f) `lastAssetPaths.value` mutation moved out of `synthesizeAndBuild` and into the post-swap `.then(...)` block so a concurrent file event during reload doesn't race the asset list against the server state. New tests: 7 in `tests/unit/local/http-server-cors.test.ts` (cross-API contamination guard + greedy proxy + missing-method early-return + REST v1 fallthrough) + 4 in `tests/unit/local/container-pool-dispose.test.ts` (drain wait + post-dispose release + idempotency) + 3 reload-orchestrator tests (baseline-after-swap + add-only diff + same-route-different-lambda) + 2 file-watcher tests (closed-flag + onChange-throws-recovery) + 5 cors-handler tests (Vary header on each origin path + empty-entry rejection + negative-header pin) + 1 stage-resolver test (cross-API stage mismatch).
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` / `cdkd local start-api` extend Node.js runtime support to `nodejs24.x` and Python to `python3.14`; same `public.ecr.aws/lambda/<lang>:<v>` base-image pattern, no code-path changes beyond the `LANGUAGE_MAP` entries in [src/local/runtime-image.ts](src/local/runtime-image.ts) and the matching `nodejs24.x` / `python3.14` rows in the per-runtime test tables. The "Other runtimes follow in subsequent PRs" error message was updated to reflect the wider supported set (`nodejs18.x` / `nodejs20.x` / `nodejs22.x` / `nodejs24.x` / `python3.11` / `python3.12` / `python3.13` / `python3.14`).
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` / `cdkd local start-api` Ruby runtime support (first sub-PR of #248) — `ruby3.2` / `ruby3.3` now resolve to `public.ecr.aws/lambda/ruby:<v>` base images, which bundle the same RIE binary as the Node.js / Python base images so the docker-runner / env-resolver code paths are unchanged. Ruby's Handler grammar is `<file>.<func>` — identical to Node.js and Python — so the inline-`Code.ZipFile` materializer keeps its single `handler.lastIndexOf('.')` parse and only the file extension differs (`.rb`). Implementation: two new `SUPPORTED_RUNTIMES` rows in [src/local/runtime-image.ts](src/local/runtime-image.ts); the deferred-runtime error message updated to drop Ruby from the rejection list. Integration test at `tests/integration/local-invoke-ruby/` deploys nothing and exercises `ruby3.3` end-to-end against the Lambda Ruby base image (asset-backed handler + env-var override + inline `Code.fromInline`); structurally mirrors `tests/integration/local-invoke-python/`. Other runtimes from #248 (Java / .NET / Go / `provided.*`) follow in subsequent sub-PRs.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` / `cdkd local start-api` Java runtime support (second sub-PR of #248) — `java8.al2` / `java11` / `java17` / `java21` now resolve to `public.ecr.aws/lambda/java:<v>` base images. Unlike Node.js / Python / Ruby, Java is **asset-backed only**: the Handler shape `package.Class::method` names a compiled JVM class on the classpath, which can't be expressed as a single inline source file. Mechanism: `RuntimeSpec.fileExtension` is widened to `string | null`; Java entries set `fileExtension: null`, and `resolveRuntimeFileExtension` rejects null with a clear "use `lambda.Code.fromAsset(<dir>)`" routing message. Both `cdkd local invoke` and `cdkd local start-api` call `resolveRuntimeFileExtension` only on the inline-`Code.ZipFile` branch, so asset-backed Java Lambdas pass through unchanged — only inline attempts hit the rejection. Implementation: 4 new `SUPPORTED_RUNTIMES` rows + null-check in `resolveRuntimeFileExtension` in [src/local/runtime-image.ts](src/local/runtime-image.ts); the deferred-runtime prefix list drops `java` (so `java19`-style typos fall to the unknown-runtime branch with the full supported-list message instead of staying in a "follow in subsequent PRs" branch). Integration test at `tests/integration/local-invoke-java/` deploys nothing and exercises `java17` end-to-end: asset-backed handler (`Handler::handleRequest` compiled via `amazoncorretto:17` docker JDK image — host doesn't need a JDK installed) + `--event` payload + the inline rejection path (`CfnFunction` with `Code.ZipFile` + `runtime: java17` → cdkd refuses with the routing message). Other runtimes from #248 (.NET / Go / `provided.*`) follow in subsequent sub-PRs.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` / `cdkd local start-api` .NET runtime support (third sub-PR of #248) — `dotnet6` / `dotnet8` now resolve to `public.ecr.aws/lambda/dotnet:<v>` base images. Same shape as Java (PR #256): .NET is **asset-backed only** because the Handler value `Assembly::Namespace.Class::Method` names a compiled CLR assembly / DLL, which can't be expressed as a single inline source file. Reuses the `fileExtension: null` + `resolveRuntimeFileExtension` rejection mechanism added for Java — no new code paths, only 2 additional `SUPPORTED_RUNTIMES` rows in [src/local/runtime-image.ts](src/local/runtime-image.ts); the deferred-runtime prefix list drops `dotnet` (so `dotnet9`-style typos fall to the unknown-runtime branch). Integration test at `tests/integration/local-invoke-dotnet/` deploys nothing and exercises `dotnet8` end-to-end: asset-backed handler (`Function::Function.Handler::HandleRequest` compiled via `mcr.microsoft.com/dotnet/sdk:8.0` docker SDK image — host doesn't need a .NET SDK installed) + `--event` payload + the inline rejection path (`CfnFunction` with `Code.ZipFile` + `runtime: dotnet8` → cdkd refuses with the routing message). Other runtimes from #248 (Go / `provided.*`) follow in subsequent sub-PRs.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` / `cdkd local start-api` `provided.al2` / `provided.al2023` runtime support + `go1.x` deprecation rejection (final sub-PR of #248) — closes #248 in full. The OS-only `provided.al2` / `provided.al2023` runtimes resolve to `public.ecr.aws/lambda/provided:<v>` base images (~50MB each — much smaller than the language-specific images since these ship only the OS + RIE); they're the canonical hosts for Go (via a `bootstrap` binary), Rust, C/C++, or any other compiled native runtime. Same `fileExtension: null` mechanism as Java / .NET — `provided.*` is asset-backed only because the Handler value names an arbitrary `bootstrap` binary that can't be expressed as inline source. The deprecated `go1.x` runtime (AWS Lambda EOL 2024-01-08) is special-cased in `resolveRuntimeSpec` with a migration pointer to `lambda.Runtime.PROVIDED_AL2023` instead of falling through to the generic "unknown runtime" branch — users who still have `lambda.Runtime.GO_1_X` in their CDK code get the explicit next step. The deferred-prefix branch in `resolveRuntimeSpec` is GONE — every Lambda runtime is now either resolved by `SUPPORTED_RUNTIMES`, special-cased as deprecated (`go1.x`), or rejected as unknown — meeting #248's acceptance criteria. The stale "v1 scope" docstring wording was also dropped now that the runtime-image module is feature-complete. Integration test at `tests/integration/local-invoke-provided/` deploys nothing and exercises `provided.al2023` end-to-end: asset-backed Go `bootstrap` handler (compiled inside `golang:1.21-alpine` — host doesn't need a Go toolchain) + `--event` payload round-trip + inline rejection on both `provided.al2` and `provided.al2023` + the `go1.x` deprecation message. Implementation: 2 new `SUPPORTED_RUNTIMES` rows + 1 special-case `go1.x` branch in [src/local/runtime-image.ts](src/local/runtime-image.ts); 6 new unit test cases; new integ fixture under `tests/integration/local-invoke-provided/`.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local run-task <Stack/TaskDefinitionPath>` (Phase 1 of #262) — ECS counterpart of `cdkd local invoke`. Synthesizes the CDK app, locates the target `AWS::ECS::TaskDefinition`, stands up a per-task docker network on subnet `169.254.170.0/24` with the AWS-published `amazon/amazon-ecs-local-container-endpoints:latest-amd64` sidecar at `169.254.170.2`, and starts every container in `dependsOn` order. Containers reach each other by `--network-alias <CFn Name>`; AWS SDK calls inside containers pick up `ECS_CONTAINER_METADATA_URI_V4` and (when `--assume-task-role` is set) `AWS_CONTAINER_CREDENTIALS_RELATIVE_URI` for IAM task-role emulation. The essential container's exit code drives the CLI exit. **Image source**: `ContainerImage.fromAsset` (CDK asset hash extracted from `Fn::Sub` Image — reuses the shared `src/assets/docker-build.ts` helper), same-account/region ECR (reuses `src/local/ecr-puller.ts`), or any public image (`public.ecr.aws/...` / `docker.io/...`). **Secrets**: `Secrets[].ValueFrom` is resolved at startup via `SecretsManager.GetSecretValue` (with `:<json-key>::` extraction support) / `SSM.GetParameter(WithDecryption: true)`; failures hard-error with the offending container + secret name. **DependsOn conditions**: START / COMPLETE / SUCCESS / HEALTHY (HEALTHY polls `docker inspect --format '{{.State.Health.Status}}'` capped at 5 min); cyclic dependencies rejected up front. **Volumes**: `Host: { SourcePath }` → bind mount; `Host` with no SourcePath → anonymous; `DockerVolumeConfiguration` → `docker volume create`; `EFSVolumeConfiguration` / `FSxWindowsFileServerVolumeConfiguration` → hard-error with a "bind-mount a local dir instead" routing message. **Networking**: `awsvpc` mapped to `bridge` with a warn (docker can't emulate ENI-per-task). **Lifecycle**: ^C cleans up containers + sidecar + network; double-^C exits 130 immediately (matches `cdkd local start-api`'s pattern). Flags: `--cluster <name>` (default `cdkd-local`), `--env-vars <file>` (SAM-shape JSON, `Parameters` global), `--container-host <ip>` (default `127.0.0.1` — numeric IP, no hostnames; same constraint as `local start-api`), `--assume-task-role [<arn>]` (bare flag uses template's `TaskRoleArn`; explicit ARN overrides; calls `sts:AssumeRole` once at startup and exposes the creds via the metadata sidecar), `--no-pull`, `--platform`, `--keep-running` (keeps user containers for `docker exec` post-mortem), `--detach` (start and return; CI smoke tests). **Phase 2 (`cdkd local start-service`)** and **Phase 3 (Service Connect / Cloud Map)** are explicitly out of scope. Implementation across `src/local/{ecs-task-resolver,ecs-secrets-resolver,ecs-network,ecs-task-runner,docker-runner}.ts` + `src/cli/commands/local-run-task.ts`; new `LocalRunTaskError` in `src/utils/error-handler.ts`; Phase 1 unit tests under `tests/unit/local/ecs-*.test.ts` + `tests/unit/cli/local-run-task.test.ts`; Docker-only integ fixtures at `tests/integration/local-run-task/` (nginx single container) and `tests/integration/local-run-task-multi-container/` (busybox sidecar pattern with `dependsOn: { condition: 'START' }` + shared volume). `docker-runner.ts` was extended with an optional `network?: string` field on `DockerRunOptions` so `runDetached` can join the per-task network when needed; existing `cdkd local invoke` / `cdkd local start-api` callers are unaffected (field optional).
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local invoke` resolves `lambda.DockerImageCode.fromEcr` `Fn::Join` Code.ImageUri shapes (issue #286 Gap 2). Pre-fix `extractImageUri` only recognized flat strings + `Fn::Sub`; a container Lambda built with `lambda.DockerImageCode.fromEcr(repo, { tagOrDigest })` produced an `Fn::Join` (verified via `cdk synth` + `jq` against a real CDK 2.x app) that fell through to `undefined`, and the resolver then errored with the misleading ZIP-branch "no Runtime property" message. Post-fix, `tryResolveImageFnJoin` (and its supporting helpers `findEcrRepositoryRefInTree` / `resolveImageIntrinsic` / `resolveImageIntrinsicAny` / `substituteImagePlaceholders` plus the `FnJoinResolveOutcome` type) is **extracted** from `ecs-task-resolver.ts` (where PR #280 introduced it for ECS `ContainerImage.fromEcrRepository`) into the new shared module [src/local/intrinsic-image.ts](src/local/intrinsic-image.ts), and `lambda-resolver.ts:extractImageUri` calls it for `Fn::Join` shapes. Resolution outcomes: literal-only joins (no intrinsic refs) resolve cleanly; same-stack ECR Repository refs return `needs-state` and surface a clear "deploy first / use fromImageAsset / pin a public image" hint; imported-repo shapes that reference `Ref: AWS::URLSuffix` without pseudo-parameter context return `not-applicable` and surface a separate "pseudo parameter not resolved" hint (rather than the misleading ZIP-branch error); malformed shapes surface `unsupported-join` with a precise reason. The ECS resolver continues to use the helper via re-exported type alias `EcsImageResolutionContext = ImageResolutionContext` so existing `src/cli/commands/local-run-task.ts` callers are unchanged. Implementation: new shared module + 5 new unit tests in `tests/unit/local/lambda-resolver.test.ts` (same-stack reject / malformed reject / imported-shape reject / literal-only resolve / regressions on existing flat-string + Fn::Sub paths) + 14 new unit tests in `tests/unit/local/intrinsic-image.test.ts` covering every outcome branch + 47 existing ECS resolver tests preserved unchanged. The 400-line duplicate in `ecs-task-resolver.ts` is gone.
- ✅ CLI: `cdkd local start-api` one HTTP server per API (closes issue #260) + `--container-host` default fix + quiet `docker pull` by default. Pre-PR `cdkd local start-api` lumped every discovered API into a single HTTP server on a single port. That broke realistic CDK apps with multiple APIs (admin + public, internal + external) because authorizers, CORS configs, and stage variables are all per-API — lumping them into one server forced an awkward "first-match-wins" semantic and let one API's auth bleed into another. Post-PR the CLI groups discovered routes by API surface (`AWS::ApiGatewayV2::Api` / `AWS::ApiGateway::RestApi` / `AWS::Lambda::Url` keyed by backing Lambda) and launches one [startApiServer](src/local/http-server.ts) per group; each server gets its own port, its own filtered `ContainerPool`, its own authorizer pipeline, and its own CORS config. The new helper [src/local/api-server-grouping.ts](src/local/api-server-grouping.ts) does the grouping (`groupRoutesByServer` + `filterRoutesByApiIdentifier` + `availableApiIdentifiers`); the CLI's boot loop, shutdown loop, and `--watch` reload loop all iterate over the resulting `BootedApiServer[]`. New `--api <id>` flag restricts to a single API. Port allocation: `--port 0` (default) auto-allocates each server; `--port N` makes the first server `N` and increments for each subsequent server (`N+1`, `N+2`, ...). **Bonus fix**: the `--container-host` default was `host.docker.internal`, which Docker rejects as an invalid IP in `docker run -p <ip>:<port>:8080` (the `-p` parser doesn't accept hostnames) — every fresh-install user hit "docker: Invalid ip address: host.docker.internal" on the first `curl` to a Lambda route until they explicitly passed `--container-host 127.0.0.1`. Default flipped to `127.0.0.1` and the help text now spells out the IP-not-hostname constraint. **Bonus fix #2**: `pullImage` no longer streams `docker pull` progress to stdout in the default compact log level; the noise (4+ "Status: Image is up to date" lines on every cached run) is now silenced and only re-enabled with `--verbose`. Errors still surface — captured stderr is folded into the thrown `DockerRunnerError`. The existing single-server `createReloadOrchestrator` stays in place (and its 10+ unit tests are unaffected); the new CLI uses a dedicated multi-server `reloadAllServers` coordinator inline. New unit test file `tests/unit/local/api-server-grouping.test.ts` (9 cases) covers grouping by HTTP API + REST v1 + Function URL, kind-disambiguation when two APIs share a logical id, identifier filtering, and the available-identifiers diagnostic.
- ✅ Fix: `TemplateParser.extractRefsFromValue` now explicitly recurses into `Fn::Join` / `Fn::Select` / `Fn::Split` array arguments to surface buried `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` deps for the DAG (closes Gap 7 of #286 — same class of bug as #275/#276 for `Fn::Sub`). The pre-fix catch-all `Object.values(obj).forEach(...)` recursion accidentally produced the right answer because the array elements were walked anyway, but the support was implicit and would silently regress the next time someone added a new early-return for another intrinsic. CDK emits this shape whenever a construct builds a derived value from a sibling — verified via real `cdk synth` on 2026-05-12 against a DynamoDB Table → IAM Role policy: `{Fn::Join: [':', ['arn', 'aws', 'dynamodb', {Ref: 'AWS::Region'}, {Ref: 'AWS::AccountId'}, {Fn::Join: ['/', ['table', {Ref: 'MyTable...'}]]}]]}`, plus the canonical Fn::Select + Fn::Split + Fn::GetAtt ARN-extractor pattern (`{Fn::Select: [5, {Fn::Split: [':', {Fn::GetAtt: [<Table>, 'Arn']}]}]}`). Implementation skips the delimiter (Fn::Join[0]) / index (Fn::Select[0] only recurses defensively because that slot is normally a literal number) and only descends into the value-bearing slots. Pseudo-parameter refs (`AWS::Region` / `AWS::AccountId` / etc.) are still filtered at the `Ref` early-return. No edges are added for the intrinsic wrappers themselves — only for the inner refs uncovered by the recursion. Implementation in [src/analyzer/template-parser.ts](src/analyzer/template-parser.ts); 14 new unit tests at [tests/unit/analyzer/template-parser.test.ts](tests/unit/analyzer/template-parser.test.ts) covering Fn::Join with buried Ref / Fn::GetAtt, the canonical multi-nested DynamoDB ARN shape, Fn::Select+Fn::Split+Fn::GetAtt chains, pseudo-parameter filtering inside composite intrinsics, composition with the `Fn::Sub` 1-arg implicit-Ref path from #276, and 2 end-to-end DagBuilder integration tests asserting the graph edges land.
- ✅ Fix: `cdkd local start-api` recognizes additional CDK 2.x-canonical CFn intrinsic shapes for Lambda ARN references in API Gateway resolvers (closes issue #286 Gaps 3 / 4). `route-discovery.ts`'s `IntegrationUri` resolver now accepts the `Fn::Sub` invoke-ARN wrapper (both 1-arg `{Fn::Sub: 'arn:...${LogicalId.Arn}/invocations'}` AWS-docs-canonical form AND 2-arg `{Fn::Sub: [template, {VarName: {Fn::GetAtt: [LogicalId, 'Arn']}}]}` what-CDK-`Fn.sub(template, vars)`-emits form) alongside the pre-existing `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt: [..., 'Arn']` / `Fn::Join` invoke-ARN wrapper. `authorizer-resolver.ts`'s `AuthorizerUri` resolver now accepts the full quartet too — pre-fix it only recognized `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt: [..., 'Arn']` and hard-errored on `Fn::Join`, which CDK 2.x's `apigatewayv2-authorizers.HttpLambdaAuthorizer` actually synthesizes (verified via real `cdk synth` on 2026-05-12). Both call sites now route through the shared helper `resolveLambdaArnIntrinsic` in the new module [src/local/intrinsic-lambda-arn.ts](src/local/intrinsic-lambda-arn.ts) — same extraction pattern as PR #293 used for `tryResolveImageFnJoin` in `intrinsic-image.ts`. The helper returns a discriminated union `{kind: 'resolved', logicalId} | {kind: 'unsupported', detail}` so each call site wraps the unsupported case with its own error class (`Error` for route-discovery, which the top-level catch re-wraps as `RouteDiscoveryError`; `RouteDiscoveryError` directly for authorizer-resolver). The two pre-extraction `resolveLambdaArnIntrinsic` / `resolveLambdaArn` near-duplicates (~50 LOC each, 95% identical) are gone — future shape additions get fixed once. Both `Fn::Sub` forms require the invoke-ARN marker `:lambda:path/2015-03-31/functions/` in the template so a bare `Fn::Sub: '${X.Arn}'` against an arbitrary template is still rejected (preserves pre-PR rejection intent). Implementation: new shared module + 5 new tests in `tests/unit/local/authorizer-resolver.test.ts` (Fn::Join invoke-ARN + Fn::Sub invoke-ARN + Fn::Join non-invoke-ARN reject + 2 existing tests preserved) + 2 new tests in `tests/unit/local/route-discovery.test.ts` (Fn::Sub 1-arg + Fn::Sub 2-arg; existing rejection test preserved with updated wording) + 15 new tests in `tests/unit/local/intrinsic-lambda-arn.test.ts` covering every accept / reject branch.
- ✅ Fix: `cdkd local run-task --from-state` substitutes intrinsic-valued `ContainerDefinitions[].Environment[].Value` AND `Secrets[].ValueFrom` against deployed state + AWS pseudo parameters (closes issue #291). Bundled cdkd-side fix: `ECSProvider.convertContainerDefinitions` was casting every nested-object array field (`Environment` / `EnvironmentFiles` / `Secrets` / `MountPoints` / `VolumesFrom` / `DependsOn` / `Ulimits`) as `as KeyValuePair[]` / `as Secret[]` / etc. without actually transforming the keys — CFn emits PascalCase, ECS SDK requires camelCase, and the silent cast left the wire shape in PascalCase. AWS rejected `RegisterTaskDefinition` with `secret.name should not be null or empty.` on any TaskDef that templated `Secrets`; per-PR audit caught the same shape mismatch on the 6 siblings (the existing `local-run-task-multi-container` integ happened to work only because its `DependsOn` was ignored leniently by the SDK input parser; this PR brings every field in line with the SDK contract via dedicated `convertEnvironment` / `convertEnvironmentFiles` / `convertSecrets` / `convertMountPoints` / `convertVolumesFrom` / `convertDependsOn` / `convertUlimits` helpers analogous to the existing `convertPortMappings` / `convertLogConfiguration`). Pre-fix, `Environment[].Value: { Ref: 'MyTable' }` and `Secrets[].ValueFrom: { Ref: 'MySecret' }` (the standard CDK shape for `table.tableName` / `ecs.Secret.fromSecretsManager(secret)` / `ecs.Secret.fromSsmParameter(param)`) silently dropped — the literal-only / `pickString` parsing in `parseContainerDefinition` rejected every intrinsic and the runtime saw an empty env or missing secret. Post-fix, when `--from-state` is set cdkd loads the stack's S3 state and routes every intrinsic-valued env / secret entry through the shared `substituteAgainstState` helper in [src/local/state-resolver.ts](src/local/state-resolver.ts), which now supports `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` / `Fn::Sub` / `Fn::Join` + `AWS::AccountId` / `AWS::Region` / `AWS::Partition` / `AWS::URLSuffix` pseudo parameters (Gap 1 of #286). Per-key best-effort: an unresolvable entry (state missing the referenced logical id, attribute not captured at deploy time, unsupported intrinsic) drops with a `Container '<name>': Environment '<KEY>' dropped: <reason>` warning on the task's `warnings` array; the run-task invocation never aborts. Implementation: [src/local/state-resolver.ts](src/local/state-resolver.ts) (new `SubstitutionContext` with optional `pseudoParameters` bag — backward-compatible: callers can still pass a bare `Record<string, ResourceState>`) + [src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts](src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts) (new `containerHasIntrinsicEnvOrSecret` scan + `needsEnvOrSecretSubstitution` flag on `EcsImageResolutionNeeds`, intrinsic-aware env-var / secret parsing in `parseContainerDefinition`, per-container `warnings: string[]` field that the task-runner surfaces) + [src/cli/commands/local-run-task.ts](src/cli/commands/local-run-task.ts) (state-load gated on `needsEnvOrSecretSubstitution` too; pseudo-parameter resolution fires for env/secret needs even when the image doesn't trigger them — the `ecs.Secret.fromSsmParameter` shape is `Fn::Join` over `${AWS::Partition}` / `${AWS::Region}` / `${AWS::AccountId}` + `Ref: <Param>`). 20 new unit tests across `tests/unit/local/{state-resolver,ecs-task-resolver}.test.ts` covering each intrinsic shape end-to-end + the warn-and-drop fallbacks. Integ fixture at `tests/integration/local-run-task-from-state/` extended with a DynamoDB Table + SecretsManager Secret + a busybox printer TaskDef that echoes 4 env vars + the resolved secret length; `verify.sh` asserts every value is substituted against the deployed state.
- ✅ Fix: `cdkd local invoke --from-state` now passes AWS pseudo parameters (`${AWS::AccountId}` / `${AWS::Region}` / `${AWS::Partition}` / `${AWS::URLSuffix}`) AND `Fn::Join` shapes into the env-var substitution context, closing the documented gap that PR #294 left for `cdkd local run-task` only. Pre-fix, a Lambda env var like `REGION_URL: { 'Fn::Sub': 'https://${AWS::Region}.example.com' }` warned-and-dropped because `local-invoke.ts` passed the bare `state.resources` map (the pre-PR `substituteAgainstState` signature) without the `pseudoParameters` bag that `state-resolver.ts` now reads for AWS::* refs. Post-fix, `local-invoke.ts` constructs a full `SubstitutionContext` whenever the function's template env contains any intrinsic value (gated via the new `envHasIntrinsicValue` helper to skip the STS hop on literal-only env maps), populating `pseudoParameters` from a single `sts:GetCallerIdentity` + `derivePartitionAndUrlSuffix(region)` (reused from `src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts`). STS failures degrade to warn — the substitution still runs for non-`AWS::*` refs. Region precedence mirrors `local-run-task`: `--region` > `AWS_REGION` > `AWS_DEFAULT_REGION` > synth-derived stack region. Implementation: [src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts](src/cli/commands/local-invoke.ts) (new `envHasIntrinsicValue` + `resolvePseudoParametersForInvoke` helpers + updated `--from-state` block) + reuses the shared `SubstitutionContext` from [src/local/state-resolver.ts](src/local/state-resolver.ts) (unchanged, already PR #294-compatible). 8 new unit tests in `tests/unit/cli/local-invoke-from-state-pseudo.test.ts` covering the gating helper + canonical Fn::Join-with-pseudo-params + Fn::Sub-with-AWS::Region + the pre-fix warn-and-drop baseline + mixed success/failure paths. Integ fixture at `tests/integration/local-invoke-from-state/` deliberately not extended (real-AWS deploy is heavy and the existing fixture already covers the state-resolution path; the new pseudo-param surface is fully covered at the unit layer).
- ✅ Fix: `cdkd local run-task` resolves `Fn::Join` / `Fn::Sub` intrinsics in `TaskDefinition.TaskRoleArn` / `ExecutionRoleArn` and `Volumes[].Host.SourcePath` (closes Gaps 5 + 6 of #286). **Gap 5** (role ARN, verified via real `cdk synth` on 2026-05-12): typical `new iam.Role(...)` + `taskRole: role` still emits the already-supported `Fn::GetAtt: [..., 'Arn']`, but `iam.Role.fromRoleArn(stack, id, cdk.Fn.join(...))` synthesizes a `Fn::Join` shape that pre-fix `resolveRoleArn` silently dropped (`undefined`). Post-fix, when state + pseudo parameters are available (`--from-state` flow), the resolver delegates to the shared `substituteAgainstState` helper in [src/local/state-resolver.ts](src/local/state-resolver.ts) (which already handles `Fn::Join` / `Fn::Sub` / `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` for env + secrets) and surfaces the literal ARN; without `--from-state` the pre-PR silent-undefined behavior is preserved for backward compatibility. **Gap 6** (volume source path): pre-fix `parseVolume` accepted only flat-string `Host.SourcePath` via `pickString` — `{Fn::Sub: '/data/${AWS::Region}'}` / `{Fn::Join: ['/', ['/data', cdk.Aws.REGION, 'shared']]}` / `{Ref: <Param>}` all silently dropped to anonymous-volume kind (silent empty mount at runtime). Post-fix `parseVolume` accepts the same intrinsic shapes via `substituteAgainstState`; unresolvable intrinsics **hard-error** (rather than silently dropping to an empty mount), because a Host bind mount with no path is unsafe to proxy as an anonymous volume. Detection side: `detectEcsImageResolutionNeeds.needsEnvOrSecretSubstitution` now also flags intrinsic-valued role ARNs (`Fn::Join` / `Fn::Sub` only — `Ref` / `Fn::GetAtt` shapes resolve to the placeholder ARN without state) and intrinsic-valued volume source paths, so the CLI's existing `--from-state` state-load + STS pseudo-parameter resolution path covers them automatically. Implementation: [src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts](src/local/ecs-task-resolver.ts) (extended `resolveRoleArn` signature with `SubstitutionContext`; new `resolveVolumeSourcePath` helper; extended `parseVolume` signature with `subContext`; new `volumeHasIntrinsicSourcePath` + `isFnJoinOrSubIntrinsic` detectors). 15 new unit tests in `tests/unit/local/ecs-task-resolver.test.ts` covering each intrinsic shape end-to-end on both fields, the no-context silent-drop path on role ARN, the no-context hard-error path on volume source path, the unresolvable-context hard-error / silent-drop paths, malformed non-string non-object SourcePath rejection, and the `detectEcsImageResolutionNeeds` plumbing.

## Dependencies

### Key Dependencies

- `@aws-sdk/client-*` - AWS SDK v3 (various services)
- `graphlib` - DAG construction
- `archiver` - ZIP packaging for file assets
- `chokidar` - File watcher backing `cdkd local start-api --watch` (PR 8c)
- `yaml` - CFn-aware YAML codec for `cdkd export` / `cdkd import --migrate-from-cloudformation` (preserves `!Ref` / `!GetAtt` / `!Sub` shorthand intrinsics on round-trip — see [src/cli/yaml-cfn.ts](src/cli/yaml-cfn.ts))

### Dev Dependencies

- `esbuild` - Build tool
- `vitest` - Testing framework
- `eslint` - Linting
- `prettier` - Formatting
- `typescript` - Type checking

## Node.js Version

- **`package.json` engines**: Node.js >= 20.0.0 (the lower bound users of cdkd must meet).
- **Local dev / CI Node version**: 24.15.0, pinned by `.node-version` (managed by Vite+ / mise).
- **`vp pack` build target**: Node 20 (the runtime cdkd ships to users).
- **TypeScript type stripping**: Node 24 strips type annotations by default, so `node scripts/foo.ts` runs `.ts` files directly — no `tsx` / `ts-node` dev dependency needed. Use this for ad-hoc scripts under `scripts/`; prefer registering longer-lived scripts as Vite+ tasks in `vite.config.ts` (see "Build System" above).

## Workflow Rules

- **When adding new functionality or fixing bugs**: Always add corresponding unit tests. Do not wait to be asked.
